2:24:1348:0:14:72:365:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Financial Risk Measurement for Financial Risk Management
2:25:1404:14:14:72:482:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Torben G. Andersen, Tim Bollerslev, Peter F. Christoffersen, and Francis X. Diebold
2:26:1487:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:NBER Working Paper No. 18084
2:27:1515:14:14:72:121:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:May 2012

2:29:1536:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:A:ABSTRACT
2:30:1544:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Current practice largely follows restrictive approaches to market risk measurement, such as historical
2:31:1646:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:simulation or RiskMetrics. In contrast, we propose flexible methods that exploit recent developments
2:32:1746:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:in financial econometrics and are likely to produce more accurate risk assessments, treating both portfolio-level
2:33:1859:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:and asset-level analysis.  Asset-level analysis is particularly challenging because the demands of real-world
2:34:1968:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:risk management in financial institutions – in particular, real-time risk tracking in very high-dimensional
2:35:2075:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:situations – impose strict limits on model complexity.  Hence we stress powerful yet parsimonious
2:36:2172:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:models that are easily estimated.  In addition, we emphasize the need for deeper understanding of the
2:37:2273:14:14:72:540:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:links between market risk and  macroeconomic fundamentals, focusing primarily on links among equity
2:38:2372:14:14:72:540:476:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:return volatilities, real growth, and real growth volatilities.  Throughout, we strive not only to deepen
2:39:2477:14:14:72:540:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:our scientific understanding of market risk, but also cross-fertilize the academic and practitioner communities,
2:40:2589:14:42:72:502:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:promoting improved market risk measurement technologies that draw on the best of both.
2:41:2675:42:14:72:170:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:?:Torben G. Andersen

5:115:6963:0:30:91:227:685:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:1  Introduction
5:116:6978:30:18:91:519:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Financial risk management is a huge field with diverse and evolving components, as
5:117:7060:18:18:91:519:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evidenced by both its historical development (e.g., Diebold (2012)) and current best
5:118:7144:18:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:practice (e.g., Stulz (2002)).  One such component – probablythekey component –
5:119:7223:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is riskmeasurement, in particular the measurement of financial asset return volatil-
5:120:7307:18:18:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ities and correlations (henceforth “volatilities”).  Crucially,  asset-return volatilities
5:121:7397:18:18:91:519:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are time-varying, with persistent dynamics.  This is true across assets, asset classes,
5:122:7484:18:18:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time periods,  and countries,  as vividly brought to the fore during numerous crisis
5:123:7568:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:events,  most  recently  and  prominently  the  2007-2008  financial  crisis  and  its  long-
5:124:7661:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lasting aftermath.  The field of financial econometrics devotes considerable attention
5:125:7747:18:18:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  time-varying  volatility  and  associated  tools  for  its  measurement,  modeling  and
5:126:7838:18:17:91:519:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forecasting.  In this chapter we suggest practical applications of the new “volatility
5:127:7924:17:18:91:519:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:econometrics” to the measurement and management of market risk, stressing parsi-
5:128:8004:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:monious models that are easily estimated.  Our ultimate goal is to stimulate dialog
5:129:8087:18:18:91:519:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between the academic and practitioner communities, advancing best-practice market
5:130:8168:18:39:91:518:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk measurement and management technologies by drawing upon the best of both.
5:131:8246:39:26:91:283:365:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:1.1  Six Emergent Themes
5:132:8270:26:18:91:519:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Six key themes emerge, and we highlight them here.  We treat some of them directly
5:133:8352:18:18:91:519:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in explicitly-focused sections, while we treat others indirectly, touching upon them
5:134:8436:18:18:91:431:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in various places throughout the chapter, and from various angles.
5:135:8502:18:17:109:520:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The first theme concerns aggregation level.  We consider both portfolio-level (ag-
5:136:8584:17:18:91:519:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gregated, “top-down”) and asset-level (disaggregated, “bottom-up”) modeling, em-
5:137:8664:18:18:91:519:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:phasizing the related distinction between risk measurement and risk management.
5:138:8743:18:18:91:519:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Risk measurement generally requires only a portfolio-level model, whereas risk man-
5:139:8826:18:18:91:287:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:agement requires an asset-level model.
5:140:8864:18:18:109:520:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  second  theme  concerns  the  frequency  of  data  observations.   We  consider
5:141:8948:18:18:91:519:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both low-frequency and high-frequency data, and the associated issue of parametric
5:142:9030:18:18:91:519:160:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:vs.   nonparametric  volatility  measurement.   We  treat  all  cases,  but  we  emphasize
5:143:9120:18:0:91:519:142:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the appeal of volatility measurement using nonparametric methods used with high-
6:144:9201:0:18:91:449:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequency data, followed by modeling that is intentionally parametric.
6:145:9271:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  third  theme  concerns  modeling  and  monitoring  entire  time-varying  condi-
6:146:9355:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional densities rather than just conditional volatilities.  We argue that a full condi-
6:147:9443:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional density perspective is necessary for thorough risk assessment, and that best-
6:148:9527:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:practice risk management should move – and indeedismoving – in that direction.
6:149:9605:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We discuss methods for constructing, evaluating and combining full conditional den-
6:150:9688:18:18:91:160:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sity forecasts.
6:151:9703:18:18:109:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The fourth theme concerns dimensionality reduction in multivariate “vast data”
6:152:9781:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:environments, a crucial issue in asset-level analysis.  We devote considerable atten-
6:153:9866:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion to frameworks that facilitate tractable modeling of the very high-dimensional
6:154:9948:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariance matrices of practical relevance.  Shrinkage methods and factor structure
6:155:10031:18:18:91:302:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(and their interface) feature prominently.
6:156:10073:18:18:109:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The fifth theme concerns the links between market risk and macroeconomic funda-
6:157:10152:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mentals.  Recent work is starting to uncover the links between asset-market volatility
6:158:10238:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and macroeconomic fundamentals.  We discuss those links, focusing in particular on
6:159:10320:18:18:91:494:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:links among equity return volatilities, real growth, and real growth volatilities.
6:160:10402:18:18:109:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The sixth theme, the desirability of conditional as opposed to unconditional risk
6:161:10483:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measurement,  is so important that we dedicate the following subsection to an ex-
6:162:10564:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tended  discussion  of  the  topic.   We  argue  throughout  the  chapter  that,  for  most
6:163:10655:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial risk management purposes,  the conditional perspective is distinctly more
6:164:10738:18:39:91:303:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relevant for monitoring daily market risk.
6:165:10780:39:26:91:318:287:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:1.2  Conditional Risk Measures
6:166:10810:26:18:91:519:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our  emphasis  on  conditional  risk  measurement  is  perhaps  surprising,  given  that
6:167:10898:18:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:many popular approaches adopt an unconditional perspective.  However,  consider,
6:168:10978:18:38:91:453:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for example, the canonical Value-at-Risk (V aR) quantile risk measure,
6:169:11048:38:0:145:319:187:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:p=PrT(rT+1≤−V aRpT+1|T)  =
6:170:11074:0:27:328:385:203:12:g_d0_f10:6:g_d0_f11:A:∫−V aRpT+1|T
6:171:11086:27:0:335:350:176:8:g_d0_f9:8:g_d0_f9:?:−∞
6:172:11088:0:0:390:520:187:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:fT(rT+1)drT+1,(1)
7:173:11106:0:18:91:518:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:wherefT(rT+1)  denotes  the  density  of  future  returnsrT+1conditionalon  time-T
7:174:11188:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:information.  As the formal definition makes clear,V aRis distinctly a conditional
7:175:11270:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measure.  Nonetheless, banks often rely onV aRfrom “historical simulation” (HS-
7:176:11349:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:V aR).  The HS-V aRsimply approximates theV aRas the 100pthpercentile or the
7:177:11425:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:Tpthorder statistic of a set ofThistorical pseudo portfolio returns constructed using
7:178:11510:18:18:91:354:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:historical asset prices but today’s portfolio weights.
7:179:11564:18:18:109:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Pritsker (2006) discusses several serious problems with historical simulation.  Per-
7:180:11648:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:haps  most  importantly,  it  does  not  properly  incorporate  conditionality,  effectively
7:181:11740:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replacing the conditional return distribution in equation (1) with its unconditional
7:182:11824:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:counterpart.   This  deficiency  of  the  conventional  HS  approach  is  forcefully  high-
7:183:11915:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lighted by banks’ proprietary P/L as reported in Berkowitz and O’Brien (2002) and
7:184:11996:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  clustering  in  time  of  the  correspondingV aRviolations,  reflecting  a  failure  by
7:185:12088:18:18:91:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the banks to properly account for persistent changes in market volatility.1The only
7:186:12171:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:source of dynamics in HS-V aRis the evolving window used to construct historical
7:187:12251:17:18:91:441:434:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:pseudo portfolio returns, which is of minor consequence in practice.2
7:188:12320:18:18:109:520:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 1 directly illustrates this hidden danger of HS. We plot on the left axis
7:189:12400:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the cumulative daily loss (cumulative negative return) on an S&P500 portfolio, and
7:190:12482:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the right axis the 1% HS-V aRcalculated using a 500 day moving window, for a
7:191:12561:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample period encompassing the recent financial crisis (July 1, 2008 - December 31,
7:192:12644:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:2009).  Notice that HS-V aRreacts only slowly to the dramatically increased risk in
7:193:12727:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  fall  of  2008.   Perhaps  even  more  strikingly,  HS-V aRreacts  very  slowly  to  the
7:194:12820:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decreased  risk  following  the  market  trough  in  March  2009,  remaining  at  its  peak
7:195:12911:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:through  the  end  of  2009.   This  happens  because  the  early-sample  extreme  events
7:196:13000:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that caused the increase in HS-V aRremain in the late-sample 500-day estimation
7:197:13079:18:18:91:133:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:window.
7:198:13086:18:18:109:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:More generally, the sluggishness of HS-V aRdynamics implies that traders who
7:199:13162:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:base  their  positions  on  HS  will  reduce  their  exposure  too  slowly  when  volatility
7:200:13254:18:17:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:increases, and then increase exposure too slowly when volatility subsequently begins
7:201:13338:17:12:105:273:183:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:A:1See also Perignon and Smith (2010a).
7:202:13375:12:16:105:519:171:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:2Boudoukh  et  al.  (1998)  incorporate  more  aggressive  updating  into  historical  simulation,  but
7:203:13478:16:0:91:334:155:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the basic concerns expressed by Pritsker (2006) remain.

8:226:14040:18:18:109:520:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  sluggish  reaction  to  current  market  conditions  is  only  one  shortcoming  of
8:227:14128:18:18:91:520:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:HS-V aR.  Another is the lack of a properly-defined conditional model, which implies
8:228:14212:18:18:91:520:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that it does not allow for the construction of a term structure ofV aR.  Calculating a

8:231:14458:18:18:91:519:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by the square root of 10,  but this extrapolation is typically not valid unless daily
8:232:14543:18:18:91:407:250:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:returns are iid and normally distributed, which they are not.3
8:233:14605:18:17:109:520:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To further illustrate the lack of conditionality in the HS-V aRmethod consider
8:234:14683:17:18:91:519:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 2.  We first simulate daily portfolio returns from a mean-reverting volatility

9:248:15196:12:12:91:520:518:12:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f15:B:is Persistent.We simulate returns from a realistically-calibrated dynamic volatility model, after
9:249:15293:12:12:91:520:506:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:which  we  compute  1-day  1%  HS-V aRusing  a  rolling  window  of  500  observations.   We  plot  the

9:252:15572:47:18:91:519:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:window of 500 observations.  As the true portfolio return distribution is known, the
9:253:15656:18:18:91:520:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:true daily coverage of the nominal 1% HS-V aRcan be calculated using the return
9:254:15735:18:18:91:519:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:generating  model.   Figure  2  shows  the  conditional  coverage  probability  of  the  1%
9:255:15826:18:18:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:HS-V aRover time.  Notice from the figure how an HS-V aRwith a nominal coverage
9:256:15905:18:18:91:519:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:probability of 1% can have a true conditional probability as high as 10%, even though
9:257:15990:18:18:91:519:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the unconditional coverage is correctly calibrated at 1%.  On any given day the risk
9:258:16074:18:18:91:519:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:manager thinks that there is a 1% chance of getting a return worse than the HS-V aR,
9:259:16158:18:17:91:520:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but in actuality there may as much as a 10% chance of exceeding theV aR.  Figure 2
9:260:16240:17:18:91:519:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:highlights the potential benefit of conditional density modeling:  The HS-V aRmay
9:261:16321:18:18:91:520:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assess risk correctlyon average(i.e., unconditionally) while still being terribly wrong
9:262:16408:18:18:91:519:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:at any given time (i.e., conditionally).  A conditional density model will generate a
9:263:16493:18:18:91:520:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamicV aRthat  attempts  to  keep  the  conditional  coverage  rate  at  1%  on  any
9:264:16579:18:18:91:142:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:given day.
9:265:16589:18:18:109:520:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The above discussion also hints at a problem with theV aRrisk measure itself.
9:266:16666:18:18:91:519:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:It does not say anything about how large the expected loss will be on days when
9:267:16745:18:0:91:519:166:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:V aRis exceeded.  Other risk measures, such as Expected Shortfall (ES), attempt to
10:268:16828:0:35:91:282:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:remedy that defect.  We defineESas
10:269:16862:35:0:216:299:650:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:A:ESpT+1|T=p−1
10:270:16874:0:27:304:319:666:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:?:∫p

10:272:16877:0:35:324:520:650:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:V aRγT+1|Tdγ .(2)
10:273:16894:35:18:91:520:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Because it integrates over the left tail,ESis sensitive to the shape of theentireleft
10:274:16979:18:18:91:519:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tail of the distribution.4By averaging all of theV aRs below a prespecified coverage
10:275:17063:18:18:91:519:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate, the magnitude of the loss across all relevant scenarios matters.  Thus, even if
10:276:17148:18:18:91:520:561:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:theV aRmight be correctly calibrated at, say, the 5% level, this does not ensure that
10:277:17233:18:18:91:519:543:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the 5% ES is also correct.  Conversely, even if the 5%ESis estimated with precision,
10:278:17317:18:18:91:520:525:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this  does  not  imply  that  the  5%V aRis  valid.   Only  if  the  return  distribution  is
10:279:17410:18:18:91:519:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characterized appropriately throughout the entire tail region can we guarantee that
10:280:17493:18:18:91:377:489:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the different risk measures all provide accurate answers.
10:281:17550:18:17:109:519:471:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Our main point of critique still applies, however. Any risk measure, whetherV aR,
10:282:17631:17:18:91:520:454:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:ES,  or  anything  else,  that  neglects  conditionality,  will  inevitably  miss  important
10:283:17723:18:18:91:519:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aspects of the dynamic evolution of risk.  In the conditional analyses of subsequent
10:284:17807:18:39:91:508:418:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:sections, we focus mostly on conditionalV aR, but we also treat conditionalES.5
10:285:17886:39:26:91:269:379:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:1.3  Plan of the Chapter
10:286:17910:26:18:91:519:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We proceed systematically in several steps.  In section 2 we consider portfolio level
10:287:17995:18:18:91:519:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analysis, directly modeling conditional portfolio volatility using exponential smooth-
10:288:18081:18:18:91:519:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing and GARCH models, along with more recent “realized volatility” procedures that
10:289:18163:18:18:91:456:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effectively incorporate the information in high-frequency intraday data.
10:290:18235:18:18:109:520:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In section 3 we consider asset level analysis, modeling asset conditional covariance
10:291:18319:18:18:91:519:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrices, again using GARCH and realized volatility techniques.  The relevant cross-
10:292:18403:18:17:91:519:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sectional dimension is often huge, so we devote special attention to dimensionality-
10:293:18487:17:16:91:190:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduction methods.
10:294:18505:16:16:105:520:212:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:4In contrast toV aR, the expected shortfall is acoherentrisk measure in the sense of Artzner
10:295:18597:16:11:91:519:196:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:et al. (1999) as demonstrated by, e.g., F ̈ollmer and Schied (2002).  Among other things, this ensures
10:296:18699:11:9:91:426:185:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:that it captures the beneficial effects of portfolio diversification, unlikeV aR.
10:297:18780:9:15:105:519:176:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:5ESis  increasingly  used  in  financial  institutions,  but  it  has  not  been  incorporated  into  the
10:298:18885:15:12:91:520:161:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:international regulatory framework for risk control, likely because it is harder thanV aRto estimate
10:299:18985:12:0:91:175:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:reliably in practice.
11:300:19007:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  section  4  we  consider  links  between  return  volatilities  and  macroeconomic
11:301:19093:18:18:91:488:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fundamentals, with special attention to interactions across the business cycle.
11:302:19172:18:46:109:239:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We conclude in section 5.
11:303:19197:46:29:91:472:603:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:2  Conditional Portfolio-Level Risk Analysis
11:304:19241:29:18:91:519:574:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The portfolio risk measurements that we discuss in this section require only a univari-
11:305:19328:18:18:91:519:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ate portfolio-level model.  In contrast,  active portfolio risk management,  including
11:306:19414:18:18:91:519:538:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:V aRminimization  and  sensitivity  analysis,  as  well  as  system-wide  risk  measure-
11:307:19502:18:18:91:500:520:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ments, all require a multivariate model, as we discuss subsequently in section 3.
11:308:19583:18:18:109:520:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  practice,  portfolio  level  analysis  is  often  done  via  historical  simulation,  as
11:309:19675:18:18:91:519:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:detailed  above.   We  argue,  however,  that  there  is  no  reason  why  one  cannot  esti-
11:310:19768:18:18:91:519:466:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mate a parsimonious dynamic model for portfolio level returns.  If interest centers
11:311:19851:18:18:91:519:448:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the distribution of the portfolio returns,  then this distribution can be modeled
11:312:19935:18:18:91:519:430:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:directly  rather  than  via  aggregation  based  on  a  larger,  and  almost  inevitably  less
11:313:20029:18:18:91:265:412:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well-specified, multivariate model.
11:314:20064:18:18:109:520:394:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  construction  of  historical  returns  on  the  portfolio  in  place  is  a  necessary
11:315:20155:18:17:91:519:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:precursor to any portfolio-level risk analysis.  In principle it is easy to construct a
11:316:20242:17:18:91:520:359:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time  series  of  historical  portfolio  returns  using  current  portfolio  holdings,WT=
11:317:20331:18:0:91:177:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(w1,T, ... ,wN,T)
11:318:20348:0:7:178:180:348:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:A:′
11:319:20349:7:0:185:441:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:and historical asset returns,6Rt=  (r1,t, ... ,rN,t)
11:320:20401:0:7:442:444:348:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:?:′
11:321:20402:7:41:446:449:341:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?::
11:322:20403:41:0:187:221:300:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:rw,t=
11:323:20408:0:29:235:247:315:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:N∑
11:324:20410:29:0:232:246:286:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:i=1
11:325:20413:0:0:252:319:300:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:wi,Tri,t≡W
11:326:20423:0:11:322:324:308:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:A:′
11:327:20424:11:36:319:520:297:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:TRt, t= 1,2,...,T .(3)
11:328:20446:36:18:91:519:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  practice,  however,  historical  prices  for  the  assets  held  today  may  not  be  avail-
11:329:20542:18:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:able.   Examples  where  difficulties  arise  include  derivatives,  individual  bonds  with
11:330:20634:18:18:91:519:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:various maturities, private equity, new public companies, merger companies and so
11:331:20715:18:18:91:519:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on.  For these cases “pseudo” historical prices must be constructed using either pric-
11:332:20801:18:18:91:519:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing models, factor models or some ad hoc considerations.  The current assets without
11:333:20885:18:15:105:519:171:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:6The portfolio return is a linear combination of asset returns when simple rates of returns are
11:334:20980:15:0:91:519:156:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:used.  When log returns are used the portfolio return is only approximately linear in asset returns.
12:335:21081:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:historical prices can, for example, be matched to “similar” assets by capitalization,
12:336:21166:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:industry, leverage, and duration.  Historical pseudo asset prices and returns can then
12:337:21252:18:18:91:429:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be constructed using the historical prices on the substitute assets.
12:338:21320:18:18:109:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We focus our discussion onV aR.7We begin with a discussion of the direct com-
12:339:21397:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:putation of portfolioV aRvia exponential smoothing, followed by GARCH modeling,
12:340:21476:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and more recent realized volatility based procedures.  Notwithstanding a number of
12:341:21558:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well-know drawbacks, see, e.g., Stulz (2008),V aRremains by far the most prominent
12:342:21640:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and commonly-used quantitative risk measure.  The main techniques that we discuss
12:343:21721:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are, however, easily adapted to allow for the calculation of other portfolio-level risk
12:344:21808:18:39:91:389:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measures, and we will briefly discuss how to do so as well.
12:345:21867:39:22:91:519:484:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:F:2.1  Modeling Time-Varying Volatilities Using Daily Data
12:346:21923:22:26:128:220:462:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:and GARCH
12:347:21932:26:18:91:520:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The lack of conditionality in the HS-V aRand related HS approaches discussed above
12:348:22014:18:18:91:519:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is a serious concern.  Several procedures are available for remedying this deficiency.
12:349:22100:18:18:91:519:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Chief among these are RiskMetrics (RM) and Generalized Autoregressive Conditional
12:350:22181:18:17:91:519:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Heteroskedasticity  (GARCH)  models,  both  of  which  are  easy  to  implement  on  a
12:351:22267:17:35:91:347:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio basis.  We discuss each approach in turn.
12:352:22318:35:26:91:371:330:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.1.1  Exponential Smoothing and RiskMetrics
12:353:22362:26:18:91:520:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Whereas  the  HS-V aRmethodology  makes  no  explicit  assumptions  about  the  dis-
12:354:22446:18:18:91:519:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tributional  model  generating  the  returns,  the  RM  filter/model  implicitly  assumes
12:355:22535:18:18:91:519:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a very tight parametric specification by incorporating conditionality via univariate
12:356:22619:18:17:91:519:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio-level exponential smoothing of squared portfolio returns.  This directly par-
12:357:22706:17:18:91:519:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allels the exponential smoothing of individual return squares and cross products that
12:358:22791:18:16:105:519:215:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:7Although the Basel Accord calls for banks to report 1%V aR’s, for various reasons banks tend
12:359:22884:16:12:91:519:199:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:to report more conservativeV aR’s; see, e.g., the results in Berkowitz and O’Brien (2002), Perignon
12:360:22983:12:12:91:519:187:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:et al. (2008), Perignon and Smith (2010a) and Perignon and Smith (2010b).  Rather than simply
12:361:23076:12:12:91:520:175:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:scaling  up  a  1%V aRbased  on  some  “arbitrary”  multiplication  factor,  the  procedures  that  we
12:362:23178:12:0:91:454:163:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:discuss below may readily be used to achieve any desired, more conservative,V aR.
13:363:23260:0:18:91:412:685:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:underlies the basic RM approach at the individual asset level.8
13:364:23323:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Again,  taking  the  portfolio-level  pseudo  returns  from  (3)  as  the  data  series  of
13:365:23414:18:33:91:379:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest we can define the portfolio-level RM variance as
13:366:23471:33:33:226:520:616:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=λσ2t−1+  (1−λ)r2w,t−1,(4)
13:367:23500:33:18:91:520:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the variance forecast for daytis constructed at the end of dayt−1 using the
13:368:23581:18:18:91:520:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:square of the return observed at the end of dayt−1 as well as the variance on day
13:369:23662:18:18:91:520:547:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:t−1.  In practice this recursion can be initialized by setting the initialσ20equal to the
13:370:23751:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unconditional sample variance, say ˆσ2.  Note that repeated substitution in (4) yields
13:371:23837:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an expression for the current smoothed value as an exponentially weighted moving
13:372:23917:18:37:91:255:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:average of past squared returns:
13:373:23949:37:0:247:275:456:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=
13:374:23953:0:29:289:302:471:8:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f10:A:∞∑
13:375:23955:29:0:286:301:442:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:j=0
13:376:23958:0:41:306:364:456:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:φjr2w,t−1−j,
13:377:23970:41:18:91:121:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where
13:378:23975:18:26:260:350:397:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:φj=  (1−λ)λj.
13:379:23988:26:18:91:308:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence the name “exponential smoothing.”
13:380:24027:18:33:109:390:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the RM framework,V aRis then simply obtained as
13:381:24077:33:32:232:520:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:RM-VaRpT+1|T≡σT+1Φ−1p,(5)
13:382:24102:32:18:91:520:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where Φ−1pis thepthquantile of the standard normal distribution.  Although other
13:383:24182:18:18:91:519:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributions and quantiles could be used in place of the normal – and sometimes are –
13:384:24268:18:18:91:519:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the assumption of conditional normality remains dominant.  Similarly, the smoothing
13:385:24351:18:18:91:520:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameterλmay in principle be calibrated to best fit the specific historical returns at
13:386:24438:18:18:91:519:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hand although, following RM, it is typically fixed at a preset value of 0.94 with daily
13:387:24525:18:15:105:519:198:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:8Empirically more realistic long-memory hyperbolic decay structures, similar to the long-memory
13:388:24620:15:12:91:519:183:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:type GARCH models briefly discussed below, have also been explored by RM more recently; see,
13:389:24712:12:12:91:519:171:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:e.g., Zumbach (2006).  However, following standard practice we will continue to refer to exponential
13:390:24812:12:0:91:263:159:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:smoothing simply as the RM approach.
14:391:24849:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns.  Altogether, the implicit assumption of zero mean returns, a fixed smoothing
14:392:24934:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameter, and conditional normality therefore implies that no parameters and/or
14:393:25014:18:18:91:270:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributions need to be estimated.
14:394:25049:18:18:109:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Extending the approach to longer return horizons,  the conditional variance for
14:395:25128:18:33:91:225:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thek-day return in RM is
14:396:25152:33:33:149:520:580:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:V ar(rw,t+k+rw,t+k−1+...+rw,t+1|Ft)≡σ2t:t+k|t=k σ2t+1.(6)
14:397:25209:33:18:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence the RM model can be thought of as a random walk model in variance, insofar
14:398:25289:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the variance scales with the return horizon.  More precisely, exponential smoothing
14:399:25375:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is optimal if and only if squared returns follow a “random walk plus noise” model – a
14:400:25460:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“local level” model in the terminology of Harvey (1989) – in which case the minimum
14:401:25543:17:18:91:438:476:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:MSE forecast at any horizon is simply the current smoothed value.9
14:402:25609:18:18:109:520:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Unfortunately, however, the historical record of volatility across numerous asset
14:403:25690:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:classes suggest that volatilities are unlikely to follow random walks, and hence that
14:404:25775:18:18:91:519:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the flat forecast function associated with exponential smoothing is inappropriate for
14:405:25860:18:18:91:519:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility.  In particular, the lack of mean-reversion in the RM variance calculations
14:406:25946:18:18:91:519:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies that the term structure of volatility is always flat,  which violates both in-
14:407:26032:18:18:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tuition  and  historical  experience.   Suppose,  for  example,  that  current  volatility  is
14:408:26126:18:18:91:519:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high by historical standards, as was the case during the height of the financial crisis
14:409:26213:18:18:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  the  earlier  part  of  the  sample  in  Figures  1  and  2.   The  RM  model  will  then
14:410:26307:18:18:91:519:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simply extrapolate the high current volatility across all future horizons.  By contrast,
14:411:26395:18:18:91:519:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an empirically more realistic mean-reverting volatility model would correctly predict
14:412:26480:18:18:91:477:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the high volatility observed during the crisis would eventually subside.
14:413:26557:18:17:109:520:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  dangers  of  simply  scaling  the  daily  variance  by  the  horizonk,  as  done  in
14:414:26646:17:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(6),  are  discussed  further  in  Diebold  et  al.  (1998a).   Of  course,  the  one-day  RM
14:415:26739:18:18:91:519:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility  does  adjust  much  more  quickly  to  changing  market  conditions  than  the
14:416:26829:18:18:91:519:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:HS  approach,  but  the  flat  volatility  term  structure  is  unrealistic  and,  when  taken
14:417:26923:18:18:91:519:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:literally, RM does not appear to be a prudent approach to volatility modeling and
14:418:27004:18:18:91:519:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measurement.  Furthermore, it is only valid as a volatility filter and not as a data
14:419:27088:18:0:105:240:153:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:A:9See Nerlove and Wage (1964).
15:420:27119:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:generating  process  for  simulating  future  returns.   Hence  we  now  turn  to  GARCH
15:421:27207:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models, which allow for much richer terms structures of volatility and which can be
15:422:27290:18:35:91:358:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used to simulate the return process forward in time.
15:423:27342:35:26:91:279:614:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.1.2  The GARCH(1,1) Model
15:424:27369:26:18:91:519:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To allow for time variation in both the conditional mean and variance of univariate
15:425:27452:18:32:91:225:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio returns, we write
15:426:27479:32:33:153:520:538:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:rw,t=μt+σtzt,  zt∼i.i.d., E(zt) = 0, V ar(zt) = 1.(7)
15:427:27532:33:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For  simplicity  we  will  henceforth  assume  a  zero  conditional  mean,μt≡0.   This
15:428:27618:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:directly parallels the RM approach, and it is a common assumption in risk manage-
15:429:27699:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment when short (e.g., daily or weekly) return horizons are considered.  It is readily
15:430:27785:18:18:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:justified by the fact that the magnitude of the daily volatility (conditional standard
15:431:27871:18:18:91:520:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deviation)σteasily dominates that ofμtfor most portfolios of practical interest.  This
15:432:27957:18:18:91:519:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is also indirectly manifest by the fact that,  in practice,  accurate estimation of the
15:433:28044:18:18:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mean is typically much more difficult than accurate estimation of volatility.  Still,
15:434:28129:18:18:91:519:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional  mean  dynamics  could  easily  be  incorporated  into  any  of  the  GARCH
15:435:28216:18:17:91:511:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models discussed below by considering demeaned returnsrw,t−μtin place ofrw,t.
15:436:28293:17:18:109:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The key object of interest is the conditional standard deviation,σt.  If it depends
15:437:28376:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:non-trivially  on  the  currently  observed  conditioning  information,  we  say  thatrw,t
15:438:28466:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:follows a GARCH process.  Numerous competing parameterizations forσthave been
15:439:28543:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proposed in the literature for best capturing the temporal dependencies in the con-
15:440:28626:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ditional variance of portfolio returns; see, e.g., the list of models and corresponding
15:441:28713:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:acronyms in Bollerslev (2010).  However, the simple symmetric GARCH(1,1) intro-
15:442:28792:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:duced by Bollerslev (1986) remains by far the most commonly used formulation in
15:443:28871:18:33:91:335:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:practice.  The GARCH(1,1) model is defined by
15:444:28916:33:32:229:520:185:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=ω+αr2w,t−1+β σ2t−1.(8)
15:445:28942:32:0:91:519:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Extensions to higher order GARCH models are straightforward but usually unnec-
16:446:29022:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:essary empirically,  so we concentrate on the GARCH(1,1) throughout most of the
16:447:29101:18:18:91:507:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:chapter, while discussing some important generalizations in the following section.
16:448:29183:18:18:109:531:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Perhaps surprisingly, GARCH is closely-related to exponential smoothing of squared
16:449:29265:18:39:91:314:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns.  Repeated substitution in (8) yields
16:450:29310:39:0:224:252:592:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=
16:451:29314:0:16:270:277:600:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:ω
16:452:29315:16:0:260:288:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:1−β
16:453:29318:0:0:294:315:592:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:?:+α
16:454:29320:0:29:323:336:607:8:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f10:A:∞∑
16:455:29322:29:0:320:335:578:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:j=1
16:456:29325:0:41:340:387:592:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:βj−1r2t−j,
16:457:29335:41:18:91:524:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so the GARCH(1,1) process implies that current volatility is an exponentially weighted
16:458:29421:18:18:91:519:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:moving average of past squared returns.  Hence GARCH(1,1) volatility measurement
16:459:29501:18:18:91:299:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is related to RM volatility measurement.
16:460:29541:18:18:109:520:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:There  are,  however,  crucial  differences  between  GARCH  and  RM.  First,  the
16:461:29623:18:18:91:519:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH  parameters,  and  hence  ultimately  the  GARCH  volatility,  are  estimated
16:462:29706:18:18:91:519:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using rigorous statistical methods that facilitate probabilistic inference.  By contrast,
16:463:29795:18:18:91:519:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the parameters used in exponential smoothing are set in an ad hoc fashion.  More
16:464:29875:18:17:91:520:425:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specifically, the vector of GARCH parameters,θ= (ω,α,β),is typically estimated
16:465:29953:17:40:91:308:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by maximizing the log likelihood function,
16:466:29995:40:0:158:295:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:?:lnL(θ;rw,T,...,rw,1)∝ −
16:467:30018:0:29:303:315:383:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:T∑
16:468:30020:29:0:299:313:354:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:t=1
16:469:30023:0:9:319:324:377:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:[
16:470:30024:9:0:326:336:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ln
16:471:30026:0:9:338:343:377:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(
16:472:30027:9:0:343:370:368:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:σ2t(θ)
16:473:30033:0:9:370:375:377:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:)
16:474:30034:9:0:378:440:368:12:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f6:?:−σ−2t(θ)r2w,t
16:475:30047:0:9:443:448:377:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:]
16:476:30048:9:40:452:520:368:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:.(9)
16:477:30052:40:18:91:520:328:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This likelihood function is based on the assumption thatztin (7) isi.i.d. N(0,1).
16:478:30133:18:18:91:519:310:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:However, the assumption of conditional normality underlying the (quasi-) likelihood
16:479:30216:18:18:91:519:292:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function in (9) is merely a matter of convenience.  If the conditional return distri-
16:480:30301:18:18:91:519:274:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bution  is  non-normal,  the  resulting  quasi  MLE  generally  still  produces  consistent
16:481:30392:18:18:91:519:256:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and asymptotically normal, albeit not fully efficient, parameter estimates, see, e.g.,
16:482:30478:18:18:91:519:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bollerslev and Wooldridge (1992).  The log-likelihood optimization in (9) can only be
16:483:30563:18:17:91:519:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:done numerically.  However, GARCH models are parsimonious and specified directly
16:484:30643:17:18:91:519:203:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in terms of univariate portfolio returns, so that only a single numerical optimization
16:485:30729:18:16:91:149:185:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:is needed.10
16:486:30741:16:15:101:519:169:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:10This optimization can be performed in a matter of seconds on a standard desktop computer
16:487:30831:15:0:91:519:154:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:using standard software such as Excel, as discussed by Christoffersen (2003).  For further discussion
17:488:30934:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second,  and crucially from the vantage point of financial market risk measure-
17:489:31013:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment, the covariance stationary GARCH(1,1) process has dynamics that eventually
17:490:31092:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:produce reversion in volatility to a constant long-run value.  This enables interesting
17:491:31179:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  realistic  forecasts  and  contrasts  sharply  with  the  RM  exponential  smoothing
17:492:31268:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approach in which, as discussed earlier, the term structure of volatility is forced to
17:493:31354:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be flat.  To see the mean reversion that GARCH enables, rewrite the GARCH(1,1)
17:494:31432:18:18:91:169:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model in (8) as
17:495:31447:18:26:196:520:559:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=  (1−α−β)σ2+αr2w,t−1+β σ2t−1,(10)
17:496:31484:26:18:91:520:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereσ2≡ω/(1−α−β) denotes the long-run, or unconditional daily variance, or
17:497:31559:18:33:91:167:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equivalently as
17:498:31574:33:32:183:520:482:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(σ2t−σ2)  =α(r2w,t−1−σ2) +β(σ2t−1−σ2).(11)
17:499:31616:32:18:91:519:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence the forecasted deviation of the conditional variance from the long-run vari-
17:500:31698:18:18:91:519:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance is a weighted average of the deviation of the current conditional variance from
17:501:31782:18:18:91:519:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  long-run  variance,  and  the  deviation  of  the  squared  return  from  the  long-run
17:502:31874:18:18:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance.  RM’s exponential smoothing creates a parallel weighted average, with the
17:503:31957:18:18:91:520:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:key difference that exponential smoothing imposesα+β= 1,  whereas covariance
17:504:32033:18:33:91:519:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stationary GARCH(1,1) imposesα+β <1.  Finally, we can rearrange (11) to write
17:505:32110:33:33:168:520:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(σ2t−σ2)  =  (α+β) (σ2t−1−σ2) +ασ2t−1(z2t−1−1),(12)
17:506:32161:33:17:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where  the  last  term  on  the  right  has  zero  mean.   Hence,  the  mean  reversion  of
17:507:32252:17:18:91:520:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the conditional variance (or lack thereof) is governed by (α+β).  So long as (α+
17:508:32332:18:18:91:519:259:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:β)<1,  which  must  hold  for  the  covariance  stationary  GARCH(1,1)  processes  of
17:509:32417:18:18:91:519:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:empirical  relevance,  the  conditional  variance  is  mean-reverting,  with  the  speed  of
17:510:32509:18:18:91:279:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mean reversion governed by (α+β).
17:511:32542:18:18:109:520:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The mean-reverting property of GARCH volatility forecasts has important impli-
17:512:32620:18:18:91:519:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cations for the volatility term structure.  To construct the volatility term structure
17:513:32706:18:22:91:520:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:corresponding to a GARCH(1,1) model, we need thek-day ahead conditional vari-
17:514:32783:22:0:91:373:147:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:of inference in GARCH models, see also Andersen et al. (2006a).
18:515:32848:0:33:91:436:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance forecast.  By repeated substitution in equation (12), we obtain
18:516:32916:33:33:206:520:652:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t+k|t=σ2+ (α+β)k−1(σ2t+1−σ2).(13)
18:517:32951:33:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Under our maintained assumption that returns have conditional mean zero, the vari-
18:518:33033:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance of thek-day cumulative return is simply the sum of the corresponding 1- through
18:519:33117:18:18:91:520:583:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:k-day ahead variance forecasts.  Simplifying this sum,  it may be informatively ex-
18:520:33200:18:21:91:143:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pressed as
18:521:33210:21:0:182:334:544:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t:t+k|t=k σ2+ (σ2t+1−σ2)
18:522:33236:0:9:337:346:561:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(
18:523:33237:9:16:347:410:552:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:?:1−(α+β)k
18:524:33245:16:0:354:404:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:?:1−α−β
18:525:33250:0:17:413:422:561:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:)
18:526:33251:17:29:425:520:544:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:.(14)
18:527:33256:29:18:91:519:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence, in contrast to the flat volatility term structure associated with the RM fore-
18:528:33341:18:18:91:519:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cast  in  (6),  the  GARCH  volatility  term  structure  is  upward  or  downward  sloping
18:529:33431:18:18:91:519:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depending  on  the  level  of  current  conditional  variance  compared  to  long-run  vari-
18:530:33523:18:17:91:117:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance.
18:531:33528:17:18:109:520:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To summarize the discussion thus far, we have seen that GARCH is attractive
18:532:33603:18:18:91:519:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relative to RM because it moves from ad hoc exponential smoothing to rigorous yet
18:533:33684:18:18:91:519:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple likelihood-based probabilistic modeling, and because it allows for the mean
18:534:33766:18:18:91:519:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reversion routinely observed in actual financial market volatilities.  In addition, and
18:535:33853:18:18:91:519:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:crucially, the basic GARCH(1,1) model is readily extended in a variety of important
18:536:33936:18:35:91:379:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and empirically-useful directions, to which we now turn.
18:537:33992:35:25:91:366:319:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.1.3  Extensions of the Basic GARCH Model
18:538:34034:25:18:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:One important generalization of the basic GARCH(1,1) model involves the enrich-
18:539:34113:18:18:91:519:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ment of the dynamics via higher-order specifications to obtain GARCH(p,q) models
18:540:34193:18:18:91:520:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:withp≥1,q≥1.   Indeed,  Engle  and  Lee  (1999)  show  that  the  GARCH(2,2)  is
18:541:34273:18:18:91:519:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of particular interest because, under certain parameter restrictions, it implies that
18:542:34358:18:18:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional variance dynamics may be decomposed into long-run and short-run com-
18:543:34438:18:18:91:134:204:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ponents,
18:544:34446:18:0:180:520:186:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(σ2t−qt)  =α(r2w,t−1−qt−1) +β(σ2t−1−qt−1),(15)
19:545:34494:0:33:91:455:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the long-run component,qt, is a separate autoregressive process,
19:546:34564:33:33:210:520:652:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:qt=ω+ρqt−1+φ(r2w,t−1−σ2t−1).(16)
19:547:34596:33:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Of course, this “component GARCH” model is a very special version of a component
19:548:34676:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model, and one may argue that it is not a component model at all, but rather just
19:549:34757:18:18:91:224:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a restricted GARCH(2,2).
19:550:34781:18:18:109:520:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:More  general  component  modeling  is  easily  undertaken,  however,  allowing  for
19:551:34865:18:18:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:additive superposition of independent autoregressive-type components, as in Gallant
19:552:34948:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et  al.  (1999),  Alizadeh  et  al.  (2002)  and  Christoffersen  et  al.  (2008),  all  of  whom
19:553:35045:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:find  evidence  of  component  structure  in  volatility.   Under  appropriate  conditions,
19:554:35136:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such structures may be shown to approximate very strong dependence, i.e.  “long-
19:555:35216:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:memory,”  in  which  shocks  to  the  conditional  variance  decay  at  a  slow  hyperbolic
19:556:35307:18:18:91:519:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate,  see,  e.g.,  Granger  (1980),  Cox  (1981),  Andersen  and  Bollerslev  (1997),  and
19:557:35398:18:18:91:295:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Barndorff-Nielsen and Shephard (2001).
19:558:35436:18:18:109:520:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Exact  long-memory  behavior can  also easily  be  incorporated into  the GARCH
19:559:35515:18:18:91:519:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling  framework  to  more  closely  mimic  the  dependencies  observed  with  most
19:560:35601:18:18:91:519:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial assets  and/or  portfolios;  see,  e.g.,  Bollerslev and  Mikkelsen  (1999).11As
19:561:35691:18:18:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed further below, properly incorporating these types of long-memory depen-
19:562:35772:18:18:91:519:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dencies generally also results in more accurate volatility forecasts over long horizons.
19:563:35860:18:18:109:520:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To take a second example of the extensibility of GARCH models, note that all
19:564:35936:18:18:91:519:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the models considered so far, including the RM filter, imply symmetric response
19:565:36018:18:18:91:519:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to positive and negative return shocks.  However, equity markets, and particularly
19:566:36100:18:18:91:519:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equity indexes, often seem to display a strong asymmetry, whereby a negative return
19:567:36183:18:17:91:519:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:boosts  volatility  by  more  than  a  positive  return  of  the  same  absolute  magnitude.
19:568:36275:17:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  standard  GARCH  model  is  readily  extended  to  capture  this  effect  by  simply
19:569:36364:18:18:91:519:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:including  a  separate  term  for  the  past  negative  return  shocks,  as  in  the  so-called
19:570:36459:18:16:101:519:207:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:11The basic RiskMetrics approach has also recently been extended to allow the smoothing param-
19:571:36553:16:12:91:520:191:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:etersφjused in filtering the returns to exhibit a fixed pre-specified hyperbolic slow long-memory
19:572:36650:12:12:91:519:179:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:type decay;  see Zumbach (2006).  However,  the same general set of drawbacks pertaining to the
19:573:36745:12:0:91:192:167:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:basic RM filter remain.
20:574:36770:0:33:91:399:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:threshold-GARCH model proposed by Glosten et al. (1993),
20:575:36826:33:33:168:520:652:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=ω+αr2w,t−1+γ r2w,t−1I(rw,t−1<0) +β σ2t−1,(17)
20:576:36875:33:18:91:520:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereI(·) denotes the indicator function.  For well diversified equity portfoliosγis
20:577:36959:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:typically  estimated  to  be  positive  and  highly  statistically  significant.   In  fact,  the
20:578:37056:18:18:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asymmetry in the volatility appears to  have increased over time and  the estimate
20:579:37138:18:18:91:519:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the conventionalαARCH coefficient in equation (17) is often insignificant with
20:580:37220:18:18:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recent data, so that the dynamics appear to be driven exclusively by the negative
20:581:37301:18:18:91:127:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shocks.
20:582:37308:18:18:109:520:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Other popular asymmetric GARCH models include the EGARCH model of Nel-
20:583:37378:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:son (1991), in which the logarithmic conditional variance is a function of the “raw”
20:584:37462:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and absolute standardized return shocks, and the NGARCH model of Engle and Ng
20:585:37539:18:33:91:281:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(1993).  In the NGARCH(1,1) model,
20:586:37573:33:33:199:520:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=ω+α(rw,t−1−γ σt−1)2+β σ2t−1,(18)
20:587:37609:33:18:91:471:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where asymmetric response in the conventional direction occurs forγ >0.
20:588:37680:18:18:109:520:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  parallel  to  the  RM-V aRdefined  in  equation  (5),  a  GARCH-based  one-day
20:589:37762:18:18:91:520:356:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:V aRmay correspondingly be calculated by simply multiplying the one-day volatility
20:590:37844:18:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forecast from any GARCH model by the requisite quantile in the standard normal
20:591:37922:18:18:91:154:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution,
20:592:37935:18:25:220:520:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:GARCH-VaRpT+1|T≡σT+1Φ−1p.(19)
20:593:37964:25:18:91:520:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This GARCH-V aR, of course, implicitly assumes that the returns are conditionally
20:594:38045:18:18:91:519:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:normally distributed. This is a much better approximation than assuming the returns
20:595:38128:18:18:91:519:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are unconditionally normally distributed,  and it is entirely consistent with the fat
20:596:38213:18:18:91:405:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tails routinely observed in unconditional return distributions.
20:597:38276:18:18:109:520:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As  noted  earlier,  however,  standardized  innovationsztfrom  GARCH  models
20:598:38353:18:18:91:519:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sometimes have fatter tails than the normal distribution, indicating that conditional
20:599:38438:18:18:91:519:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:normality  is  not  acceptable.   The  GARCH-based  approach  explicitly  allows  us  to
20:600:38526:18:0:91:519:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:remedy  this  problem,  by  using  other  conditional  distributions  and  corresponding

21:623:39072:18:18:91:520:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Note  also  that  in  contrast  to  the  RM-basedV aRs,  which  simply  scale  with  the

21:628:39415:18:18:109:519:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For now,  to illustrate the conditionality afforded by the GARCH-V aR,  and to
21:629:39493:18:18:91:520:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contrast it with HS-V aR, we plot in Figure 3 theV aRs from an NGARCH model
21:630:39568:18:17:91:519:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and RiskMetrics (RM). The figure clearly shows that allowing for GARCH (or RM)
21:631:39646:17:18:91:520:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditionally makes theV aRs move up and, equally importantly, come down much
21:632:39723:18:18:91:520:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:faster than the HS-V aRs.  Moreover, contrasting the two curves, it is evident that
21:633:39806:18:18:91:520:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allowing for asymmetry in a rising market desirably allows NGARCH-V aRto drop
21:634:39883:18:18:91:520:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more  quickly  than  RM-V aR.   Conversely,  the  NGARCH-V aRrises  more  quickly
21:635:39964:18:0:91:520:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than RM-V aR(andV aRs based on symmetric GARCH models) in falling markets.
22:636:40040:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Several studies by Engle (2001), Engle (2004), Engle (2009b), and Engle (2011) have
22:637:40123:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shown that allowing for asymmetries in the conditional variance can materially affect
22:638:40208:18:18:91:204:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH-basedV aRs.
22:639:40225:18:18:109:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  procedures  discussed  in  this  section  were  originally  developed  for  daily  or
22:640:40315:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:coarser  frequency  returns.   However,  high-frequency  intraday  price  data  are  now
22:641:40403:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:readily available for a host of different assets and markets.  We next review recent
22:642:40487:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:research on so-called realized volatilities constructed from such high-frequency data,
22:643:40573:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and show how to use them to provide even more accurate assessment and modeling
22:644:40651:18:39:91:199:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of daily market risks.
22:645:40673:39:26:91:395:502:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.2  Intraday Data and Realized Volatility
22:646:40715:26:17:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Higher frequency data add little to the estimation of expected returns.  At the same
22:647:40799:17:18:91:519:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time,  however,  the theoretical results in Merton (1980) and Nelson (1992) suggest
22:648:40882:18:18:91:519:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that higher frequency data should be very useful in the construction of more accurate
22:649:40967:18:18:91:519:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility  models,  and  in  turn  expected  risks.   In  practice,  however,  the  statistical
22:650:41063:18:18:91:519:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling of high-frequency data is notoriously difficult, and the daily GARCH and
22:651:41144:18:18:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:related volatility forecasting procedures discussed in the previous section have been
22:652:41229:18:18:91:519:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shown  to  work  poorly  when  applied  directly  to  high-frequency  intraday  returns;
22:653:41317:18:18:91:519:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:see, e.g., Andersen and Bollerslev (1997) and Andersen et al. (1999).  Fortunately,
22:654:41400:18:18:91:519:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:extensive research efforts over the past decade have shown how the rich information
22:655:41483:18:18:91:519:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inherent in the now readily available high-frequency data may be effectively harnessed
22:656:41569:18:18:91:378:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:through the use of so-called realized volatility measures.
22:657:41627:18:18:109:520:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To formally define the realized volatility concepts, imagine that the instantaneous
22:658:41710:18:18:91:519:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns, or logarithmic price increments, evolve continuously through time according

22:660:41832:32:33:226:520:211:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:dp(t)  =μ(t)dt+σ(t)dW(t),(20)
22:661:41861:33:0:91:519:178:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereμ(t)  andσ(t)  denote the instantaneous drift and volatility, respectively, and

23:663:42030:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time return representation in equation (7), withrw,t≡p(t)−p(t−1) and the unit
23:664:42107:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time interval normalized to a day.  Just as the conditional mean in equation (7) can
23:665:42191:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be  safely  set  to  zero,  so  too  can  the  drift  term  in  equation  (20).   Hence,  in  what
23:666:42289:18:18:91:213:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:follows, we setμ(t) = 0.
23:667:42313:18:18:109:523:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Following Andersen and Bollerslev (1998b), Andersen et al. (2001b) and Barndorff-
23:668:42394:18:18:91:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Nielsen and Shephard (2002), the realized variation (RV) on daytbased on returns

23:679:42723:18:18:91:520:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns in a 24-hour market, corresponding to ∆ = 5/(24·60)≈0.00347, while 5-
23:680:42800:18:18:91:519:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:minute returns in a market that is open for six-and-half hours per day, like the U.S.

23:682:42960:18:18:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expression in equation (21) looks exactly like a sample variance for the high-frequency

23:684:43128:18:18:91:391:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the returns are not centered around the sample mean.
23:685:43184:18:18:109:520:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Assume  for  the  time  being  that  the  prices  defined  by  the  process  in  equation

23:687:43357:18:18:91:520:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to progressively finer sampled returns, theRVestimator approaches the integrated
23:688:43437:18:18:91:519:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance  of  the  underlying  continuous-time  stochastic  volatility  process  on  dayt,
23:689:43527:18:15:101:519:261:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:12The notion of a continuously evolving around-the-clock price process is,  of course,  fictitious.
23:690:43626:15:12:91:519:246:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Most financial markets are only open for part of the day, and prices are not continuously updated and
23:691:43727:12:12:91:519:234:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:sometimes jump.  The specific procedures discussed below have all been adapted to accommodate
23:692:43820:12:12:91:519:222:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:these features and other types of market microstructure frictions, or “noise,” in the actually observed
23:693:43923:12:0:91:186:210:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:high-frequency prices.
24:694:43947:0:22:91:200:685:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:formally defined by,13
24:695:43969:22:0:249:281:663:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:IVt=
24:696:43973:0:27:291:306:679:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:A:∫t
24:697:43975:27:0:297:311:652:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:t−1
24:698:43978:0:29:316:520:663:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2(τ)dτ.(22)
24:699:43990:29:18:91:519:634:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hence,  in  contrast  to  the  RM-  and  GARCH-based  volatility  estimates  discussed
24:700:44076:18:18:91:520:616:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:above, thetrueex-post volatility for the day effectively becomes observable.  And it
24:701:44160:18:18:91:519:598:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does so in an entirely model-free fashion regardless of the underlying process that
24:702:44243:18:18:91:210:580:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:actually describesσ(t).
24:703:44266:18:17:109:520:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In practice, of course, prices are not available on a continuous basis.  However,
24:704:44347:17:18:91:520:545:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with  prices  for  many  assets  recorded,  say,  every  minute,  a  dailyRVcould  easily
24:705:44436:18:18:91:519:527:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be  computed  from  one-minute  squared  returns.   Still,  returns  at  the  one-minute
24:706:44524:18:18:91:519:509:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequency  are  likely  affected  by  various  market  microstructure  frictions,  ornoise,
24:707:44615:18:18:91:520:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:arising from bid-ask bounces, a discrete price grid, and the like.14Of course, even
24:708:44698:18:18:91:519:473:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with  one-minute  price  observations  on  hand,  we  may  decide  to  construct  the  RV
24:709:44787:18:18:91:519:455:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measures from five-minute returns, as these coarser sampled data are less susceptible
24:710:44872:18:18:91:519:437:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to contamination from market frictions.  Clearly, this involves a loss of information
24:711:44957:18:18:91:519:419:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as the majority of the recorded prices are ignored.  Expressed differently, it is feasible
24:712:45047:18:18:91:519:401:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to construct five different sets of (overlapping) 5-minute intraday return sequences
24:713:45131:18:18:91:519:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from the given data, but in computing the regular five-minute based RV measure we
24:714:45212:18:18:91:406:365:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exploit only one of these series – a theme we return to below.
24:715:45274:18:18:109:520:347:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  optimal  choice  of  high-frequency  grid  over  which  to  measure  the  returns
24:716:45360:18:17:91:519:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obviously depends on the specific market conditions.  The “volatility signature plot”
24:717:45445:17:18:91:519:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of Andersen et al. (2000b) is useful for guiding this selection.  It often indicates the
24:718:45533:18:18:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adequacy of 5-minute sampling across a variety of assets and markets, as originally
24:719:45616:18:18:91:519:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advocated by Andersen and Bollerslev (1998a).15Meanwhile, as many markets have
24:720:45694:18:18:91:519:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:become  increasingly  more  liquid  it  would  seem  reasonable  to  resort  to  even  finer
24:721:45786:18:18:91:519:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sampling intervals with more recent data although, as noted below, the gains from
24:722:45867:18:20:91:519:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:doing so in terms of the accuracy of realized volatility based forecast appear to be
24:723:45951:20:7:101:410:202:7:g_d0_f14:7:g_d0_f14:?:13More precisely, ∆−1/2(RVt(∆)−IVt)→N(0,2IQt), whereIQt≡∫1
24:724:46009:7:0:405:419:195:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f16:?:0σ
24:725:46011:0:15:419:520:202:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:4(t−1 +τ)dτand the
24:726:46029:15:9:91:502:187:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:convergence is stable in law; for a full theoretical treatment, see, e.g., Andersen et al. (2010a).
24:727:46128:9:15:101:519:178:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:14Brownlees and Gallo (2006) contain a useful discussion of the relevant effects and some of the
24:728:46224:15:8:91:339:163:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:practical issues involved in high-frequency data cleaning.
24:729:46282:8:0:101:378:155:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:15See also Hansen and Lunde (2006) and the references therein.
25:730:46346:0:18:91:155:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fairly minor.
25:731:46359:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One way to exploit all the high-frequency returns, even if the RV measure is based
25:732:46441:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on returns sampled at a lower frequency, is to compute alternative RV estimator using
25:733:46526:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  different  offset  relative  to  the  first  return  of  the  trading  day,  and  then  combine
25:734:46624:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:them.  For example, if one-minute returns are given, one may construct a new RV
25:735:46703:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimator using an equal-weighted average of the five alternative regular five-minute
25:736:46788:18:18:91:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:RV estimators available each day.  We will denote this estimatorAvgRVbelow.  The
25:737:46868:18:18:91:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:upshot  is  that  theAvgRVestimator  based  on  five-minute  returns  is  much  more
25:738:46952:18:18:91:502:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:robust to microstructure noise than the singleRVbased on one-minute returns.
25:739:47028:18:18:109:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In markets that are not open 24 hours per day, the change from the closing price
25:740:47108:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on dayt−1 to the opening price on daytshould also be accounted for.  This can
25:741:47185:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be done by simply scaling up the trading day RV by the proportion corresponding
25:742:47264:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the missing over-night variation, or any of the other more complicated methods
25:743:47345:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:advocated in Hansen and Lunde (2005).  As is the case for the daily GARCH mod-
25:744:47423:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:els discussed above, corrections may also be made for the fact that days following
25:745:47505:18:18:91:508:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weekends and holidays tend to have proportionally higher than average volatility.
25:746:47586:18:18:109:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Several other realized volatility estimators have been developed to guard against
25:747:47667:18:18:91:520:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the influences of market microstructure frictions.  In contrast to the simpleRVt(∆)
25:748:47750:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimator, which formally deteriorates as the length of the sampling interval ∆ ap-
25:749:47833:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proaches zero if the prices are observed with error, these other estimators are typ-
25:750:47917:18:18:91:520:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ically  designed  to  be  consistent  forIVtas  ∆→0,  even  in  the  presence  of  mar-
25:751:48004:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ket microstructure noise.  Especially prominent are the realized kernel estimator of
25:752:48088:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Barndorff-Nielsen et al. (2008), the pre-averaging estimator of Jacod et al. (2009),
25:753:48172:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the two-scale estimator of A ̈ıt-Sahalia et al. (2011).  These alternative estimators
25:754:48261:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are generally more complicated to implement than theAvgRVestimator, requiring
25:755:48338:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the choice of additional tuning parameters, smoothing kernels, and appropriate block
25:756:48422:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sizes.  Importantly, the results in Andersen et al. (2011a) show that, when used for
25:757:48506:18:17:91:520:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility  forecasting,  the  simple-to-implementAvgRVestimator  performs  on  par
25:758:48589:17:18:91:428:183:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:with, and often better than, these more complex RV estimators.16
25:759:48653:18:16:101:520:165:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:16Note, however, that while theAvgRVestimator provides a very effective way of incorporat-
25:760:48743:16:0:91:519:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ing  ultra  high-frequency  data  into  the  estimation  by  averaging  all  of  the  possible  squared  price

27:804:50525:123:12:91:520:459:12:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f15:B:Figure 5:  S&P500:  QQ Plots for Realized Volatility and Log Realized Volatility.The

27:808:50904:12:12:91:520:411:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:whereAvgRVis the average of five daily RVs each computed from 5-minute squared returns on a
27:809:50995:12:47:91:264:399:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:1-minute grid of S&P500 futures prices.
27:810:51034:47:18:91:318:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:largest ever recorded NYSE trading volume.
27:811:51076:18:18:109:520:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Time series plots such as that of Figure 4, of course, begin to inform us about
27:812:51155:18:18:91:519:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aspects of the dynamics of realized volatility.  We will shortly explore those dynamics
27:813:51242:18:18:91:519:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in greater detail.  But first we briefly highlight an important empirical aspect of the
27:814:51329:18:18:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributionof  realized  volatility,  which  has  been  documented  in  many  contexts:
27:815:51417:18:18:91:519:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realized volatility is highly right-skewed, whereas the natural logarithm of realized
27:816:51502:18:17:91:519:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility  is  much  closer  to  Gaussian.   In  Figure  5  we  report  two  QQ  (Quantile-
27:817:51594:17:18:91:519:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Quantile)  plots  of  different  volatility  transforms  against  the  normal  distribution.
27:818:51686:18:18:91:520:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The top panel shows the QQ plot for dailyAvgRVin standard deviation form, while
27:819:51765:18:18:91:520:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  bottom  panel  shows  the  QQ-plot  for  dailyAvgRVin  logarithmic  form.   The
27:820:51849:18:18:91:519:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:right tail in the top panel is obviously much fatter than for a normal distribution,
27:821:51933:18:0:91:519:155:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereas the right tail in the bottom panel conforms more closely to normality.  This
28:822:52019:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approximate  log-normality  of  realized  volatility  is  often  usefully  exploited,  even  if
28:823:52114:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it provides only a rough approximation, based on empirical observation rather than
28:824:52196:18:35:91:211:649:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:theoretical derivation.18
28:825:52221:35:26:91:373:614:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.2.1  Dynamic Modeling of Realized Volatility
28:826:52267:26:18:91:519:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Although dailyRVis ultimately only an estimate of the underlying true integrated
28:827:52347:18:18:91:519:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance, it is potentially highly accurate and thus presents an intriguing opportunity.
28:828:52435:18:17:91:520:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:By treating the dailyRVs, or any of the other high-frequency based RV measures, as
28:829:52517:17:18:91:519:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:direct ex-post observations of the true daily integrated variances, the RV approach
28:830:52600:18:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:permits the construction of ex-ante volatility forecasts using standard ARMA time
28:831:52681:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:series tools.  Moreover, recognizing the fact that the measures are not perfect, certain
28:832:52769:18:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:kinds of measurement errors can easily be incorporated into this framework.  The
28:833:52849:18:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:upshot is that if the frequency of interest is daily, then using sufficiently high-quality
28:834:52939:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intra-day  price  data  enables  the  risk  manager  to  treat  volatility  as  effectively  ob-
28:835:53035:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:served.  This is fundamentally different from the RM filter and GARCH style models
28:836:53117:18:18:91:519:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed  above,  in  which  the  daily  variances  are  inferred  from  past  daily  returns
28:837:53211:18:18:91:389:391:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditionalon the specific structure of the filter or model.
28:838:53271:18:18:109:520:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To further help motivate such an approach, we plot in Figure 6 the autocorrelation
28:839:53353:18:18:91:520:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function  (ACF)  of  dailyAvgRVand  daily  returns.   The  horizontal  lines  in  each
28:840:53439:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plot  show  the  Bartlett  two-standard-deviation  bands  around  zero.   The  ACFs  are
28:841:53527:18:17:91:519:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strikingly different; the realized variance ACF is always positive, highly statistically
28:842:53615:17:18:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significant, and very slowly decaying, whereas the daily return ACF is insignificantly
28:843:53701:18:18:91:519:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:different  from  zero.   The  exceptionally  slow  decay  of  the  realized  variance  ACF
28:844:53791:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggests  long-memory  dynamics,  in  turn  implying  that  equity  market  volatility  is
28:845:53881:18:18:91:519:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:highly forecastable. This long-memory property of RV is found across numerous asset
28:846:53964:18:18:91:519:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:classes; see, for example, Andersen et al. (2001b) for evidence on foreign exchange
28:847:54047:18:18:91:519:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rates  and  Andersen  et  al.  (2001a)  for  comparable  results  pertaining  to  individual
28:848:54139:18:18:91:263:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equities and equity-index returns.
28:849:54173:18:15:101:519:176:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:18Indeed, as noted by Forsberg and Bollerslev (2002), among others, RV cannot formally be log-
28:850:54267:15:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:normally distributed across all return horizons, because the log-normal distribution is not closed
28:851:54365:12:0:91:215:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:under temporal aggregation.
