29:872:54903:11:47:91:400:368:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:5-minute squared returns on a 1-minute grid of S&P500 futures prices.
29:873:54972:47:18:109:520:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Simple  AR  type  models  provide  a  natural  starting  point  for  capturing  these
29:874:55057:18:18:91:520:303:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dependencies.   LetRVtdenote  any  of  the  high-frequency-based  realized  volatility
29:875:55143:18:18:91:519:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measures introduced above.  As an example,  one could specify a simple first-order
29:876:55225:18:33:91:348:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:autoregressive model for the daily volatility series,
29:877:55278:33:33:231:520:234:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:RVt=β0+β1RVt−1+νt.(23)
29:878:55300:33:17:91:520:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This, and any higher order AR models forRVt, can easily be estimated by a standard
29:879:55382:17:18:91:215:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:OLS regression package.
29:880:55405:18:18:109:519:166:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One could go farther and endowintegratedvariance with AR(1) dynamics, and
29:881:55478:18:0:91:520:148:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recognize thatRVtcontains some measurement error since in real empirical work the
30:882:55561:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:underlying sampling cannot pass all the way to continuous time.  ThenRVtwould
30:883:55638:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equal an AR(1) process plus a measurement error, which yields an ARMA(1,1) model
30:884:55718:18:33:91:229:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if the two are independent,
30:885:55745:33:33:205:406:616:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:RVt=β0+β1RVt−1+α1νt−1+νt.
30:886:55770:33:18:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Estimation of this model formally requires use of non-linear optimization techniques,
30:887:55855:18:18:91:421:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but it is still very easy to do using standard statistical packages.
30:888:55923:18:18:109:520:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although  the  simple  short-memory  AR(1)  model  above  may  be  adequate  for
30:889:56003:18:18:91:520:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:short-horizon risk forecasts, the autocorrelation function forAvgRVshown in Fig-
30:890:56083:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ure 6 clearly suggests that when looking at longer, say monthly, forecast horizons,
30:891:56166:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more accurate forecasts may be obtained by using richer dynamic models that better
30:892:56248:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:capture the long-range dependence associated with slowly-decaying autocorrelations.
30:893:56331:18:18:91:520:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Unfortunately, however, when|β1|<1 the AR(1) process has short memory, in the
30:894:56408:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sense that its autocorrelations decay exponentially quickly.  On the other hand, when
30:895:56493:18:18:91:520:422:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:β1= 1 the process becomes a random walk (1−L)RVt=β0+νt, and has such strong
30:896:56568:18:18:91:519:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:memory that covariance stationarity and mean reversion are both lost.  A useful mid-
30:897:56652:18:33:91:427:386:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:dle ground may be obtain by allowing for fractional integration,19
30:898:56718:33:33:248:520:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(1−L)dRVt=β0+νt.(24)
30:899:56738:33:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This long-memory model is mean reverting if 0< d <1 and covariance stationary
30:900:56815:18:17:91:520:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if  0< d <1/2.   Fractional  integration  contrasts  to  the  extremely  strong  integer
30:901:56903:17:18:91:519:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:integration  associated  with  the  random  walk  (d=  1)  or  the  covariance-stationary
30:902:56992:18:18:91:520:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:AR(1) case (d= 0).  Crucially, it allows for long-memory dynamics in the sense that
30:903:57075:18:18:91:500:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:autocorrelations decay only hyperbolically, akin to the pattern seen in Figure 6.
30:904:57156:18:18:109:520:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Long-memory models can, however, be somewhat cumbersome to estimate and
30:905:57227:18:18:91:519:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implement.  Instead, a simpler approach may be pursued by directly exploiting longer
30:906:57311:18:18:91:520:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:run realized volatility regressors.  Specifically, lettingRVt−4:tandRVt−21:tdenote the
30:907:57397:18:16:101:520:177:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:19The fractional differencing operator (1−L)dis formally defined by its binomial expansion; see,
30:908:57493:16:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:e.g., Baillie et al. (1996) and the discussion therein pertaining to the so-called fractional integrated
30:909:57597:12:0:91:219:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:GARCH (FIGARCH) model.
31:910:57621:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weekly and monthly realized volatilities, respectively, obtained by summing the cor-
31:911:57705:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding daily volatilities.  Many researchers,  including Andersen et al. (2007a),
31:912:57790:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have found that the so-called heterogenous autoregressive, or HAR-RV, model, orig-
31:913:57872:18:33:91:264:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:inally introduced by Corsi (2009),
31:914:57906:33:33:152:520:598:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:RVt=β0+β1RVt−1+β2RVt−5:t−1+β3RVt−21:t−1+νt,(25)
31:915:57953:33:18:91:519:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provides  a  very  good  fit  for  most  volatility  series.   As  shown  in  Corsi  (2009),  the
31:916:58050:18:18:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:HAR  model  may  be  viewed  as  an  approximate  long-memory  model.   In  contrast
31:917:58134:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  the  exact  long-memory  model  above,  however,  the  HAR  model  can  easily  be
31:918:58220:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimated  by  OLS.  Even  closer  approximations  to  exact  long-memory  dependence
31:919:58305:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can  be  obtained  by  including  coarser,  say  quarterly,  lagged  realized  volatilities  on
31:920:58400:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the right-hand side of the equation.  A leverage effect, along the lines of the GJR-
31:921:58484:18:18:91:519:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH model discussed above, can also easily be incorporated into the HAR-RV
31:922:58560:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling framework by including on the right-hand-side additional volatility terms
31:923:58642:18:18:91:508:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interacted with dummies indicating the sign ofrt−1, as in Corsi and Reno (2010).
31:924:58722:18:33:109:479:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The HAR regressions can, of course, also be written in logarithmic form
31:925:58793:33:33:115:520:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:logRVt=β0+β1logRVt−1+β2logRVt−5:t−1+β3logRVt−21:t−1+νt.(26)
31:926:58852:33:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The log specification conveniently induces approximate normality, as demonstrated
31:927:58933:18:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Figure 5 above.  It also ensures positivity of volatility fits and forecasts, by expo-
31:928:59022:18:17:91:283:302:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:nentiating to “undo” the logarithm.20
31:929:59059:17:18:109:520:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Armed  with  a  forecast  for  tomorrow’s  volatility  from  any  one  of  the  HAR-RV
31:930:59145:18:18:91:520:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or other time series models discussed above, saŷRVT+1|T, a one-dayV aRis easily
31:931:59225:18:18:91:155:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:computed as
31:932:59236:18:26:217:520:231:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:RV−V aRpT+1|T=̂RVT+1|TΦ−1p,(27)
31:933:59267:26:20:91:520:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where  Φ−1prefers to the relevant quantile from the standard normal.  Andersen et al.
31:934:59352:20:16:101:519:185:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:20Note  however  that  forecasts  ofRVt+1obtained  by  exponentiating  forecasts  of  logRVt+1are
31:935:59449:16:12:91:519:169:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:generally biased, due to the nonlinearity of the exp(·) transformation.  Although we will not pursue
31:936:59549:12:12:91:519:157:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:it  here,  one  could  perform  a  bias  correction,  which  would  depend  on  the  possibly  time-varying
31:937:59656:12:0:91:481:145:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:variance ofνt.  A similar problem applies to the EGARCH model briefly discussed above.

32:953:59897:12:12:91:519:447:12:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f15:B:2009.The dashed line shows 10-day 1% HAR-V aRbased on the HAR forecasting model for 10-
32:954:59984:12:12:91:520:435:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:day realized volatility.  The solid line shows 10-day 1% GARCH-V aR.  When computingV aRthe
32:955:60075:12:47:91:482:423:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:10-day returns divided by the expected volatility are assumed to be normally distributed.
32:956:60164:47:18:91:520:376:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2003a) use this observation to construct RV-basedV aRs with properties superior to
32:957:60247:18:18:91:515:358:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH-V aR.  We will discuss this approach in more detail in section 2.3.2 below.
32:958:60328:18:18:109:520:340:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To illustrate, we show in Figure 7 the GARCH-V aRfrom Figure 3 together with
32:959:60404:18:18:91:520:322:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the HAR-RV-V aRbased on equation (27) constructed using the simple linear HAR-
32:960:60482:18:18:91:520:304:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:RV specification in (25). The figure shows that HAR-RV-V aRreaches its peak before
32:961:60564:18:18:91:520:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH-V aR.  Equally important, the HAR-RV-V aRdrops back to a more normal
32:962:60638:18:18:91:519:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:level sooner than the GARCH-V aRafter the trough in the market on March 2009.
32:963:60715:18:18:91:519:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Intuitively, by using the more accurate RV measure of current volatility the model
32:964:60797:18:17:91:519:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is able to more quickly adjust to the changing market conditions and overall level of
32:965:60882:17:18:91:519:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market risk.  Of course, the commonly employed RM-V aRin Figure 3 is even slower
32:966:60962:18:18:91:520:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to adjust than the GARCH-V aR, and the HS-V aRin Figure 1 adjusts so slowly that
32:967:61042:18:18:91:397:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it remains at its maximum sample value at the end of 2009.
32:968:61100:18:18:109:520:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As discussed above,V aRand other risk measures are often computed for a two-
32:969:61176:18:0:91:519:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:week horizon.  The risk manager is therefore interested in a 10-day volatility forecast.
33:970:61266:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Another advantage of the RV based approach, and the HAR-RV model in particular,
33:971:61345:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is that it can easily be adapted to deliver the required multi-period variance forecasts.
33:972:61434:18:33:91:371:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Specifically, consider the modified HAR-RV regression,
33:973:61488:33:33:134:520:616:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:RVt:t+9=β0+β1RVt−1+β2RVt−5:t−1+β3RVt−21:t−1+νt:t+9.(28)
33:974:61543:33:33:91:355:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:An RV basedV aRcan now easily be computed via
33:975:61588:33:32:202:408:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:RV−V aRpT+10|T=̂RVT+1:T+10|TΦ−1p,
33:976:61621:32:15:91:121:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where
33:977:61626:15:29:150:461:503:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f5:A:̂RVT+1:T+10|T=ˆβ0+ˆβ1RVT+ˆβ2RVT−4:T+ˆβ3RVT−20:T,
33:978:61674:29:18:91:519:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denotes the 10-day forecast obtained directly from the modified HAR-RV model in
33:979:61753:18:18:91:519:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equation (28).  Hence, in contrast to GARCH models, there is no need to resort to
33:980:61834:18:18:91:519:438:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:the use of complicated recursive expressions along the lines of the formula forσ2t:t+k|t
33:981:61922:18:18:91:519:420:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the GARCH(1,1) model in equation (14).  The modified HAR-RV model in (28)
33:982:61999:18:34:91:519:402:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:builds the appropriate mean reversion directly into the requisite variance forecasts.21
33:983:62086:34:26:91:318:368:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.2.2  Realized Volatilities and Jumps
33:984:62124:26:18:91:519:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The continuous-time process in equation (20) formally rules out discontinuities in the
33:985:62210:18:18:91:519:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:underlying price process.  However, financial prices often exhibit “large” movements
33:986:62294:18:18:91:519:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:over short time-intervals, or “jumps.” A number of these jumps are naturally associ-
33:987:62378:18:18:91:519:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ated with readily identifiable macroeconomic news announcement, see, e.g., Andersen
33:988:62461:18:18:91:519:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2003b) and Andersen et al. (2007b), but many others appear idiosyncratic or
33:989:62544:18:17:91:519:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asset specific in nature.  Such large price moves are inherently more difficult to guard
33:990:62632:17:18:91:519:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:against, and the measurement and management of jump risk requires the use of dif-
33:991:62713:18:18:91:519:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ferent statistical distributions and risk management procedures from the ones needed
33:992:62797:18:18:91:519:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to measure and manage the Gaussian diffusive price risks implied by the price process
33:993:62882:18:18:91:177:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in equation (20).
33:994:62899:18:17:109:520:163:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In particular, taking into account the possibility of jumps in the underlying price
33:995:62982:17:0:101:519:146:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:21Note however that a new HAR-RV model must be estimated for each forecast horizon of interest.
34:996:63079:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:process, the realized variation measures discussed above no longer converge to the
34:997:63161:18:33:91:435:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:integrated variance.  Instead, the total ex-post variation is given by
34:998:63231:33:33:255:520:634:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:QVt=IVt+JVt,(29)
34:999:63247:33:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereIVtas before,  in equation (22),  accounts for the variation coming from the
34:1000:63328:18:40:91:388:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:continuous, or smooth, price increments over the day, and
34:1001:63385:40:0:263:298:543:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:JVt=
34:1002:63389:0:28:311:324:558:8:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f10:?:Jt∑
34:1003:63392:28:0:308:323:530:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:j=1
34:1004:63395:0:40:328:520:543:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:J2t,j,(30)
34:1005:63405:40:18:91:520:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measures the variation due to theJtjumps that occurred on dayt;  i.e.,Jt,j, j=
34:1006:63483:18:18:91:520:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1,2,...,Jt.   This  does  not  invalidateAvgRV,  or  any  of  the  other  RV  estimators
34:1007:63571:18:18:91:519:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed  above,  as  an  ex-post  measure  for  the  total  daily  quadratic  variation,  or
34:1008:63665:18:18:91:520:449:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:QVt.   It  does,  however,  suggest  the  use  of  more  refined  procedures  for  separately
34:1009:63758:18:18:91:302:431:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimatingQVtandIVt, and in turnJVt.
34:1010:63794:18:18:109:520:413:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Several alternative volatility estimators that are (asymptotically) immune to the
34:1011:63875:18:18:91:519:395:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:impact  of  jumps  have  been  proposed  in  the  literature.   The  first  was  the  bipower
34:1012:63968:18:42:91:416:377:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variation estimator of Barndorff-Nielsen and Shephard (2004b),
34:1013:64030:42:0:147:215:335:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:BPVt(∆)   =
34:1014:64041:0:16:224:231:343:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:π
34:1015:64042:16:0:225:231:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:2
34:1016:64043:0:16:246:277:343:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:N(∆)
34:1017:64047:16:0:236:288:327:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:N(∆)−1
34:1018:64053:0:30:293:317:351:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:A:N(∆)−1∑
34:1019:64060:30:0:301:316:321:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:j=1
34:1020:64063:0:40:329:520:335:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:A:|∆pt−1+j∆| |∆pt−1+(j+1)∆|,(31)
34:1021:64093:40:18:91:520:295:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where  ∆pt−1+j∆≡pt−1+j∆−pt−1+(j−1)∆.   The  idea  behind  the  bipower  variation
34:1022:64174:18:18:91:519:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimator is intuitively simple. When ∆ goes to zero the probability of jumps arriving
34:1023:64260:18:18:91:520:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:both in time intervalj∆ and (j+ 1)∆ goes to zero along with the absolute value of
34:1024:64341:18:18:91:520:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the non-jump returns.  The product|∆pt−1+j∆||∆pt−1+(j+1)∆|will therefore vanish
34:1025:64420:18:18:91:520:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asymptotically.   Consequently,BPVt(∆)  will  converge  to  the  integrated  variance
34:1026:64505:18:18:91:519:205:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:F:IVt,  as  opposed  toQVt,  for  ∆  approaching  zero,  even  in  the  presence  of  jumps.22
34:1027:64597:18:17:91:519:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In contrast,  the key terms in the realized variance estimator,  namely the intraday
34:1028:64681:17:16:101:520:170:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:22Theπ/2 normalization arises from the fact that the expected value of an absolute standard
34:1029:64772:16:12:91:520:154:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:normal random variable equals (π/2)1/2, while the ratio involvingN(∆) provides a finite-sample
34:1030:64866:12:0:91:328:142:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:adjustment for the loss of one term in the summation.
35:1031:64921:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:squared returns (∆pt−1+j∆)2, will include the price jumps as well as the “smooth”
35:1032:65002:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:continuous price variation.  TheRVt(∆) estimator therefore always converges toQVt
35:1033:65083:18:18:91:213:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for ∆ approaching zero.
35:1034:65106:18:18:109:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:TheBPVt(∆) estimator is subject to the same type of microstructure frictions
35:1035:65182:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that plague theRVt(∆) estimator at ultra-high sampling frequencies.  Thus,  even
35:1036:65262:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:if a one-minute grid of prices is available, it might still be desirable to use coarser,
35:1037:65350:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:say  five-minute,  returns  in  the  calculation  ofBPVt(∆)  to  guard  against  market
35:1038:65437:18:18:91:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:microstructure noise.  A simple average of the five differentBPVt(∆)’s could then
35:1039:65518:18:18:91:351:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used to compute an improvedAvgBPVestimator.
35:1040:65561:18:18:109:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although theBPVt(∆) estimator is formally consistent forIVtin the idealized
35:1041:65636:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:setting without market microstructure noise, the presence of large jumps can result
35:1042:65719:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in non-trivial upward biases in practice.  Motivated by this observation,  Andersen
35:1043:65802:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2010c) recently proposed an alternative class of jump-robust estimators, the
35:1044:65886:18:41:91:463:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:neighborhood truncation measures.  The simplest version takes the form,
35:1045:65957:41:0:100:182:410:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:MinRVt(∆)   =
35:1046:65970:0:16:200:207:418:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:π
35:1047:65971:16:0:190:218:402:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:π−2
35:1048:65974:0:9:223:232:427:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:(
35:1049:65975:9:16:243:275:418:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:N(∆)
35:1050:65979:16:0:233:285:402:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:N(∆)−1
35:1051:65985:0:31:286:323:427:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:)N(∆)−1∑
35:1052:65993:31:0:308:322:396:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:j=1
35:1053:65996:0:0:335:355:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:min
35:1054:65999:0:10:356:363:420:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:{
35:1055:66000:10:0:363:494:410:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:?:|∆pt−1+j∆|,|∆pt−1+(j+1)∆|
35:1056:66025:0:10:494:505:420:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f7:?:}2
35:1057:66027:10:40:508:511:410:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:.
35:1058:66028:40:18:91:519:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The intuition behind the MinRV estimator is similar to that for the original BPV
35:1059:66108:18:18:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimator.  When ∆ goes to zero, the probability of jumps arriving in two adjacent
35:1060:66190:18:18:91:519:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time-intervals of length ∆ goes to zero, so the minimum is unaffected by jumps.  The
35:1061:66274:18:18:91:519:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:main difference is that the jump is now fully neutralized,  even at a given discrete
35:1062:66358:18:18:91:519:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sampling  frequency,  in  the  sense  that  the  jump  size  has  no  direct  impact  on  the
35:1063:66451:18:18:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimator.  Hence the finite sample distortion of the MinRV estimator is significantly
35:1064:66537:18:18:91:519:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:less than that of BPV estimator.23By this same reasoning, a related jump-robust
35:1065:66616:18:18:91:519:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:MedRV estimator may be constructed from the properly scaled square of the median
35:1066:66696:18:18:91:519:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of three adjacent absolute returns cumulated across the trading day, see Andersen
35:1067:66777:18:18:91:217:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2010c) for details.
35:1068:66804:18:16:101:519:190:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:23This  is  true  as  long  as  there  are  no  adjacent  jumps  at  the  sampling  frequency  used.   Both
35:1069:66911:16:12:91:519:174:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:estimators  suffer  from  significant  upward  biases  if  adjacent  jumps  are  present.   This  has  led  to
35:1070:67021:12:12:91:519:162:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:additional  procedures  that  enhance  the  robustness  properties  even  further;  see  the  discussion  in
35:1071:67129:12:0:91:197:150:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Andersen et al. (2011b).
36:1072:67155:0:18:109:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another intuitively simple approach for estimatingIVt, first explored empirically
36:1073:67236:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by Mancini (2001), is to use truncation, the idea being that the largest price incre-
36:1074:67321:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ments are the ones associated with jumps.  Specifically, by only summing the squared
36:1075:67405:18:41:91:259:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:return below a certain threshold,
36:1076:67438:41:0:182:240:590:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:TVt(∆)   =
36:1077:67448:0:29:249:268:605:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:A:N(∆)∑
36:1078:67453:29:0:252:267:576:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:j=1
36:1079:67456:0:41:274:429:590:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:∆p2t−1+j∆I( ∆pt−1+j∆<T),
36:1080:67480:41:18:91:519:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  resulting  estimator  again  consistently  estimates  only  the  continuous  variation
36:1081:67571:18:18:91:520:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provided that the thresholdTconverges to zero at an appropriate rate as ∆ goes
36:1082:67649:18:18:91:519:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  zero.   Since  the  continuous  variation  changes  over  time,  and  in  turn  the  likely
36:1083:67744:18:18:91:519:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:magnitude of the corresponding continuous price increments, it is also important to
36:1084:67827:18:18:91:519:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allow the threshold to vary over time, both within and across days.  This choice of
36:1085:67910:18:18:91:519:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time-varying threshold can be somewhat delicate to implement in practice; see, e.g.,
36:1086:67994:18:18:91:393:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bollerslev and Todorov (2011b) and the discussion therein.
36:1087:68052:18:18:109:520:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Regardless of which of these differentIVtestimators is used, we obtain an empir-
36:1088:68132:18:18:91:519:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ically feasible decomposition of the total daily variation into the part associated with
36:1089:68220:18:17:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the “small”, or continuous, price moves, and the part associated with the “large,”
36:1090:68302:17:18:91:519:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and generally more difficult to hedge, price moves, or jumps.  Even if the risk man-
36:1091:68386:18:18:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ager is not interested in this separation per se, this decomposition can still be very
36:1092:68472:18:18:91:492:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:useful for the construction of improvedV aRs and other related risk measures.
36:1093:68549:18:18:109:520:316:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In particular, it is often the case that the variation associated with jumps tends
36:1094:68631:18:18:91:519:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be much more erratic and less predictable than the variation associated with the
36:1095:68714:18:18:91:519:280:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:continuous price component.  As such, the simple HAR-RV type forecasting models
36:1096:68793:18:18:91:519:262:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed  above  may  be  improved  by  allowing  for  different  dynamics  for  the  two
36:1097:68883:18:18:91:519:244:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:different sources of daily variation.  Such an approach was first pursued by Andersen
36:1098:68968:18:31:91:372:226:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2007a), who found that the HAR-RV-CJ model,
36:1099:69019:31:21:161:425:195:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:?:RVt=β0+β1IVt−1+β2IVt−5:t−1+β3IVt−21:t−1
36:1100:69058:21:0:199:450:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:?:+α1JVt−1+α2JVt−5:t−1+α3JVt−21:t−1+νt,
36:1101:69095:0:41:499:520:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(32)
36:1102:69099:41:0:91:519:144:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indeed produces even better RV forecasts than the HAR-RV model in equation (25),
37:1103:69181:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:which  implicitly  restricts  theαiandβicoefficients  in  equation  (32)  to  be  identi-
37:1104:69270:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cal.  Instead, by allowing for “αeffects” and “βeffects” in the HAR-RV-CJ model,
37:1105:69350:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we capture the fact that the variation associated with jumps is less persistent and
37:1106:69433:18:18:91:306:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:predictable than the continuous variation.
37:1107:69475:18:18:109:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Further refinements allowing for leverage effects and/or other asymmetries and
37:1108:69553:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-linearities could easily be incorporated into the same HAR-RV modeling frame-
37:1109:69634:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:work by including additional explanatory variables on the right-hand-side.  But the
37:1110:69717:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple-to-estimate HAR-RV-CJ model typically does a remarkably good job of ef-
37:1111:69795:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fectively  incorporating  the  empirically  most  relevant  dynamic  dependencies  of  the
37:1112:69885:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intraday  price  data  into  the  daily  and  longer-run  volatility  forecasts  of  practical
37:1113:69979:18:34:91:132:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest.
37:1114:69988:34:26:91:300:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.2.3  Combining GARCH and RV
37:1115:70017:26:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:So  far  we  have  presented  GARCH  and  RV  based  procedures  as  two  distinct  ap-
37:1116:70104:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proaches.  There are, however, good reasons to combine the two.  The ability of RV
37:1117:70186:18:18:91:519:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to rapidly deliver precise information regarding the current level of volatility along
37:1118:70272:18:18:91:519:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the ability of GARCH to appropriately smooth noisy volatility proxies make
37:1119:70351:18:18:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such a combination appealing.  Another advantage of combined models is the ability
37:1120:70433:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to integrate the RV process naturally within a complete characterization of the return
37:1121:70519:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution, thus allowing the RV dynamics to become a natural and direct deter-
37:1122:70600:18:17:91:520:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:minant of the time-variation in risk measures such asV aRand expected shortfall.
37:1123:70680:17:18:91:451:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The following section will elaborate on those features of the approach.
37:1124:70751:18:18:109:520:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The simplest way of cobining GARCH and RV is to include the RV measure as
37:1125:70824:18:33:91:516:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an additional explanatory variable on the right-hand-side of the GARCH equation,
37:1126:70904:33:33:200:520:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=ω+αr2w,t−1+β σ2t−1+γ RVt−1.(33)
37:1127:70939:33:18:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This is often referred to as a GARCH-X model.24Estimating this model typically re-
37:1128:71021:18:15:101:519:182:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:24Professor  Robert  F.  Engle  in  his  discussion  of  Andersen  et  al.  (2003a)  at  the  2000  Western
37:1129:71128:15:12:91:519:167:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Finance Association meeting in Sun Valley, Idaho, was among the first to empirically explore this
37:1130:71225:12:12:91:519:155:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:idea.  Related analysis appears in Engle (2002b).  Lu (2005) provides another early comprehensive
37:1131:71322:12:0:91:280:143:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:empirical study of GARCH-X type models.
38:1132:71363:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sults in a statistically insignificantα(ARCH) coefficient, so that the model effectively
38:1133:71451:18:18:91:143:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:reduces to
38:1134:71461:18:26:228:520:649:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=ω+β σ2t−1+γ RVt−1.(34)
38:1135:71487:26:18:91:519:623:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Intuitively, the high-frequency-based RV measure affords a superior estimate of the
38:1136:71570:18:18:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:true ex-post daily variation compared to the daily (de-meaned) squared returns, in
38:1137:71652:18:18:91:519:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turn driving out the latter as an explanatory variable for tomorrow’s volatility.  As
38:1138:71737:18:18:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:such, whenever high-frequency based RV measures are available, it is always a good
38:1139:71819:18:18:91:519:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:idea to use the GARCH-X model instead of the conventional GARCH(1,1) model
38:1140:71893:18:18:91:311:533:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:based solely on daily return observations.25
38:1141:71937:18:18:109:520:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The GARCH-X model defined by equations (7) and (33) or (34) directly provides
38:1142:72014:18:18:91:520:497:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one-day volatility forecasts.  The calculation of longer-run k-day forecastsσ2t+k|tne-
38:1143:72100:18:18:91:519:479:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cessitates a model for forecastingRVt+kas well.  This could be accomplished in an ad
38:1144:72184:18:18:91:519:461:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hoc fashion by simply augmenting the GARCH-X model with any one of the HAR-RV
38:1145:72261:18:18:91:519:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:type models discussed in the previous sections.  The so-called Realized GARCH class
38:1146:72344:18:17:91:519:425:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of models developed by Hansen et al. (2010a) provides a more systematic approach
38:1147:72424:17:18:91:206:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for doing exactly that.
38:1148:72447:18:18:109:520:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As an example, consider the specific Realized GARCH model defined by equation
38:1149:72524:18:33:91:129:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(7) and
38:1150:72531:33:21:221:520:339:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:σ2t=ω+β σ2t−1+γRVt−1,(35)
38:1151:72556:21:33:213:520:318:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:RVt=ωX+βXσ2t+τ(zt) +νt,(36)
38:1152:72583:33:18:91:520:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereνtdenotes a random error with the property thatEt(νt) = 0, and theτ(zt)
38:1153:72659:18:18:91:520:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function allows for a contemporaneous leverage effect via the return shockztin equa-
38:1154:72743:18:18:91:519:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion (7).26Substituting the equation forσ2tinto the equation forRVtshows that the
38:1155:72824:18:16:101:519:231:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:25In  a  related  context,  Visser  (2011)  has  recently  shown  how  the  accuracy  of  the  coefficient
38:1156:72930:16:12:91:519:215:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:estimates  in  conventional  daily  GARCH  models  may  be  improved  through  the  use  of  intraday
38:1157:73031:12:8:91:255:203:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:RV-based measures in the estimation.
38:1158:73067:8:16:101:519:195:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:26A closely related class of two-shock Realized GARCH models, in which the return volatility is a
38:1159:73164:16:11:91:519:179:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:weighted average of the GARCH and RV volatilities, has recently been proposed by Christoffersen
38:1160:73259:11:12:91:519:168:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:et  al.  (2011b).   Their  affine  formulation  has  the  advantage  that  option  valuation  can  be  done
38:1161:73366:12:12:91:519:156:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:via  Fourier  inversion  of  the  conditional  characteristic  function.   Non-affine  approaches  to  option
38:1162:73475:12:0:91:466:144:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:valuation using RV have also been pursued by Corsi et al. (2011) and Stentoft (2008).
39:1163:73562:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model implies an ARMA representation for the realized volatility, but other HAR-
39:1164:73642:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:RV type structures could, of course, be used instead.  Note also that unlike regular
39:1165:73726:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH, the Realized GARCH model has two separate innovations.  However, be-
39:1166:73801:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:causeRVtis observed, estimation of the model can still be done using bivariate max-
39:1167:73884:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imum  likelihood  estimation  techniques  that  closely  mirror  the  easily-implemented
39:1168:73972:18:18:91:342:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:procedures available for regular GARCH models.
39:1169:74018:18:18:109:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The Multiplicative Error Model (MEM) of Engle (2002b) and Engle and Gallo
39:1170:74091:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2006) constitutes another framework for combining different volatility proxies (e.g.,
39:1171:74177:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:daily absolute returns, daily high-low ranges, RVs, IVs, or option implied volatilities)
39:1172:74265:18:18:91:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into  the  estimation  of  a  coherent  multivariate  model  for  return  variances.27It  is
39:1173:74357:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:natural to use this same framework to extend the GARCH-X model to allow for the
39:1174:74436:18:18:91:321:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:construction of multi-day volatility forecasts.
39:1175:74483:18:18:109:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  particular,  building  on  the  MEM  structure,  Shephard  and  Sheppard  (2010)
39:1176:74567:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:propose an extension of the basic GARCH-X model in equation (33), in which the
39:1177:74645:17:18:91:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional mean of realized volatility,μRV,t≡Et−1(RVt), is defined recursively by
39:1178:74727:18:18:91:158:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the equation,
39:1179:74740:18:26:194:520:398:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:μRV,t=ωRV+αRVRVt−1+βRVμRV,t−1.(37)
39:1180:74774:26:18:91:519:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Shephard and Sheppard (2010) refer to this model as a High-frEquency bAsed Volatil-
39:1181:74857:18:18:91:519:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:itY model, or “HEAVY” model.  Like the Realized GARCH class of models, HEAVY
39:1182:74933:18:18:91:519:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models  have  the  advantage  that  they  adapt  to  new  information  and  market  con-
39:1183:75021:18:18:91:519:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ditions much more quickly than the regular daily GARCH models.  In contrast to
39:1184:75099:18:18:91:520:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the simple GARCH(1,1) model,  for which thek-period variance forecasts in equa-
39:1185:75178:18:18:91:519:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion (13) converge monotonically to their long-run run average values, the HEAVY
39:1186:75258:18:18:91:519:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model defined by equations (33) and (37) also might show momentum effects, so that
39:1187:75340:18:18:91:519:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the convergence of the multi-period variance forecasts to the long-run unconditional
39:1188:75424:18:18:91:519:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance is not necessarily monotonic.  This point is nicely illustrated by the volatil-
39:1189:75512:18:18:91:519:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ity forecasts during the recent financial crises reported in Shephard and Sheppard
39:1190:75594:18:18:91:519:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2010),  which  show  how  the  model  sometimes  predicts  rising  volatility  even  when
39:1191:75684:18:16:101:519:174:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:27This approach has also been used by Brownlees and Gallo (2011) to compare different volatility
39:1192:75780:16:0:91:287:158:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:measures and their uses in risk management.
40:1193:75825:0:18:91:430:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the current volatility is exceptionally high by historical standards.
40:1194:75894:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Risk managers, of course, typically care not only about the dynamics of volatility
40:1195:75976:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:but also more generally about the dynamics of the entire conditional distribution of
40:1196:76060:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio returns.  Movement in conditional variance is a key driver of movement in
40:1197:76143:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the conditional distribution, but only in the unlikely case of conditional normality is
40:1198:76230:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it the entire story.  Hence we next discuss how GARCH and realized variance may
40:1199:76309:18:39:91:390:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be used in broader modeling of entire return distributions.
40:1200:76368:39:26:91:348:538:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:2.3  Modeling Return Distributions
40:1201:76402:26:18:91:519:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We have emphasized – and continue to emphasize – the potentially seriously mislead-
40:1202:76485:18:18:91:519:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing nature of unconditional risk analyses.  Here we stress the similarly potentially
40:1203:76569:18:17:91:520:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:seriously misleading nature ofGaussianrisk analyses.  There are four cases to con-
40:1204:76651:17:18:91:519:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sider,  corresponding  to  the  reliance  on  unconditional/conditional  information  and
40:1205:76740:18:18:91:338:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the use of Gaussian/non-Gaussian distributions.
40:1206:76787:18:18:109:520:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Risk  measurement  in  an  unconditional  Gaussian  framework  would  be  doubly
40:1207:76867:18:18:91:519:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:defective, first because of the deficiencies of the unconditional perspective, and second
40:1208:76956:18:18:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:because financial returns are simply not unconditionally Gaussian, as has been well-
40:1209:77040:18:18:91:519:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:known at least since the classic contributions of Mandelbrot (1963) and Fama (1965).
40:1210:77124:18:18:91:519:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:For that reason, even crude approaches like historical HS-VaR, although maintaining
40:1211:77207:18:18:91:519:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an unconditional perspective, dispense with normality by building an approximation
40:1212:77289:18:18:91:439:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the unconditional distribution from historically-observed returns.
40:1213:77358:18:18:109:520:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Figure 8 serves to illustrate the strong unconditional non-normality in returns,
40:1214:77438:18:18:91:519:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as it displays a QQ plot for daily S&P500 returns from January 2, 1990 to December
40:1215:77520:18:18:91:519:261:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:31,  2010.   That  is,  it  plots  quantiles  of  the  standardized  returns  against  quantiles
40:1216:77616:18:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the standard normal distribution.  If the returns were unconditionally normally
40:1217:77698:18:17:91:519:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributed, the points would fall along the 45-degree line.  Clearly, the daily returns
40:1218:77786:17:18:91:240:208:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are not normally distributed.
40:1219:77815:18:18:109:520:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Now  consider  the  conditional  case.   Note  that  in  specifying  the  general  condi-
40:1220:77904:18:18:91:519:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional variance model (7) we made no assumptions as to the conditional distribution
40:1221:77987:18:0:91:519:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of returns.  That is, we made no assumptions as to the distribution of returns stan-

41:1236:78541:18:18:91:520:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:example, wedidinvoke conditional normality.  At least four points are worth making.
41:1237:78624:18:18:109:520:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First,  conditional  normalitycanbe,  and  sometimes  is,  an  acceptable  assump-
41:1238:78706:18:18:91:519:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion.   Conditional  normality  does  not  imply  unconditional  normality,  and  indeed
41:1239:78794:18:18:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility dynamics “fatten” the tails of unconditional distributions relative to their
41:1240:78881:18:18:91:519:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional  counterparts,  so  that  conditionally-Gaussian  models  sometimes  match
41:1241:78967:18:18:91:519:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the unconditional fat tails present in the data.  Put differently, distributions of re-
41:1242:79054:18:18:91:519:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:turns standardized by their conditional volatilities can be approximately Gaussian,
41:1243:79137:18:17:91:381:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:even if returns are clearly unconditionally non-Gaussian.
41:1244:79194:17:18:109:520:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, conditional normality is notnecessarilyan acceptable assumption. Some-
41:1245:79272:18:18:91:520:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:times, for example, the unconditional distribution of returns might besofat-tailed
41:1246:79354:18:18:91:519:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the volatility model cannot fatten conditionally-Gaussian tails enough to match
41:1247:79438:18:0:91:309:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the unconditional distribution successfully.
42:1248:79484:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Third, beyond fat unconditional tails, there may beotherunconditional distribu-
42:1249:79563:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional features, such as skewness, that couldneverbe captured under any symmetric
42:1250:79644:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional  density  assumption  such  as  Gaussian,  independent  of  the  conditional
42:1251:79732:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance model used.  Matching the unconditional density in general requires flexible
42:1252:79817:18:18:91:393:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional varianceandconditional density specifications.
42:1253:79875:18:18:109:520:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Fourth,  our  goal  in  flexibly  specifying  the  conditional  density  is  not  merely  to
42:1254:79967:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replicate the unconditional density successfully.  Rather, for risk measurement and
42:1255:80050:18:18:91:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:management  purposes  the  conditional  density  isthe objectof  direct  and  intrinsic
42:1256:80137:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interest.   That  is,  best-practice  risk  measurement  and  management  often  requires
42:1257:80226:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an  estimate  of  the  entire  conditional  distribution  of  returns,  not  just  insufficient
42:1258:80321:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:statistics  like  its  conditional  variance,  conditional  VaR,  or  conditionally  expected
42:1259:80414:18:18:91:473:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shortfall.  Hence we need a flexibile specification of the conditional density.
42:1260:80493:18:18:109:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Empirical analyses typically find that, although standardization by GARCH and
42:1261:80570:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:related volatilities promotes normality, the standardized returns remain non-normal.
42:1262:80654:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The nature of the non-normality of standardized returns, moreover, varies system-
42:1263:80735:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:atically across asset classes.  For example, standardized returns from mature foreign
42:1264:80820:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exchange markets are typically symmetric but leptokurtic, while standardized returns
42:1265:80904:18:18:91:343:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on aggregate equity indexes are typically skewed.
42:1266:80953:18:18:109:520:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To illustrate we show in Figure 9 a Gaussian QQ plot for S&P500 returns stan-
42:1267:81030:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dardized by the time-varying volatilities from the asymmetric NGARCH(1,1) model
42:1268:81109:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:previously used in calculating the VaRs in Figure 3.  The QQ plot reveals that the
42:1269:81191:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:NGARCH-standardized returns conform more closely to normality than do the raw
42:1270:81268:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns of Figure 8.  It also reveals, however, that the left tail of the return distri-
42:1271:81356:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bution remains far from Gaussian.  In particular, there are too many large negative
42:1272:81439:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns relative to what one would expect if the standardized returns were Gaussian.
42:1273:81523:18:18:109:520:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As theV aRitself refers to a specific quantile, this QQ plot in effect provides an

44:1332:84399:18:18:91:520:288:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:AvgRV1/2t.  Putting things into perspective, the conditional non-normality of daily
44:1333:84482:18:18:91:519:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns has long been seen as a key stylized fact in market risk management; see, e.g.,

44:1336:84737:18:17:91:519:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Of course, the realized volatility used in the standardization in Figure 10 is based
44:1337:84821:17:18:91:520:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on high-frequency data over thesamedaily time interval as the return,  while the
44:1338:84901:18:18:91:453:181:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH volatility used in Figure 9 is a true one-day-ahead prediction.
44:1339:84970:18:16:101:519:163:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:28Andersen et al. (2007c) explores the theoretical basis for this relationship and provides a detailed
44:1340:85072:16:0:91:344:147:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:examination of the empirical fit for daily S&P500 returns.
45:1341:85132:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Against  this  background  on  the  very  different  distributional  properties  of  un-
45:1342:85220:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:standardized, GARCH-standardized and RV-standardized returns, in this section we
45:1343:85300:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discuss how to use the different standardizations and resulting distributions to con-
45:1344:85385:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:struct accurate predictive return distributions.  An important part of that discussion,
45:1345:85472:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:particularly in the GARCH-standardized case, involves specification of empirically-
45:1346:85555:18:35:91:403:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realistic (i.e., non-Gaussian) conditional return distributions.
45:1347:85619:35:25:91:311:560:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.3.1  Procedures Based on GARCH
45:1348:85651:25:18:91:519:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The GARCH dynamic directly delivers one-day ahead volatility forecasts.  In order
45:1349:85732:18:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to complete the daily predictive return distribution, one simply needs to postulate a
45:1350:85817:18:18:91:520:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution for theztreturn shock in equation (7).  Although the normal assumption
45:1351:85900:18:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may work well in certain cases, as Figure 9 makes clear, it often underestimates large
45:1352:85986:18:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:downside risks.  As such, it is important to consider alternatives that allow for fat
45:1353:86071:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tails and/or asymmetries in the conditional distribution.  Specifically, in the case of
45:1354:86158:18:33:91:466:427:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:V aRwe are looking for ways to more accurately assess the cut-offκ−1pin
45:1355:86229:33:33:244:520:394:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:V aRpT+1|T≡σT+1κ−1p,(38)
45:1356:86253:33:17:91:520:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instead of simply relying on Φ−1pfrom the standard normal distribution.29Of course,
45:1357:86336:17:18:91:520:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:doing this for all values ofp∈[0,1] essentially amounts to mapping out the entire
45:1358:86417:18:18:91:250:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional return distribution.
45:1359:86449:18:18:109:520:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Perhaps the most obvious approach is to look for a parametric distribution that is
45:1360:86531:18:18:91:520:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more flexible than the normal.  One example is the (standardized) Student-tdistribu-
45:1361:86615:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion, which relies on only one additional degrees-of-freedom parameter in generating
45:1362:86699:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:symmetric fat tails.  Such an approach was first pursued by Bollerslev (1987), who
45:1363:86781:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:showed how the likelihood function for the normal-GARCH model in equation (9)
45:1364:86858:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  readily  extended  to  the  GARCH-t  case,  thus  allowing  for  the  estimation  of  the
45:1365:86951:18:18:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:degrees-of-freedom parameter (along with the other GARCH parameters) that best
45:1366:87029:18:16:101:519:182:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:29The 1996 amendment to the 1988 Basel Accord somewhat arbitrarily recommends the use of a
45:1367:87119:16:12:91:520:166:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:multiplicative factor of at least−3.0 in the construction of a 1%V aR, relative to the Φ−10.01=−2.33
45:1368:87219:12:0:91:484:154:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:implied by the standard normal distribution; see also the discussion in Chan et al. (2007).
46:1369:87312:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:describes the return distribution,  and in turn the requisiteκ−1pfor calculating the
46:1370:87396:18:18:91:206:667:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:V aRin equation (38).
46:1371:87417:18:18:109:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This approach works reasonably well when the conditional return distribution is
46:1372:87496:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:close to symmetric.  However, as illustrated by the QQ plots discussed above, equity
46:1373:87580:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolios are often severely left skewed.  The Generalized Error Distribution (GED),
46:1374:87665:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first employed in this context by Nelson (1991), explicitly allows for asymmetries, as
46:1375:87751:18:18:91:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do some of the different generalizations of the Student-tdistribution suggested by
46:1376:87833:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hansen (1994) and Fernandez and Steel (1998), among others.  Alternatively, follow-
46:1377:87916:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing Engle and Gonzalez-Rivera (1991) the whole density forztmay be approximated
46:1378:87995:18:18:91:331:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using more flexible semiparametric procedures.
46:1379:88041:18:18:109:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Rather  than  postulating  a  particular  parametric  density,  one  can  also  simply
46:1380:88127:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approximate the quantiles of non-normal distributions via Cornish-Fisher type ex-
46:1381:88208:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pansions.   This  approach  was  first  advocated  in  the  context  of  GARCH  modeling
46:1382:88296:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and forecasting by Baillie and Bollerslev (1992).  The only inputs needed for esti-
46:1383:88379:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matingκ−1pare  theunconditionalsample  skewness  and  kurtosis  statistics  for  the
46:1384:88463:18:18:91:208:416:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:standardized returns.30
46:1385:88486:18:18:109:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Meanwhile,  a  common  problem  with  most  GARCH  models,  regardless  of  the
46:1386:88565:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:innovation distribution, is that the specific distribution is not preserved under tem-
46:1387:88651:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:poral aggregation; see, e.g., the discussion in Drost and Nijman (1993) and Meddahi
46:1388:88734:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  Renault  (2004).   For  example,  even  if  the  standardized  daily  returns  from  a
46:1389:88825:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH(1,1) model were normal, the implied weekly returns would not be.  In turn,
46:1390:88905:18:18:91:520:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this implies that the term structure ofV aRs is not closed under temporal aggrega-
46:1391:88987:18:18:91:520:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion either.  Instead, the multi-periodV aRs need to be computed via Monte Carlo
46:1392:89067:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simulations or other numerical methods,  as exemplified by Guidolin and Timmer-
46:1393:89146:18:18:91:520:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mann  (2006).31This  also  means  that  the  Cornish-Fisher  and  related  approxima-
46:1394:89231:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions,  which  only  provide  partial  characterizations  of  the  underlying  daily  return
46:1395:89323:18:15:101:519:218:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:30More accurate approximations may in theory be obtained by including higher order uncondi-
46:1396:89414:15:12:91:519:203:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:tional sample moments in the Cornish-Fisher expansion, but this does not always produce satisfac-
46:1397:89511:12:8:91:143:191:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:tory results.
46:1398:89524:8:16:101:519:183:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:31The  affine  GARCH  models  suggested  by  Heston  and  Nandi  (2000)  and  Christoffersen  et  al.
46:1399:89625:16:12:91:519:167:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:(2006), when combined with the methods of Albanese et al. (2004), also allow for relatively easy-
46:1400:89722:12:0:91:472:155:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:to-compute term structures for VaR, but some numerical calculations are still required.
47:1401:89811:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution in  the  form of specific quantiles,  generally will  not suffice for  answer-
47:1402:89902:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing  questions  regarding  the  distribution  of  temporally  aggregated  returns.   Below,
47:1403:89993:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we discuss a viable approach that effectively combines a parametric volatility model
47:1404:90077:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with a data-driven conditional distribution.  First, however, we discuss how realized
47:1405:90162:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatilities, if available, may be used in the calculation of even more accurate predic-
47:1406:90250:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tive return distributions by effectively incorporating the intraday information into
47:1407:90334:18:35:91:231:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the distributional forecasts.
47:1408:90363:35:25:91:369:542:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.3.2  Procedures Based on Realized Volatility
47:1409:90409:25:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  basic  idea  underlying  the  construction  of  RV-based  predictive  return  distri-
47:1410:90499:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:butions is to treat the time series of RVs as stochastic.  Hence,  in contrast to the
47:1411:90584:18:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH-based procedures, which seek to describe the predictive distribution through
47:1412:90666:18:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:an appropriately specified univariate distribution for the standardized returns, the
47:1413:90750:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:RV-based procedures necessitate, at a minimum, a bivariate random distribution for
47:1414:90832:18:18:91:295:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the returnsandthe realized volatilities.
47:1415:90872:18:18:109:520:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This relatively new approach to risk measurement was first suggested by Ander-
47:1416:90950:18:18:91:519:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sen et al. (2003a).  The approach is directly motivated by the empirical regularities
47:1417:91035:18:18:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pertaining to the RV measures highlighted above.  First, as discussed in section 2.2,
47:1418:91120:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simple  time  series  models  for  the  realized  volatilities,  like  the  HAR-RV  specifica-
47:1419:91214:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion, generally result in more accurate volatility forecasts than do the conventional
47:1420:91299:18:17:91:519:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH models  based on daily  data only.32Second,  as shown in  section  2.3,  the
47:1421:91381:17:18:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributions  of  daily  returns  standardized  by  the  same-day  RVs  typically  appear
47:1422:91471:18:18:91:519:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:close to Gaussian.  Taken together, this suggests a mixture-of-distributions type ap-
47:1423:91556:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proach for characterizing the timeT+ 1 return distribution, in which the predictive
47:1424:91639:18:18:91:374:248:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:distribution forRVT+1serves as the mixture variable.33
47:1425:91693:18:20:109:519:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f8:A:Specifically,  assuming  that  the  standardized  return  is  normal,rT+1/RV1/2T+1∼
47:1426:91776:20:15:101:519:210:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:32This empirical regularity may also be justified through more formal theoretical arguments, as to
47:1427:91874:15:12:91:519:195:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:why the simple reduced form RV-based procedures often work better than structural model-based
47:1428:91967:12:9:91:505:183:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:approaches in practice; see, Andersen et al. (2004), Andersen et al. (2011a), and Sizova (2011).
47:1429:92063:9:15:101:519:174:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:33There is a long history, dating back to Clark (1973), of using mixture-of-distributions to describe
47:1430:92164:15:12:91:519:159:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the unconditional distribution of returns. What is fundamentally different in the RV-based approach
47:1431:92263:12:0:91:392:147:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:is to treat the mixing variable as directly observable and predictable.
48:1432:92336:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:N(0,1), and that the distribution of the timeT+ 1 realized volatility conditional on
48:1433:92420:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:timeTinformation is log-normal, the resulting normal log-normal mixture distribu-
48:1434:92501:18:39:91:357:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion for the timeT+ 1 returns may be expressed as
48:1435:92550:39:0:102:167:610:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:fT(rT+1)   =
48:1436:92562:0:17:193:199:618:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:1
48:1437:92563:17:0:175:217:601:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:A:2πσ2`,T+1
48:1438:92572:0:27:221:241:626:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f9:A:∫∞
48:1439:92574:27:0:227:231:599:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:A:0
48:1440:92575:0:0:244:292:610:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:y−3/2exp
48:1441:92583:0:20:294:304:630:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:{

48:1443:92585:0:17:314:336:618:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:?:r2T+1
48:1444:92590:17:0:319:331:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:2y

48:1450:92619:20:41:492:509:610:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:dy ,
48:1451:92623:41:18:91:520:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereμ`,T+1andσ2`,T+1denote, respectively, the timeTconditional mean and vari-
48:1452:92701:18:18:91:520:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance oflog(RVT+1).  For example, postulating a HAR-RV type model forlogRVwith
48:1453:92778:18:32:91:258:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:homoskedastic errors, we obtain,
48:1454:92810:32:33:131:480:501:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:μ`,T+1=β0+β1log(RVT) +β2log(RVT−4:T) +β2log(RVT−20:T),
48:1455:92864:33:18:91:250:468:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:andσ2`,T+1=σ2v, respectively.34
48:1456:92895:18:18:109:520:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The simple HAR-RV model for the conditional meanμ`,T+1could, of course, be
48:1457:92969:18:18:91:519:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:extended in several directions.  For instance, as noted above, when modeling large
48:1458:93051:18:18:91:519:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equity portfolios, asymmetries, or “leverage effcts,” are often statistically significant.
48:1459:93141:18:18:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Also, in their actual empirical implementation Andersen et al. (2003a) use a long-
48:1460:93223:18:18:91:519:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:memory  ARFIMA  model  forlogRVin  place  of  the  HAR-RV  formulation.   This
48:1461:93301:18:18:91:519:360:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:makes  little  difference  for  the  maximum  ten-days  forecast  horizons  considered  in
48:1462:93391:18:17:91:519:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:their analysis, but it could be important to do so in the calculation of longer run, say
48:1463:93479:17:18:91:520:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:quarterly (∼66 days ahead) or annual (∼252 days ahead), distributional forecasts.
48:1464:93560:18:18:109:519:307:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  mixture  distribution  described  above  treatsσ`,tas  constant.   However,  it
48:1465:93644:18:18:91:519:289:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is natural to think about the volatility-of-volatility as being time varying with its
48:1466:93729:18:18:91:519:271:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:own  GARCH  dynamics.   Such  an  approach  has  been  pursued  empirically  by  Ma-
48:1467:93813:18:18:91:519:253:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:heu  and  McCurdy  (2011),  who  report  that  allowing  for  temporal  variation  inσ`,t
48:1468:93902:18:18:91:519:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:does not actually result in materially different predictive return distributions.  Go-
48:1469:93988:18:18:91:519:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing  one  step  further,  Bollerslev  et  al.  (2009a)  develop  a  joint  conditional  density
48:1470:94083:18:18:91:519:199:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model  for  the  returns,  the  “smooth”  volatility,  and  the  variation  due  to  jumps
48:1471:94173:18:15:101:519:181:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:34Although it is not possible to express the density function in closed form, it is easy to calculate
48:1472:94274:15:12:91:519:166:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:numerically by repeated simulations from a normal distribution with a random variance drawn from
48:1473:94370:12:0:91:368:154:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:a log-normal distribution with the requisite mean and variance.
49:1474:94435:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:{rt,ln (BPVt),ln (RVt/BPVt)}.   In  that  model  the  predictive  distribution  for  the
49:1475:94523:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns is therefore obtained through a more complicated normal mixture involving
49:1476:94604:18:18:91:438:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two separate mixing variables, but the basic idea remains the same.
49:1477:94671:18:18:109:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This continues to be an active area of research, and it is too early to say which of
49:1478:94755:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the different approaches will be the “winner.” It is evident, however, that any of the
49:1479:94841:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively  simple  RV-based  procedures  described  above  almost  invariably  generate
49:1480:94929:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:more  accurate  predictive  return  distributions  than  the  traditional  GARCH-based
49:1481:95015:18:35:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributional forecast, especially over relatively short one-day to one-week horizons.
49:1482:95102:35:25:91:300:524:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.3.3  Combining GARCH and RV
49:1483:95131:25:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Just as the GARCH and RV concepts may be formally combined in the construction
49:1484:95209:18:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  volatility  forecasts,  they  may  be  similarly  combined  to  produce  distributional
49:1485:95300:18:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forecasts.  The procedures discussed in the previous section,  of course,  also utilize
49:1486:95387:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the realized volatility measures in the construction of the forecasts.  However, they
49:1487:95472:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:generally do not provide a direct link between the GARCH conditional varianceσt
49:1488:95551:18:18:91:276:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the realized volatility measures.
49:1489:95588:18:18:109:520:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Forsberg and Bollerslev (2002) provides a first attempt at doing that.  Their RV-
49:1490:95669:18:18:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH  style  model  is  based  on  the  assumption  that  RV  is  conditionally  Inverse
49:1491:95758:18:32:91:206:355:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:Gaussian distributed35
49:1492:95780:32:0:230:327:323:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:fT(RVT+1)∼IG
49:1493:95792:0:9:330:335:332:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:(
49:1494:95793:9:0:335:370:323:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:σ2T+1,η
49:1495:95800:0:9:371:376:332:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:)
49:1496:95801:9:33:378:381:323:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:,
49:1497:95802:33:33:91:483:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:together with a GARCH-style process for the conditional expectation of RV,
49:1498:95876:33:33:189:422:257:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:ET(RVT+1)   =σ2T+1=ω+αr2w,T+β σ2T.
49:1499:95910:33:18:91:519:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Further  assuming  that  the  RV-standardized  returns  are  normally  distributed,  re-
49:1500:95998:18:18:91:519:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sults in the predictive normal inverse Gaussian (NIG) distribution with conditional
49:1501:96081:18:16:101:519:188:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:35The  Inverse  Gaussian  distribution  closely  approximates  the  log-normal  distribution  for  the
49:1502:96183:16:0:91:289:172:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:realized volatility depicted in Figure 5 above.
50:1503:96232:0:35:91:164:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:varianceσT+1,
50:1504:96245:35:0:120:187:650:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:fT(rw,T+1) =
50:1505:96257:0:16:190:197:666:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:∫

50:1507:96293:0:9:440:445:659:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(
