50:1511:96303:35:18:91:519:615:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Closely related RV-GARCH type models have also been developed and used in the
50:1512:96380:18:18:91:519:597:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:context  of  option  pricing  by  Christoffersen  et  al.  (2011b),  Corsi  et  al.  (2011)  and
50:1513:96476:18:17:91:172:579:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stentoft (2008).
50:1514:96492:17:18:109:520:562:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The more recent Realized GARCH and HEAVY models discussed in section 2.2.3
50:1515:96566:18:18:91:519:544:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:takes this approach one step further by providing a coherent joint modeling frame-
50:1516:96648:18:18:91:520:526:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:work for{rt,σt,RVt}, where, importantly, the conditional variance of the returns,
50:1517:96729:18:18:91:519:508:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:σ2t, is not identical to the conditional expectation ofRVt.  These models directly de-
50:1518:96815:18:18:91:519:490:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:liver one-day volatility and return distribution forecasts.  In contrast to the GARCH-
50:1519:96901:18:18:91:519:472:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:X  style  models  and  some  of  the  RV-based  procedures  discussed  above,  multi-day
50:1520:96989:18:18:91:519:454:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributional  forecasts  may  also  readily  be  computed  using  numerical  simulation
50:1521:97078:18:18:91:148:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:techniques.
50:1522:97089:18:18:109:520:418:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:These and other related GARCH-RV forecasting approaches are still being ex-
50:1523:97164:18:18:91:519:400:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plored  in  the  literature.   Given  the  significant  improvements  afforded  by  incorpo-
50:1524:97256:18:18:91:519:382:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rating  the  intraday  information  into  the  GARCH  volatility  forecasts  through  the
50:1525:97345:18:18:91:519:364:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:RV measures, especially during rapidly changing market conditions, we expect these
50:1526:97427:18:34:91:485:346:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:procedures to play an increasingly important role as the field moves forward.
50:1527:97504:34:26:91:251:312:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.3.4  Simulation Methods
50:1528:97529:26:18:91:519:286:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In the discussion above,  we have often pointed to the use of numerical simulation
50:1529:97611:18:18:91:519:268:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:techniques as a way to calculate quantiles or distributions that are not available in
50:1530:97696:18:18:91:519:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:closed form. These techniques differ in terms of their underlying assumptions ranging
50:1531:97781:18:18:91:356:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from fully parametric to essentially non-parametric.
50:1532:97833:18:18:109:520:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Bootstrapping,  or  Filtered  Historical  Simulation  (FHS),  assumes  a  parametric
50:1533:97917:18:17:91:519:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model for the second moment dynamics, and then bootstraps from the standardized
50:1534:97996:17:0:91:519:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns to build up the required distribution.  At the portfolio level this is easy to
51:1535:98084:0:33:91:419:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:do.  First calculate the standardized pseudo portfolio returns as,
51:1536:98150:33:33:219:520:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆzw,t=rw,t/ˆσt,   t= 1,2,...,T ,(39)
51:1537:98186:33:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using  one  of  the  variance  models  discussed  above.   Then,  in  order  to  calculate  a
51:1538:98279:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one-day-aheadV aR, one simply use the order statistic for the standardized returns
51:1539:98361:18:33:91:356:583:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:combined with the volatility forecast to construct,36
51:1540:98414:33:32:203:407:550:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:FHS−V aRpT+1≡σT+1ˆzw((T+ 1)p).
51:1541:98444:32:18:91:519:518:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This same idea could also be used to numerically calculate theV aRfor parametric
51:1542:98524:18:18:91:519:500:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributions  where  the  quantiles  are  not  readily  available,  by  repeatedly  drawing
51:1543:98616:18:18:91:265:482:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:zw,tfrom the specific distribution.
51:1544:98651:18:18:109:520:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The construction of multi-dayV aRs is more time consuming, but conceptually
51:1545:98726:18:18:91:519:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:straightforward.  It requires simulating future paths from the volatility model using
51:1546:98811:18:18:91:519:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  standardized  returns  sampled  with  replacement  as  the  innovations.   This  ap-
51:1547:98900:18:18:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:proach  has  been  exploited  by  Diebold  et  al.  (1998b),  Hull  and  White  (1998)  and
51:1548:98991:18:18:91:519:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Barone-Adesi et al. (1998), among others, and we refer to these studies for further
51:1549:99074:18:18:91:342:374:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:details concerning its practical implementation.37
51:1550:99124:18:18:109:520:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The FHS methodology was originally developed in a GARCH setting.  However,
51:1551:99198:18:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for some of the RV-based procedures discussed above, one would naturally use RV
51:1552:99277:18:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or  its  expected  value  to  standardize  the  portfolio  returns.   In  these  situations  the
51:1553:99373:18:32:91:323:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:standardized returns should be sampled from
51:1554:99416:32:0:207:273:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:ˆzw,t=rw,t/
51:1555:99427:0:11:275:287:281:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:√
51:1556:99428:11:33:287:404:270:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:RVt,   t= 1,2,...,T .
51:1557:99449:33:18:91:101:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or
51:1558:99451:18:0:192:258:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:ˆzw,t=rw,t/
51:1559:99462:0:11:259:271:230:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:√
51:1560:99463:11:26:271:420:219:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Et−1[RVt],   t= 1,2,...,T .
51:1561:99490:26:18:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Of course, if the underlying model is based on a specific distributional assumption
51:1562:99573:18:15:101:519:175:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:36For the Expected Shortfall in equation (2) one would simply average over the draws that exceed
51:1563:99669:15:9:92:146:160:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ˆzw((T+ 1)p.
51:1564:99681:9:0:101:505:151:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:37Pritsker (2006) also provides additional evidence on the effectiveness of the FHS approach.
52:1565:99776:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:about the RV-standardized returns, that distribution should be used in lieu of the
52:1566:99858:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-parametric bootstrap.  Also, for RV-based GARCH models and related proce-
52:1567:99935:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dures, one might need to perform a bootstrap from the supposedlyi.i.d.bivariate
52:1568:100014:18:35:91:448:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:innovations for RV and returns.  But the basic idea remains the same.
52:1569:100083:35:26:91:266:596:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:2.3.5  Extreme Value Theory
52:1570:100110:26:18:91:519:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The different parametric and non-parametric procedures discussed above for charac-
52:1571:100192:18:17:91:519:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:terizing the conditional return distribution, including the simulation based bootstrap
52:1572:100278:17:18:91:520:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:procedures, are designed to work well for center of the distribution andV aRs with
52:1573:100360:18:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively  large  coverage  rates,  say  in  excess  of  5%.   In  many  situations,  however,
52:1574:100455:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one is primarily interested in the tails of the distributions and the risks associated
52:1575:100541:18:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with extremely large price changes.  Extreme Value Theory (EVT) provides a formal
52:1576:100622:18:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:statistical  framework  for  meaningfully  estimating  the  tails  based  on  extrapolating
52:1577:100713:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from the available observations.  McNeil et al. (2005) provides an excellent survey
52:1578:100796:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of these techniques and their application in quantitative risk management, and we
52:1579:100877:18:18:91:519:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:merely highlight some of the key ideas here; early important work in this area also
52:1580:100960:18:18:91:475:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:include Diebold et al. (1998b), Longin (2000) and McNeil and Frey (2000).
52:1581:101033:18:18:109:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Standard EVT is based on the assumption ofi.i.d.observations.  This may be a
52:1582:101109:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:good approximation for many applications in actuarial science, but financial returns
52:1583:101193:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  large  absolute  price  changes,  in  particular,  are  obviously  noti.i.d.through
52:1584:101281:18:17:91:519:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time.  However, in parallel to the FHS approach discussed immediately above, EVT
52:1585:101361:17:18:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may easily be combined with dynamic volatility models by applying the EVT-based
52:1586:101440:18:18:91:520:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approximations to the estimated return shocks ˆzw,t=rw,t/ˆσtrather than the returns
52:1587:101523:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:themselves.   Since  the  return  shocks  are  much  closer  to  beingi.i.d.than  are  the
52:1588:101613:18:18:91:519:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns, this makes the application of EVT much more reasonable.  Having estimated
52:1589:101695:18:18:91:519:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the tails for ˆzw,t, these are easily transformed to tails or extreme quatiles of the raw
52:1590:101784:18:18:91:226:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns by scaling with ˆσt.
52:1591:101812:18:18:109:520:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:EVT has the advantage that each tail of the distribution can be modeled sepa-
52:1592:101889:18:18:91:519:176:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rately.  But it has the limitation that it only describes the tails of the distribution
52:1593:101976:18:0:91:519:158:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and not the entire distribution.  It is therefore not possible to simulate data from an
53:1594:102065:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:EVT distribution unless further assumptions are made.  One way to proceed is to use
53:1595:102148:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:EVT in the tails combined with FHS for characterizing the center of the distribution.
53:1596:102233:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Assume for example that EVT captures well the 2% most extreme positive shocks
53:1597:102310:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  the  3%  most  extreme  negative  shocks.   Return  shocks  can  then  be  simulated
53:1598:102399:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by first drawing a trinomial variable that comes up{−1,0,+1}with probabilities
53:1599:102477:18:18:91:520:595:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f3:B:{.03,.95,.02}.   When  the  trinomial  comes  up  0  then  a  shock  is  drawn  randomly
53:1600:102565:18:18:91:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(with replacement) from the sample of ˆzw,twith the left 3% and right 2% extremes
53:1601:102646:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:removed.  When the trinomial comes up−1 then a shock is drawn from the left-tail
53:1602:102726:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:EVT distribution.  Similarly,  a draw is made from the right-tail EVT distribution
53:1603:102808:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:when the trinomial comes up +1.  This same idea may also be used in “stress testing”
53:1604:102892:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the portfolio, by increasing the probabilities assigned to the tails, in turn generating
53:1605:102980:18:18:91:493:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a disproportionate number of draws from the extreme part of the distribution.
53:1606:103057:18:18:109:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Portraying prices as evolving in continuous time, the extreme price increments are
53:1607:103139:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:naturally thought of as “jumps.” The discussion in section 2.2.2 above outlines several
53:1608:103226:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ways for disentangling the jumps on an ex-post basis with the help of high-frequency
53:1609:103310:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intraday data. Following the recent work of Bollerslev and Todorov (2011b), the high-
53:1610:103395:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequency filtered jumps may in turn be used in the estimation of the corresponding
53:1611:103478:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:jump  tail  distribution  and  the  probability  of  observing  an  extreme  price  change.
53:1612:103569:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Work long these lines is still in its infancy.  However, we conjecture that in parallel
53:1613:103656:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the gains in predictive accuracy afforded by the use of realized volatility measures
53:1614:103743:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relative to GARCH type models estimated with daily data only, similar gains may
53:1615:103822:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be available through the proper use of the high-frequency data for more accurately
53:1616:103904:18:45:91:453:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimating the jump tails and the extremes of the return distributions.
53:1617:103975:45:30:91:444:245:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:3  Conditional Asset-Level Risk Analysis
53:1618:104015:30:18:91:519:215:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Our discussion up until now has focused on dynamic volatility models for univariate
53:1619:104098:18:18:91:519:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns.   These  methods  are  well-suited  for  portfolio-level  risk  measures  such  as
53:1620:104189:18:18:91:520:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aggregateV aRandES.  However, they are less well-suited for providing input into
53:1621:104269:18:18:91:519:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  active  risk  management  process.   If,  for  example,  the  risk  manager  wants  to
53:1622:104360:18:0:91:520:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:know the sensitivity of the portfolioV aRto a simultaneous increase in stock market
54:1623:104445:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility and asset correlations, as typically occurs in times of market stress, then
54:1624:104531:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:a  multivariate  model  is  needed.   Active  risk  management,  such  as  portfolioV aR
54:1625:104619:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:minimization,  also  requires  a  multivariate  model  that  provides  a  forecast  for  the
54:1626:104711:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entire  covariance  matrix.38Bank-wideV aRis  also  made  up  of  many  desks  with
54:1627:104794:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multiple traders on each desk, and any sub-portfolio analysis is not possible with the
54:1628:104880:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aggregate  portfolio-based  approach.   Similarly,  multivariate  models  are  needed  for
54:1629:104970:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:calculating sensitivity risk measures and answering questions such as:  “If I add an
54:1630:105054:18:18:91:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:additional 1,000 shares of Apple to my portfolio, how much will myV aRincrease?”
54:1631:105134:18:18:109:520:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this section we therefore consider the specification of models for the fullN-
54:1632:105214:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:dimensional conditional distribution of asset returns.  To set out the notation, let Ωt
54:1633:105301:18:18:91:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:denote theN×Ncovariance matrix of theN×1 vector of asset returnsRt.  The
54:1634:105373:18:18:91:520:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariance matrix will have12N(N+ 1) distinct elements, but structure needs to be
54:1635:105454:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imposed to guarantee that the covariance matrix forecasts are positive definite (pd),
54:1636:105539:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or even positive semi-definite (psd).  A related, and equally important, practical issue
54:1637:105627:17:18:91:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:involves the estimation of the parameters governing the dynamics for the12N(N+ 1)
54:1638:105708:18:18:91:193:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individual elements.
54:1639:105728:18:18:109:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We  begin  with  a  brief  discussion  of  models  and  methods  based  on  daily  data.
54:1640:105816:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We then discuss how high-frequency data and realized variation measures may be
54:1641:105894:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:incorporated into the construction of better covariance matrix and multivariate dis-
54:1642:105978:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tributional forecasts. A notable aspect of our treatment is our inclusion and emphasis
54:1643:106064:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on methods that are applicable even whenNis (relatively) large.  This contrasts with
54:1644:106148:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:much of the extant literature, which focuses on relatively low-dimensional models.39
54:1645:106232:18:15:101:519:290:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:38Brandt et al. (2004) provide an alternative and intriguing approach for dimension reduction by
54:1646:106328:15:12:91:519:275:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:explicitly parameterizing the portfolio weights as a function of observable state variables, thereby
54:1647:106428:12:9:91:355:263:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:sidestepping the need to estimate the full covariance matrix.
54:1648:106489:9:15:101:519:254:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:39See  Bauwens  et  al.  (2006)  for  a  survey  of  multivariate  GARCH  models,  and  Chib  and  Asai
54:1649:106592:15:12:91:519:239:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:(2009) for a survey of multivariate stochastic volatility models, involving daily data and moderate
54:1650:106691:12:0:91:141:227:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:dimensions.
55:1651:106704:0:23:91:519:685:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:F:3.1  Modeling Time-Varying Covariances Using Daily Data
55:1652:106759:23:25:128:220:662:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:and GARCH
55:1653:106768:25:18:91:519:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The natural multivariate generalization of the RM variance dynamics in equation (4)
55:1654:106851:18:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provides  a  particularly  simple  approach  to  modeling  large  dimensional  covariance
55:1655:106940:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrices.   It  assumes  that  the  dynamics  of  all  the  variances  and  covariances  are
55:1656:107032:18:33:91:285:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:driven by a single scalar parameterλ,
55:1657:107069:33:33:218:520:550:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ωt=λΩt−1+ (1−λ)Rt−1R′t−1.(40)
55:1658:107098:33:18:91:520:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In parallel to the univariate case, the recursion may be initialized by setting Ω0equal
55:1659:107185:18:18:91:299:499:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:to the sample average coverage matrix.40
55:1660:107225:18:17:109:520:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The simple structure of equation (40) guarantees that the estimated covariance
55:1661:107303:17:18:91:520:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrices are psd, and even pd if the initial covariance matrix, Ω0, is pd, as the sum
55:1662:107388:18:18:91:519:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a psd and pd matrices is itself pd.  Letting Ω0equal the sample coverage matrix, it
55:1663:107474:18:18:91:520:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will be pd as long as the sample sizeTexceeds the number of assetsNand none of
55:1664:107552:18:18:91:519:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the assets are trivial linear combinations of others, thus rendering the RM covariance
55:1665:107638:18:18:91:232:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix forecasts pd as well.
55:1666:107666:18:18:109:520:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:At the same time, however, the RM approach is clearly very restrictive, imposing
55:1667:107746:18:18:91:519:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the same degree of smoothness on all elements of the covariance matrix.  Moreover,
55:1668:107828:18:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariance matrix forecasts generated by the multivariate RM approach inherit the
55:1669:107909:18:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implausible scaling properties of the univariate RM forecasts in section 2.1, and will
55:1670:107995:18:18:91:482:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in general be suboptimal for the reasons discussed in the univariate context.
55:1671:108072:18:18:109:520:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This, in turn, motivates a direct extension of the univariate GARCH approach
55:1672:108148:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to a multivariate setting.  In particular, extending the expression in equation (6) to
55:1673:108234:18:18:91:519:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  vector  setting,  the  generic  representation  for  a  multivariate  return  process  with
55:1674:108328:18:32:91:431:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time-varying conditional first- and second-order moments becomes
55:1675:108392:32:19:139:520:198:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Rt=Mt+ Ω1/2tZtZt∼i.i.d.,  E(Zt) = 0,  V ar(Zt) =I,(41)
55:1676:108446:19:15:101:519:179:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:40As previously noted, empirically more realistic dependence structures have also been explored
55:1677:108541:15:12:91:519:164:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:by RM, but following standard convention, we will continue to refer to exponential smoothing as
55:1678:108636:12:0:91:170:152:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the RM approach.
56:1679:108654:0:18:91:520:684:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereIdenotes  the  identity  matrix,  and  theN×Nmatrix  Ω1/2tis  one  of  the
56:1680:108733:18:17:91:519:666:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“square-root”  representations,  e.g.,  the  Cholesky  decomposition,  of  the  covariance
56:1681:108823:17:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix Ωt.  We refer to any specification in which Ωtis a non-trivial function of the
56:1682:108908:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:timet−1 information set as a multivariate GARCH model.  As with the univariate
56:1683:108986:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models discussed above, we will assume for simplicity that the daily means are all
56:1684:109068:18:18:91:181:595:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:zero, orMt= 0.41
56:1685:109084:18:18:109:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  most  obvious  extension  of  the  popular  univariate  GARCH(1,1)  model  in
56:1686:109166:18:33:91:258:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equation (8) then takes the form
56:1687:109198:33:33:148:520:526:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:vech(Ωt)  =vech(C) +B vech(Ωt−1) +Avech(Rt−1R′t−1),(42)
56:1688:109253:33:18:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the vech, or “vector-half,”operator converts the unique upper triangular ele-
56:1689:109336:18:18:91:519:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:ments of a symmetric matrix into a12N(N+ 1)×1 column vector, and theAandB
56:1690:109409:18:17:91:519:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrices are both of dimension12N(N+ 1)×12N(N+ 1).  In parallel to the expression
56:1691:109490:17:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the univariate model in equation (10), the long-run forecasts from the multivariate
56:1692:109577:18:18:91:520:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH(1,1) model in equation (42) converges tovech(Ω) = (I−A−B)−1vech(C),
56:1693:109650:18:18:91:520:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provided  the  eigenvalues  ofA+Bare  all  less  than  unity  and  the  inverse  of  the
56:1694:109738:18:18:91:520:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(I −A−B)−1vech(C) matrix exists.  This model-implied unconditional covariance
56:1695:109815:18:18:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix can be quite sensitive to small perturbations inAandB.  As such, it is often
56:1696:109898:18:18:91:520:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:desirable  to  restrict  the  matrixCto  ensure  that  the  long-run  forecasts  from  the
56:1697:109988:18:18:91:377:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model are well behaved and converge to sensible values.
56:1698:110043:18:18:109:520:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:“Variance  targeting”provides  a  powerful  tool  for  doing  that,  in  effect  “disci-
56:1699:110131:18:18:91:519:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:plining”multivariate volatility models.  This idea was first suggested by Engle and
56:1700:110214:18:18:91:524:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Mezrich (1996), who proposed replacing theCmatrix in the multivariate GARCH(1,1)
56:1701:110294:18:37:91:182:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model above with
56:1702:110310:37:0:185:353:223:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:vech(C)   =   (I−A−B)vech(
56:1703:110336:0:16:357:363:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:1
56:1704:110337:16:0:355:362:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:T
56:1705:110338:0:29:375:386:238:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:T∑
56:1706:110340:29:0:371:385:209:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:t=1
56:1707:110343:0:31:388:425:223:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:RtR′t).
56:1708:110350:31:15:101:519:192:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:41This  assumption  is  quite  innocuous,  and  does  not  materially  affect  the  inference  over  daily
56:1709:110456:15:12:91:520:177:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:horizons.  For models defined over longer return horizons,  simply replaceRtwith the demeaned
56:1710:110549:12:0:91:299:165:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:returnsRt−Mtin all of the expressions below.
57:1711:110595:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This in turn ensures that the covariance matrix forecasts converge to their uncon-
57:1712:110677:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ditional  sample  analogue.   Of  course,  if  the  risk  manager  has  other  information
57:1713:110767:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pertaining to some of the elements in the covariance matrix, this may be used in a
57:1714:110849:18:18:91:343:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similar manner in fixing the relevant values inC.
57:1715:110898:18:18:109:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Variance targeting also helps in the implementation of multivariate volatility mod-
57:1716:110981:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:els more generally, by reducing the number of parameters to be estimated.  The most
57:1717:111064:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:general version of the multivariate GARCH(1,1) model in equation (42), for example,
57:1718:111147:18:18:91:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hasO(N4) parameters.  More precisely, there areN4/2 +N3+N2+N/2 parameters;
57:1719:111221:18:18:91:520:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:hence, for example, forN= 100 there are 51,010,050 parameters!  Estimating this
57:1720:111300:18:18:91:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:many free parameters is obviously infeasible.42The “diagonal GARCH” parameteri-
57:1721:111379:18:18:91:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zation, originally proposed by Bollerslev et al. (1988), helps by restricting theAand
57:1722:111464:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:Bmatrices to be diagonal.  The number of parameters is stillO(N2), however, and
57:1723:111543:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:full-fledged  estimation  of  the  diagonal  model  is  generally  deemed  computationally
57:1724:111633:18:17:91:331:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:infeasible for systems much larger thanN= 5.
57:1725:111677:17:18:109:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Going  one  step  farther,  we  obtain  the  most  draconian  version  of  the  diagonal
57:1726:111765:18:33:91:449:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH(1,1) model by restricting theAandBmatrices to be scalar,
57:1727:111827:33:33:213:520:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ωt=C+βΩt−1+α(Rt−1R′t−1).(43)
57:1728:111855:33:18:91:519:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This, of course, closely mirrors the RM approach discussed above, with the impor-
57:1729:111936:18:18:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tant  difference  that  the  long-run  covariance  matrix  forecasts  converge  to  the  non-
57:1730:112029:18:18:91:520:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:degenerate matrix Ω = (1−α−β)−1C(provided thatα+β <1).  Estimation of
57:1731:112098:18:18:91:519:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this model may again be further simplified through the use of covariance targeting,
57:1732:112181:18:39:91:225:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:replacing theCmatrix by
57:1733:112204:39:0:226:320:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:C=  (I−α−β)
57:1734:112215:0:17:324:330:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:1
57:1735:112216:17:0:323:330:230:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:T
57:1736:112217:0:29:342:353:254:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:T∑
57:1737:112219:29:0:338:352:225:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:t=1
57:1738:112222:0:41:356:384:239:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:RtR′t,
57:1739:112228:41:17:91:443:198:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:leaving only the two scalar parameters,αandβ, to be determined.43
57:1740:112293:17:16:101:519:181:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:42Without further restricting the structure of the model, there is also no guarantee that covariance
57:1741:112393:16:8:91:341:165:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:matrix forecasts produced by the model are actually psd.
57:1742:112449:8:0:101:520:157:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:43This  model  also  readily  ensures  that  Ωtand  the  corresponding  forecasts  are  psd,  as  long  as
58:1743:112557:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Even so, estimation can still be very cumbersome in large dimensions due to the
58:1744:112636:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:need to invert theN×Ncovariance matrix Ωtfor every day in the sample in order
58:1745:112713:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to evaluate the likelihood function, which, of course, must be done numerous times
58:1746:112795:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:during  a  numerical  optimization.   In  an  effort  to  circumvent  this  problem,  Engle
58:1747:112886:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2008) suggested replacing the regular likelihood function in the optimization
58:1748:112971:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the model by a Composite Likelihood (CL) based on summing the log-likelihoods
58:1749:113051:18:40:91:179:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of pairs of assets,
58:1750:113070:40:0:189:252:537:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:?:CL(α,β)  =
58:1751:113080:0:29:266:278:552:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:T∑
58:1752:113082:29:0:263:277:523:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:t=1
58:1753:113085:0:29:285:297:552:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:N∑
58:1754:113087:29:0:282:296:523:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:i=1
58:1755:113090:0:29:304:316:552:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:N∑
58:1756:113092:29:0:301:314:523:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:j>i
58:1757:113095:0:41:321:520:537:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:logf(α,β;Ri,t,Rj,t),(44)
58:1758:113119:41:18:91:520:496:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wherelogf(α,β;Ri,t,Rj,t) denotes the bivariate normal density for asset pairRi,tand
58:1759:113202:18:18:91:519:478:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rj,t.  Each pair of assets yields a valid (but inefficient) likelihood forαandβ, but by
58:1760:113289:18:18:91:519:460:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:summing over all pairs the resulting CL-estimator becomes “relatively efficient.”In
58:1761:113372:18:18:91:519:442:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contrast to the standard likelihood function, the CL approach requires the inversion
58:1762:113456:18:18:91:520:424:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of 2×2 matrices only, albeit a total ofN(N+ 1)/2 for each day in the sample, but
58:1763:113536:18:18:91:424:406:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that, of course, is easy to do even in high-dimensional situations.
58:1764:113603:18:18:109:520:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Still,  the  assumption  that  all  of  the  variances  and  covariances  have  the  same
58:1765:113692:18:18:91:520:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:speed of mean reversion, as dictated by theαandβscalar parameters, is obviously
58:1766:113771:18:18:91:519:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:very restrictive.  As such, more flexible procedures may be needed in describing the
58:1767:113855:18:17:91:520:334:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:temporal variation in Ωtin an empirically realistic fashion, especially when consider-
58:1768:113941:17:18:91:519:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing disperse types of assets or asset classes.  One approach that has proven especially
58:1769:114028:18:35:91:474:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:useful is to focus on modeling the correlations rather than the covariances.
58:1770:114104:35:26:91:376:264:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.1.1  Dynamic Conditional Correlation Models
58:1771:114149:26:18:91:519:238:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:A conditional covariance matrix may always be decomposed into a conditional corre-
58:1772:114231:18:18:91:519:220:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lation matrix pre- and post-multiplied by the diagonal matrix of conditional standard
58:1773:114316:18:17:91:146:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deviations,
58:1774:114327:17:23:264:520:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ωt=DtΓtDt.(45)
58:1775:114341:23:0:91:166:162:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f15:F:α >0 andβ >0.
59:1776:114356:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Motivated by this decomposition, Bollerslev (1990) first proposed treating the con-
59:1777:114439:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:ditional correlations as constant,  Γt= Γ,  so that the dynamic dependencies in Ωt
59:1778:114521:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are  driven  solely  by  the  temporal  variation  in  the  conditional  variances.   The  re-
59:1779:114615:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sulting Constant Conditional Correlation (CCC) GARCH model has the advantage
59:1780:114691:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that it is easy to estimate,  even in large dimensions,  in essence requiring only the
59:1781:114777:18:18:91:520:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimation  ofNunivariate  models.   Specifically,  for  each  of  the  individual  assets,
59:1782:114868:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one may first estimate an appropriate univariate GARCH model.  These models may
59:1783:114947:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:differ from asset to asset,  thus allowing for much richer,  possibly asymmetric and
59:1784:115031:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:long-memory  style,  dependencies  than  in  the  multivariate  diagonal  GARCH  mod-
59:1785:115116:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:els  discussed  above.   Then,  denoting  the  resulting  vector  of  standardized  returns
59:1786:115207:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by ˆet=RtˆD−1t, the conditional correlation matrix Γ is efficiently estimated by the
59:1787:115291:18:18:91:421:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample mean of the outer product of these standardized returns.
59:1788:115354:18:18:109:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although the CCC GARCH model is easy to estimate, and may work well over
59:1789:115426:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively short time-spans, the underlying assumption of constant conditional cor-
59:1790:115509:17:18:91:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relation is arguably too restrictive in many situations.44In response to this, Engle
59:1791:115593:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2002a) and Tse and Tsui (2002) independently suggested allowing for dynamically
59:1792:115673:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:varying conditional correlations within a GARCH framework.  Specifically, assuming
59:1793:115755:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  simple  scalar  diagonal  GARCH(1,1)  structure  for  the  correlations,  the  Dynamic
59:1794:115844:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Conditional  Correlation  (DCC)  GARCH  model,  first  proposed  by  Engle  (2002a),
59:1795:115928:18:33:91:198:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may be expressed as,
59:1796:115948:33:33:214:520:311:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Qt=C+β Qt−1+α(et−1e′t−1),(46)
59:1797:115977:33:18:91:520:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where as beforeet=RtD−1t, and the matrix of conditional correlations are defined
59:1798:116057:18:15:101:519:260:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:44The  literature  is  rife  with  examples  of  time-varying  correlations.   Cross-market  stock-bond
59:1799:116160:15:12:91:519:245:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:return  correlations,  for  instance,  are  often  found  to  be  close  to  zero  or  slightly  positive  during
59:1800:116273:12:12:91:519:233:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:bad economic times (recessions), but negative in good economic times (expansions); see, e.g., the
59:1801:116370:12:12:91:519:221:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:discussion  in  Andersen  et  al.  (2007b).   Numerous  studies,  including  Longin  and  Solnik  (1995),
59:1802:116475:12:12:91:519:209:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:have also demonstrated that the correlations among international equity markets change over time.
59:1803:116572:12:12:91:519:197:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Similarly, there is ample evidence from the recent financial crisis that default correlations can change
59:1804:116676:12:0:91:289:185:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:quite dramatically over short periods of time.
60:1805:116724:0:0:91:336:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:by the normalized elements ofQt,ρi,j,t=qi,j,t/
60:1806:116770:0:9:340:355:694:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f8:?:(√
60:1807:116772:9:0:355:404:685:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:?:qi,i,t√qj,j,t
60:1808:116785:0:9:404:409:694:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:)
60:1809:116786:9:33:410:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:, or in matrix format,
60:1810:116808:33:33:208:520:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Γt=diag{Qt}−1/2Qtdiag{Qt}−1/2.(47)
60:1811:116842:33:18:91:520:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This latter normalization ensures that all of the correlations fall between−1 and 1.
60:1812:116926:18:18:109:520:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  parallel  to  the  CCC  model,  estimation  of  the  DCC  model  may  proceed  in
60:1813:117011:18:18:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two steps, by first estimating univariate GARCH models for each of the assets.  In
60:1814:117093:18:18:91:519:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contrast to the CCC model, however, the second step estimation in the DCC model,
60:1815:117173:18:18:91:520:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:involving the dynamics of the Γtmatrix, requires the use of numerical optimization
60:1816:117255:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:techniques. To help facilitate this step, and at the same time ensure that the forecasts
60:1817:117343:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from the model are well-behaved, it is often desirable to rely on correlation targeting.
60:1818:117431:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The parametrization in equation (46) does not immediately lend itself to that, as the
60:1819:117516:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unconditional expectation ofQtdiffers from the unconditional expectation ofete′t.
60:1820:117597:18:33:91:486:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Instead, following Aielli (2006) and re-parameterizing the dynamics forQtas
60:1821:117672:33:0:181:367:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Qt=  (1−α−β)C∗+βQt−1+α
60:1822:117694:0:10:372:377:435:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(
60:1823:117695:10:0:377:416:425:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f7:?:e∗t−1e∗′t−1
60:1824:117706:0:10:417:422:435:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:)
60:1825:117707:10:33:426:520:425:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:,(48)
60:1826:117712:33:18:91:520:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wheree∗t=diag{Qt}1/2et, it follows thatE(Qt) =E(e∗te∗′t).  Correlation targeting
60:1827:117792:18:18:91:514:374:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:is therefore readily implemented by replacingC∗with the sample mean of thee∗te∗′t
60:1828:117873:18:18:91:519:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix,  or  some  other  hypothesized  value.   This  corrected  DCC  (cDCC)  model  is
60:1829:117961:18:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relatively easy to estimate in high dimensions when combined with the composite
60:1830:118040:18:18:91:263:320:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:likelihood idea discussed earlier.45
60:1831:118076:18:17:109:520:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another easy-to-implement DCC type model has recently been proposed by Engle
60:1832:118152:17:18:91:519:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Kelly (2008).  In this model, instead of assuming the same dynamic dependencies
60:1833:118235:18:18:91:519:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for all of the correlations, the time-varying correlations are assumed to be the same
60:1834:118320:18:18:91:519:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across all pairs of assets.  Hence the name dynamic equicorrelation, or DECO, model.
60:1835:118404:18:18:91:519:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The assumption of identical correlations, of course, is only applicable when modeling
60:1836:118489:18:18:91:520:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:similar types of assets, such as, e.g., a large cross-section of stock returns.46Following
60:1837:118579:18:16:101:519:195:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:45The original DCC model defined by (46) and (47),  and the cDCC version in (48),  also both
60:1838:118671:16:8:91:340:179:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:guarantee that Γtis psd, provided thatα >0 andβ >0.
60:1839:118722:8:15:101:519:171:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:46If this assumption is valid, imposing identical correlations will also generally enhance estimation
60:1840:118823:15:0:91:435:156:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:efficiency relative to a model that treats the pairwise correlations as unrelated.
61:1841:118907:0:33:91:482:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Engle and Kelly (2008), the DECO model may be conveniently expressed as
61:1842:118978:33:33:242:520:652:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Γt=  (1−ρt)I+ρtJ,(49)
61:1843:118999:33:18:91:518:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:whereIdenotes  theNdimensional  identity  matrix,  andJrefers  to  theN×N
61:1844:119072:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix  of  ones.   This  representation  for  Γthas  the  advantage  that  the  inverse  is
61:1845:119164:18:35:91:223:583:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:available in closed form,47
61:1846:119191:35:0:195:230:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Γ−1t=
61:1847:119196:0:17:255:261:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:1
61:1848:119197:17:0:239:278:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(1−ρt)
61:1849:119203:0:16:283:289:564:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:[
61:1850:119204:16:0:291:312:548:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:I −
61:1851:119207:0:17:349:358:556:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:?:ρt
61:1852:119209:17:0:319:388:539:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:A:1 + (N−1)ρt
61:1853:119220:0:0:392:400:548:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:A:J
61:1854:119221:0:16:404:410:564:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:]
61:1855:119222:16:36:412:415:548:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:,
61:1856:119223:36:18:91:519:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thus rendering the likelihood function easy to evaluate. Implementation of the DECO
61:1857:119306:18:18:91:519:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model, of course, still requires an assumption about the dynamic dependencies in the
61:1858:119390:18:32:91:515:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:common conditional correlation.  In particular, assuming a GARCH(1,1) structure,
61:1859:119470:32:33:233:378:444:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:ρt=ωρ+αρut+βρρt−1,
61:1860:119488:33:18:91:519:411:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the updating rule naturally given by the average conditional correlation of the
61:1861:119572:18:24:91:200:393:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:standardized returns,
61:1862:119593:24:0:232:258:369:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:ut=
61:1863:119596:0:0:267:273:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:2

61:1865:119599:12:0:289:303:375:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:i=1
61:1866:119602:0:12:307:327:387:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:?:∑N
61:1867:119604:12:16:320:369:375:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:j>iei,tej,t
61:1868:119615:16:0:289:298:359:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:N
61:1869:119616:0:13:304:323:368:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:?:∑N
61:1870:119618:13:0:316:339:355:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:A:i=1e
61:1871:119622:0:7:340:344:363:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:?:2

61:1873:119626:0:32:376:379:369:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:?:,

61:1875:119690:18:18:109:520:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To convey a feel for the importance of allowing for time-varying conditional cor-
61:1876:119771:18:18:91:519:301:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relation,  we plot in Figure 11 the estimated equicorrelations from a DECO model
