62:1893:120672:12:12:91:519:379:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:mated equicorrelations from a DECO model for the aggregate equity index returns for 16 different
62:1894:120768:12:47:91:282:367:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:developed markets from 1973 through 2009.
62:1895:120809:47:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DECO  modeling  approach  also  to  account  for  important  short-run  fluctuations  in
62:1896:120897:18:17:91:327:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the 1/2×16×15 = 120 pairwise correlations.
62:1897:120939:17:18:109:520:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The scalar DCC model defined by equations (46) and (47),  the modified DCC
62:1898:121013:18:18:91:519:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model in equation (48), and the DECO model in equation (11) are all extremely par-
62:1899:121095:18:18:91:520:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simonious and readily implemented forNlarge.  They do, however, impose severe
62:1900:121172:18:18:91:519:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restrictions on the correlations, and may thus be seen as overly simplistic in applica-
62:1901:121259:18:18:91:519:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions involving only a few assets.  More elaborate DCC models, including asymmetric
62:1902:121342:18:18:91:519:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formulations (e.g., Cappiello et al. (2006)) and regime switching type representations
62:1903:121428:18:18:91:519:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(e.g., Pelletier (2006)), have been proposed to allow for more nuanced modeling when
62:1904:121512:18:0:91:519:159:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:Nis small, sayN≤5.  We will not discuss these models here, but refer to the recent
63:1905:121596:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:book by Engle (2009a) for a comprehensive survey of DCC models.  Instead, we turn
63:1906:121677:18:35:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to an alternative way of disciplining the covariance matrix, namely factor structures.
63:1907:121763:35:26:91:335:632:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.1.2  Factor Structures and Base Assets
63:1908:121803:26:18:91:519:606:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Factor structures are,  of course,  ubiquitous in finance.  However,  we will keep our
63:1909:121889:18:18:91:519:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussion short and focussed on their explicit use in simplifying the modeling and
63:1910:121972:18:18:91:519:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forecasting of large dimensional dynamic daily covariance matrices, as required for
63:1911:122055:18:17:91:519:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk measurement and management purposes.  More detailed discussions of the use
63:1912:122134:17:18:91:520:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of traditional factor models in the construction ofV aRs and risk management more
63:1913:122215:18:18:91:424:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:generally are available in Jorion (2007) and Connor et al. (2010).
63:1914:122281:18:18:109:520:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Market risk management systems for portfolios of thousands of assets often work
63:1915:122360:18:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from a set of smaller, say 30, observed base assets believed to be the key drivers of
63:1916:122445:18:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the underlying risks.  The accuracy of the resulting risk management system, in turn,
63:1917:122530:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:depends on the distributional assumptions for the base assets and the mapping from
63:1918:122612:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the base assets to the full set of assets.  The specific choice of base assets depends
63:1919:122698:18:18:91:519:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:importantly on the portfolio at hand but may, for example, consist of equity market
63:1920:122781:18:18:91:519:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:indices, FX rates, benchmark interest rates, and so on, believed to capture the main
63:1921:122865:18:18:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sources  of  uncertainty.   These  base  assets  will  typically  also  be  among  the  most
63:1922:122957:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:liquid assets in the market.  Such an approach is, of course, easier to contemplate for
63:1923:123044:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a relatively specialized application with readily identifiable risk factors, such as a U.S.
63:1924:123135:18:17:91:519:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equity portfolio,  than a very large diversified entity, such as a major international
63:1925:123221:17:18:91:205:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bank or conglomerate.
63:1926:123242:18:18:109:520:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Specifically, letRF,tdenote theNF×1 vector of de-meaned returns on the base
63:1927:123317:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets, or systematic risk factors.  The distribution of the factors may then generally
63:1928:123404:18:33:91:173:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be expressed as,
63:1929:123420:33:33:121:520:215:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:RF,t=  Ω1/2F,tZF,t,   ZF,t∼i.i.d.,  E(ZF,t) = 0,  V ar(ZF,t) =I,(50)
63:1930:123488:33:18:91:519:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the notation corresponds directly to the one in equation (41) above for the
63:1931:123569:18:18:91:520:164:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:N×1 vector of returnsRt.  The number of base assets may be considerably higher
63:1932:123647:18:0:91:519:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:than usual for traditional factor models employed in finance, but the basic idea is to
64:1933:123735:0:18:91:414:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:keep their number much lower than the total number of assets.
64:1934:123796:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The mapping from theNFbase assets to the full set ofNassets typically consists
64:1935:123874:18:33:91:230:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of a linear factor structure,
64:1936:123903:33:33:235:520:616:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Rt=B0+B RF,t+νt,(51)
64:1937:123923:33:18:91:520:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereνtdenotes aN×1 vector of idiosyncratic risks,B0is anN×1 vector, and the
64:1938:123999:18:18:91:519:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:factor loadings are contained in theN×NFmatrixB.  The factor loadings may be
64:1939:124075:18:18:91:519:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obtained from regression, if sufficient historical data exists for the full cross-section
64:1940:124164:18:18:91:519:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  assets.   Alternatively,  one  may  exploit  the  implications  from  a  specific  pricing
64:1941:124258:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model, if such a model exists.  Sometimes, the loadings are also determined in more
64:1942:124341:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  an  ad  hoc  fashion,  by  matching  a  security  without  a  factor  loading  to  another
64:1943:124435:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:similar security with a well-defined loading.  Importantly, however, bothB0andB
64:1944:124514:18:18:91:234:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are assumed to be constant.
64:1945:124541:18:18:109:520:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Now, combining the distributional assumptions in (50) with the basic factor struc-
64:1946:124623:18:33:91:462:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ture in (51), the resulting covariance matrix forRtmay be expressed as,
64:1947:124694:33:33:242:520:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ωt=B′ΩF,tB+  Ων,t,(52)
64:1948:124716:33:18:91:520:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where Ων,tdenotes theN×Ncovariance matrix forνt.  Since Ωtand Ων,tare both of
64:1949:124793:18:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the same dimension, this expression does not directly translate into any simplification
64:1950:124880:18:18:91:520:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in the estimation of the covariance matrix for the full set ofNreturns.  However,
64:1951:124961:18:17:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assuming that the idiosyncratic risks are uncorrelated across assets and that their
64:1952:125044:17:33:91:383:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variances are constant, the expression for Ωtsimplifies to
64:1953:125102:33:33:244:520:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ωt=B′ΩF,tB+Dν,(53)
64:1954:125120:33:18:91:519:219:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:whereDν= Ων,tis a time-invariant diagonal matrix.  Moreover, the elements inDν
64:1955:125198:18:18:91:519:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are readily estimated from the variances of the residuals in the factor model (51).
64:1956:125281:18:18:91:519:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This, of course, still leaves ΩF,tto be determined.  But, by keepingNFmoderately
64:1957:125361:18:18:91:519:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:low,  ΩF,tis  much  easier  to  estimate  than  Ωt.   In  fact,  in  addition  to  any  of  the
64:1958:125456:18:0:91:519:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:techniques discussed in this section, some of the more advanced multivariate GARCH
65:1959:125540:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:procedures alluded to above could be applied for estimating ΩF,twhen the number
65:1960:125619:18:18:91:330:667:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:of base assets, orNF, is kept sufficiently low.49
65:1961:125668:18:18:109:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:A:Although convenient from a modeling perspective, the key assumption that Ων,t
65:1962:125745:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is diagonal and constant over time often appears at odds with the data.  Just as vari-
65:1963:125831:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ances (and covariances) of raw returns are clearly time-varying, so are the variances
65:1964:125916:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(and covariances) of idiosyncratic risks.  Related to this, the risk exposures of many
65:1965:126002:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets,  as  encapsulated  in  the  factor  loadings,  are  also  likely  to  change  over  time,
65:1966:126099:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rendering the key covariance matrix representation in equation (53) withBconstant
65:1967:126180:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a poor approximation over long time periods.  However, for applications exploiting
65:1968:126262:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high-frequency intraday data, it is often feasible to alleviate these drawbacks and, as
65:1969:126349:18:39:91:453:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we shall see below, factor structures are often invoked in such settings.
65:1970:126422:39:25:91:413:466:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.2  Intraday Data and Realized Covariances
65:1971:126465:25:18:91:519:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Thus far our discussion has focused on models tailored toward capturing the dynam-
65:1972:126547:18:18:91:519:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ics in daily covariances based on daily data.  As discussed in section 2.2, however, for
65:1973:126635:18:18:91:519:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:many assets intraday price data are now readily available, and just as this informa-
65:1974:126719:18:18:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion is useful for the estimation of daily variances, it should be equally, if not more,
65:1975:126807:18:18:91:351:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:useful for the estimation of daily asset covariances.
65:1976:126860:18:18:109:520:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Generalizing the univariate setting in equation (20), and providing a continuous-
65:1977:126941:18:18:91:520:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time analogue to the discrete-time representation in (41), we assume that theN×1
65:1978:127021:18:33:91:506:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:log-price vector,P(t), is governed by the following multivariate diffusion process,
65:1979:127104:33:32:214:520:282:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:dP(t)  =M(t)dt+ Ω(t)1/2dW(t),(54)
65:1980:127137:32:18:91:518:250:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:whereM(t) and Ω(t)1/2denote theN×1 instantaneous drift vector and theN×N
65:1981:127209:18:18:91:520:232:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:positive definite “square-root” of the covariance matrix, respectively, whileW(t) de-
65:1982:127294:18:18:91:520:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:notes aN-dimensional vector of independent Brownian motions.  As before, without
65:1983:127374:18:19:91:519:196:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:much loss of generality, we assume thatM(t) = 0, although non-zero drifts, as rel-
65:1984:127456:19:15:101:519:177:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:49This basic idea was pioneered by Diebold and Nerlove (1989) in their construction of a multi-
65:1985:127551:15:12:91:519:162:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:variate ARCH factor model, in which the latent time-varying volatility factors may be viewed as
65:1986:127646:12:0:91:379:150:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the base assets; see also Engle et al. (1990) and Alexander (2001).
66:1987:127715:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evant  over  longer  return  horizons,  easily  can  be  incorporated  into  the  analysis  by
66:1988:127809:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:considering de-meaned returns.  We also assume that the asset returns are linearly
66:1989:127891:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:independent, i.e., no redundant asset is included in the basic set of returns, implying
66:1990:127978:18:18:91:293:631:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:that the covariance matrix Ω(t) is pd.50
66:1991:128018:18:18:109:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The natural multivariate extension of the realized variation measure, defined in
66:1992:128098:18:42:91:473:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equation (21), to the notion of a daily realized covariance matrix is simply
66:1993:128174:42:0:200:268:553:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f8:?:RCovt(∆)≡
66:1994:128183:0:30:278:297:569:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:N(∆)∑
66:1995:128188:30:0:281:296:539:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:j=1
66:1996:128191:0:41:303:520:553:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Rt−1+j∆,∆R′t−1+j∆,∆,(55)
66:1997:128215:41:18:91:520:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where,  as  before,N(∆)  =  1/∆.   If,  ideally,  the  price  vector  process  in  equation
66:1998:128306:18:18:91:519:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(54) is continuously observable, then letting ∆ go to zero enables us to compute the
66:1999:128390:18:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realized covariance matrix in equation (55) at ever finer sampling intervals.  In this
66:2000:128476:18:18:91:520:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:scenario, theRCovtestimator converges to the integrated covariance matrix of the
66:2001:128556:18:36:91:414:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:continuous-time stochastic volatility process on dayt, given as,
66:2002:128620:36:0:242:289:404:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:ICovt=
66:2003:128626:0:27:298:313:420:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:?:∫t
66:2004:128628:27:0:305:318:393:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:t−1
66:2005:128631:0:36:323:520:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ω (τ)dτ .(56)
66:2006:128644:36:18:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This expression, and the underlying limiting arguments, represent a direct extension
66:2007:128728:18:18:91:444:350:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:of the notion of the integrated variance forN= 1 in equation (22).51
66:2008:128796:18:18:109:520:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Hence,  as  for  the  univariate  case,  thetrueex-post  covariance  matrix  becomes
66:2009:128880:18:18:91:520:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:directly observable in this ideal setting, even in the absence of a model for Ω(t).  The
66:2010:128968:18:18:91:520:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:upshot is that, as before, variancesandcovariances no longer have to be extracted
66:2011:129049:18:18:91:519:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from a nonlinear model estimated via treacherous likelihood procedures, along the
66:2012:129130:18:18:91:519:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lines of the multivariate GARCH models discussed above.  Instead, by treating the
66:2013:129211:18:17:91:519:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realized covariance matrices as realizations of the true underlying series of interest,
66:2014:129298:17:18:91:507:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:we may apply standard time series techniques for their modeling and forecasting.
66:2015:129378:18:18:109:520:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Of  course,  the  idealized frictionless  setting motivating the  recipe forRCovtin
66:2016:129461:18:16:101:519:189:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:50As we discuss at length later, when the cross-section,N, is large, it can be difficult to generate
66:2017:129561:16:8:91:487:173:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:unbiased estimates of the realized covariance matrix that satisfy this important constraint.
66:2018:129653:8:16:101:519:165:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:51For more formal development of the associated asymptotic distribution theory, see, e.g., An-
66:2019:129747:16:0:91:382:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:dersen et al. (2003a) and Barndorff-Nielsen and Shephard (2004a).
67:2020:129814:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equation (55), and its limit in equation (56), provide only an approximate description
67:2021:129900:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of reality.  For instance, as discussed in section 2.2, trades are not consummated con-
67:2022:129987:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tinuously, imposing a strict upper bound on the highest possible sampling frequency.
67:2023:130071:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This presents important new implementation challenges compared to the univariate
67:2024:130151:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:case, especially if the number of assets is large and the trading intensities of some
67:2025:130236:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets are relatively low.  In particular, while some of the techniques discussed earlier
67:2026:130325:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may be adapted for consistently estimating the individual elements of the covariance
67:2027:130409:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix in the presence of market microstructure noise, none of these generally guar-
67:2028:130493:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:antee that the estimated covariance matrix is positive definite (pd), or even positive
67:2029:130579:18:18:91:189:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:semi-definite (psd).
67:2030:130599:18:18:109:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Along  these  lines,  Andersen  et  al.  (2003a)  first  noted  that  the  simple  realized
67:2031:130690:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariance matrix in (55) will be pd by construction, as long as the asset returns are
67:2032:130776:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:linearly independent and the trading (or quoting) activity is sufficiently high.  The
67:2033:130861:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specific requirement is that price updates are available for the full cross-section of
67:2034:130947:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:assets over small enough time increments, ∆, to ensure that the number of intraday
67:2035:131029:18:18:91:520:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observations,N(∆)  =  1/∆,  exceeds the number of assets,N.  For example,  if we
67:2036:131109:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sample individual U.S. stocks every five minutes across the official trading day, the
67:2037:131194:18:18:91:447:380:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:RCovtmatrix is trivially singular if the number of stocks exceeds 78.
67:2038:131263:18:18:109:520:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For a set of very actively traded securities, the above conditions may not appear
67:2039:131344:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unduly restrictive.  After all, many assets trade multiple times each minute on aver-
67:2040:131429:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:age, often generating thousands of new trade prices per day.  Unfortunately, this is
67:2041:131513:18:18:91:520:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deceptive.  The key point is thatallassets must have traded within each sampling
67:2042:131593:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interval.  If not, this will generally result in a downward bias in the covariance esti-
67:2043:131681:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mates due to the presence of zero returns induced purely by the absence of trades
67:2044:131762:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(or quote changes) – a feature commonly labeled the Epps effect following the early
67:2045:131845:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:characterization in Epps (1979).  Since many assets periodically experience a trading
67:2046:131930:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lull,  there  will  often  be  extended  periods  of  no-trading  for  some  of  the  assets,  so
67:2047:132027:18:17:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that this can be a major concern.  Hence, when using the basic realized covariance
67:2048:132109:17:18:91:519:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix estimator in equation (55), it is critical to sample fairly sparsely to alleviate
67:2049:132197:18:18:91:520:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this bias.52Of course,  this then restricts the size of the cross-section that can be
67:2050:132282:18:0:101:519:147:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:52It  is  generally  also  advantageous  to  follow  the  subsampling  strategy  previously  outlined  in
68:2051:132389:0:18:91:235:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:analyzed quite dramatically.
68:2052:132417:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:More  generally,  the  price  synchronicity  requirement  implies  that  the  realized
68:2053:132503:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariance  matrix  cannot  be  estimated  consistently  unless  the  sampling  scheme  is
68:2054:132593:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adapted to the trading intensity of the least active asset at any given time.  This idea
68:2055:132681:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is encapsulated in the “refresh time” sampling procedure advocated by Barndorff-
68:2056:132761:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Nielsen et al. (2011) as part of their multivariate realized kernel approach to covari-
68:2057:132848:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance  matrix  estimation.   The  kernel  consists  of  the  inclusion  of  a  suitably  chosen
68:2058:132942:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weight function for the lead and lag returns in the computation of the covariance
68:2059:133023:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix.  This ensures consistency in the presence of general classes of microstructure
68:2060:133109:18:18:91:500:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:noise, while also guaranteeing that the estimate of the covariance matrix is psd.
68:2061:133190:18:18:109:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Direct application of this approach is eminently feasible for a limited number of
68:2062:133271:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:actively  traded  assets.   However,  when  the  number  of  assets  is  large,  refresh  time
68:2063:133365:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sampling results in a dramatic loss of data as intermediary prices for active assets
68:2064:133449:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are discarded until the last asset trades.  For example, Hautsch et al. (2011) assess
68:2065:133534:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that, with realistic intra-stock differences in trade arrival rates, more than 90% of
68:2066:133619:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the data are discarded for a system of twenty actively traded assets,  and the pro-
68:2067:133702:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portion continues to rise as the cross-section of assets increases.  This implies that,
68:2068:133789:18:18:91:520:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forNrising, the effective sampling frequency, 1/∆, drops quite dramatically, in turn
68:2069:133873:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rendering it difficult to satisfy the positive definiteness bound.  Equally problematic
68:2070:133960:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is the loss in estimation precision as each pairwise covariance term is computed from
68:2071:134045:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fewer and fewer intraday observations, ultimately producing a poorly estimated over-
68:2072:134129:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all covariance matrix with many zeros among the eigenvalues.  In sum, this strategy
68:2073:134212:18:18:91:306:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fails for very large cross-sections of assets.
68:2074:134258:18:18:109:520:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Two main approaches have hitherto been proposed in the literature to accom-
68:2075:134333:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modate large cross-sections, while avoiding dramatic Epps style biases.  One avenue
68:2076:134416:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is to initially ignore the requirement of positive definiteness and apply the refresh
68:2077:134501:18:21:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sampling scheme on smaller blocks of assets, thus mitigating the problems associated
68:2078:134585:21:12:91:519:197:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:section 2.2, where one generates multiple subsamples of the intraday return series by initiating the
68:2079:134685:12:12:91:519:185:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:sampling at the given frequency at different offsets relative to the opening trade, and then average
68:2080:134785:12:12:91:519:173:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the resulting covariance measures across the subsamples.  For example, by initiating sampling at
68:2081:134881:12:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:each of the first five-minute marks during the trading day, one could secure five distinct five-minute
68:2082:134983:12:0:91:210:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:return series for each asset.
69:2083:135014:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the loss of data,  and then to apply a regularization procedure to restore the
69:2084:135097:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:psd property.  The second approach is to exploit covariance matrix factor structure
69:2085:135180:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to reduce the effective dimension of the problem, thereby allowing for more reliable
69:2086:135264:18:35:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimates from a given set of intraday observations.  We now discuss these techniques.
69:2087:135350:35:26:91:402:596:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.2.1  Regularizing Techniques for RCov Estimation
69:2088:135400:26:18:91:520:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The simplest method for converting a “vast”N×Npositive semi-definite covariance
69:2089:135479:18:17:91:520:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix estimatorRCovt(∆) of less than full rank and possibly containing multiple
69:2090:135559:17:18:91:519:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zero  eigenvalues,  into  a  strictly  positive  definite  matrix  is  shrinkage.   The  idea  is
69:2091:135656:18:18:91:520:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to combineRCovt(∆) with anN×Nshrinkage target matrix, Υt, which is posi-
69:2092:135728:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tive definite and well-conditioned.  Ideally, the target should also provide a sensible
69:2093:135815:18:30:91:455:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:benchmark covariance matrix to minimize the resulting bias.  Formally,
69:2094:135885:30:36:217:520:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩSt=κRCovt(∆)  +  (1−κ) Υt,(57)
69:2095:135917:36:18:91:520:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where the weight assigned to the realized covariance matrix satisfies 0< κ <1, so
69:2096:135998:18:18:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the shrinkage estimator is a convex linear combination of a positive semi-definite and
69:2097:136084:18:18:91:409:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a positive definite matrix, implying it will be positive definite.
69:2098:136150:18:17:109:520:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As an extraordinarily simple illustration of this basic principle, in a setting with
69:2099:136234:17:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:daily  data  and  time-varying  covariance  matrices,  Ledoit  and  Wolf  (2004)  propose
69:2100:136323:18:18:91:520:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shrinkage towards the identity matrix, i.e., Υt=I, with the weight,κ, determined
69:2101:136403:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:optimally according to an asymptotic quadratic loss function.  While this will reduce
69:2102:136488:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the variance, it may, of course, induce a rather severe bias, as asset returns generally
69:2103:136576:18:18:91:200:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are highly correlated.
69:2104:136598:18:18:109:520:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To counteract this bias,  Ledoit and Wolf (2003) suggest shrinkage towards the
69:2105:136676:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covariance structure implied by a simple one-factor market model.  Specifically, fol-
69:2106:136761:18:33:91:316:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lowing the discussion in section 3.1.2 above,
69:2107:136806:33:0:250:318:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:Υt=σ2Mbb
69:2108:136814:0:8:319:321:193:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:A:′
69:2109:136815:8:32:327:520:185:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:+Dν,(58)
69:2110:136823:32:0:91:519:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereσ2Mrefers to the variance of the market return,bdenotes theN×1 vector of
70:2111:136902:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:factor loadings for each of the assets with respect to the market portfolio, andDνis a
70:2112:136988:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:diagonal matrix composed of the corresponding idiosyncratic variances.  Importantly,
70:2113:137072:18:18:91:498:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:all of these parameters are easy to estimate from simple time series regressions.
70:2114:137153:18:18:109:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In contrast to Υt=I, this procedure allows for non-trivial positive return cor-
70:2115:137232:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relation across assets, thus providing a more suitable shrinkage target for covariance
70:2116:137318:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimation.  However, it assumes that the relevant second order return moments are
70:2117:137400:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:time-invariant, so that a long time series of daily returns can be used for estimating
70:2118:137486:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:b, along with the other parameters.  This is counter to the spirit of high-frequency
70:2119:137570:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:return based estimation, where we seek to determine the time variation in the co-
70:2120:137651:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance matrix and,  as an implication,  the fluctuations in systematic market risk
70:2121:137735:18:18:91:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:exposures,  or  factor  loadings.53The  extreme  dichotomy  between  the  realized  co-
70:2122:137822:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variance matrix, estimated without bias but with poor precision, and the shrinkage
70:2123:137904:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:target, which may be strongly biased but is estimated with better precision, naturally
70:2124:137990:18:17:91:430:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggest alternative approaches that better balance the two effects.
70:2125:138057:17:18:109:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this regard, Hautsch et al. (2011) have recently suggested breaking the covari-
70:2126:138139:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance matrix into blocks according to the trading intensity of the underlying assets,
70:2127:138223:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thus minimizing the loss of data from refresh time sampling when using the multi-
70:2128:138304:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variate realized kernels to estimate the different blocks.  Of course,  simply piecing
70:2129:138390:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the covariance matrix together from separate blocks generally produces an indefinite
70:2130:138474:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix with negative as well as positive eigenvalues.  To circumvent this problem,
70:2131:138556:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Hautsch et al. (2011) adopt so-called eigenvalue cleaning to “regularize” the covari-
70:2132:138641:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance matrix in a second step, by separating the set of large and significant eigenvalues
70:2133:138729:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from those that are statistically insignificant and may have been generated by ran-
70:2134:138812:18:18:91:154:272:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:dom noise.54
70:2135:138824:18:18:109:520:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Specifically, denote the first stage realized kernel blocking estimator for the inte-
70:2136:138909:18:18:91:520:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:grated covariance matrix on daytbyˆΩt.  Eigenvalue cleaning then consists of the
70:2137:138989:18:15:101:519:218:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:53Again,  Ledoit  and  Wolf  (2003)  envision  their  estimator  to  be  applied  for  daily  data  but,  as
70:2138:139097:15:12:91:519:203:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:mentioned previously, there are recent attempts to adapt similar procedures to the high-frequency
70:2139:139194:12:8:91:123:191:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:setting.
70:2140:139202:8:16:101:519:183:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:54This approach is motivated by random matrix theory; see, e.g., Mehta (1990) for an introduc-
70:2141:139296:16:0:91:457:167:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:tion to the theory and Tola et al. (2008) for a recent application to portfolio choice.
71:2142:139385:0:30:91:414:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:following steps.  First, define the realized correlation matrix by,
71:2143:139452:30:36:257:520:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΓt=ˆD−1tˆΩtˆD−1t.(59)
71:2144:139474:36:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where, as for equation (45),ˆDt=diag(ˆΩt)1/2denotes the diagonal matrix of realized
71:2145:139557:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:standard  deviations.   Using  the  conventional  spectral  decomposition,  rewrite  the
71:2146:139645:18:15:91:201:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correlation matrix as,
71:2147:139667:15:29:264:520:568:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΓt=ˆPtˆΛtˆP′t,(60)
71:2148:139686:29:18:91:519:539:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereˆΛtis the diagonal matrix of eigenvalues,ˆλi,i= 1,...,N, sorted in descending
71:2149:139768:18:18:91:519:521:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:order so thatˆλ1≥ˆλ2...ˆλN−1≥ˆλN, andˆPtdenotes the orthonormal matrix of cor-
71:2150:139846:18:18:91:519:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding eigenvectors.  Now, lettingλindicate the appropriate (positive) threshold
71:2151:139930:18:17:91:520:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:for the significant eigenvalues, separate the first, say,keigenvalues which exceedλ
71:2152:140013:17:18:91:519:468:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into one group.  Next, equate all negative eigenvalues to zero and compute the aver-
71:2153:140097:18:0:91:154:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:age value,λ
71:2154:140108:0:10:154:160:457:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:B
71:2155:140109:10:15:154:519:447:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:t, of the positive and (modified) zero eigenvalues that are less thanλ.
71:2156:140180:15:18:91:519:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The regularized covariance matrix is then constructed from the “cleaned” matrix of
71:2157:140262:18:18:91:520:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eigenvaluesˆΛBt, with the originalkeigenvalues as the firstkdiagonal elements and
71:2158:140343:18:0:91:366:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:the remainingN−kdiagonal elements replaced byλ
71:2159:140389:0:10:366:372:403:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:B
71:2160:140390:10:27:366:506:393:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:?:t, according to the formula
71:2161:140417:27:36:244:520:366:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩRnBt=ˆDtˆPtˆΛBtˆP′tˆDt.(61)
71:2162:140446:36:18:109:520:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Pursuing a similar approach, but taking the decomposition of the covariance ma-
71:2163:140525:18:18:91:519:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trix to a logical extreme, Lunde et al. (2011) suggest estimating all covariance terms
71:2164:140611:18:17:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using only the corresponding bivariate realized kernel estimator.  This minimizes the
71:2165:140696:17:18:91:519:277:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:loss of information due to refresh time sampling, while permitting an optimal choice
71:2166:140780:18:18:91:519:259:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of kernel bandwidth for each pairwise return series.  The first stage estimator is then
71:2167:140867:18:18:91:519:241:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:obtained by assembling all the elements into a “composite realized kernel” covariance
71:2168:140952:18:18:91:519:223:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimator.  This heightens the quality of the estimate for each individual term, but it
71:2169:141039:18:18:91:519:205:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sacrifices the coherence of the overall matrix by not imposing the pd (or psd) prop-
71:2170:141123:18:18:91:519:187:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:erty beyond the bivariate systems.  Since the resulting composite covariance matrix
71:2171:141206:18:18:91:519:169:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:typically will be “far” from pd, it requires a more substantial transformation of the
71:2172:141291:18:0:91:519:151:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:entries in the covariance matrix to obtain a pd matrix than is the case for the RnB
72:2173:141376:0:18:91:507:685:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:estimator of Hautsch et al. (2011), which usually operates with only 3-5 blocks.55
72:2174:141458:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another closely related approach to the estimation ofRCov, inspired by the idea
72:2175:141537:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of dimension reduction through the imposition of a factor structure, has also been
72:2176:141619:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggested  by  Lunde  et  al.  (2011).   The  idea  is  to  let  the  correlation  structure  be
72:2177:141715:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determined only by the eigenvectors associated with the largest and most significant
72:2178:141799:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:eigenvalues.   Again,  the  significant  eigenvalues  are  identified  day-by-day  using  the
72:2179:141892:18:30:91:480:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“i.i.d.  noise threshold” prescribed by random matrix theory.56Formally, let
72:2180:141968:30:36:267:520:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A: ̃Γt= ̃Pt ̃Λt ̃P′t,(62)
72:2181:141991:36:18:91:520:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where ̃Λtdenotes thek×kdiagonal matrix containing the upper leftk×ksub-matrix
72:2182:142068:18:17:91:520:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ofˆΛt, while ̃Ptdenotes theN×kmatrix containing the firstkcolumns of eigenvectors
72:2183:142149:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fromˆPtassociated with the largestkeigenvalues.  The resultingN×Nmatrix, ̃Γt,
72:2184:142226:18:18:91:520:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is of rankkand thus not strictly positive definite.  It is also not a proper correlation
72:2185:142314:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix, as it generally fails to have unit entries along the diagonal.  Nonetheless, it
72:2186:142401:18:18:91:520:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:embodies  the  correlation  structure  implied  by  thekmost  important  eigenvectors,
72:2187:142487:18:18:91:519:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or the firstkprincipal components of the intraday returns.  Hence, it is natural to
72:2188:142570:18:30:91:408:386:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:modify this matrix to construct a proper correlation matrix,57
72:2189:142632:30:0:195:258:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A: ̃ΓPCt=I+
72:2190:142641:0:10:260:266:366:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:[
72:2191:142642:10:0:271:348:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A: ̃Pt ̃Λt ̃P′t−diag
72:2192:142660:0:10:350:357:366:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:(
72:2193:142661:10:0:360:394:356:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:?: ̃Pt ̃Λt ̃P′t
72:2194:142674:0:13:397:412:366:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:)]
72:2195:142676:13:33:414:520:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:.(63)
72:2196:142681:33:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The resulting principal component regularized realized covariance matrix estimator
72:2197:142763:18:29:91:311:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is then obtained by simply scaling up ̃ΓPCt,
72:2198:142807:29:22:255:520:273:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩPCt=ˆDt ̃ΓPCtˆDt.(64)
72:2199:142830:22:15:101:519:251:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:55The notion of a distance between covariance matrices requires the adoption of a matrix norm.
72:2200:142924:15:12:91:519:236:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Since our discussion is heuristic, we abstain from any detailed account; see, e.g., Fan et al. (2008)
72:2201:143025:12:9:91:457:224:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:for a discussion of alternative norms in the context of covariance matrix estimation.
72:2202:143110:9:15:101:519:215:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:56Alternatively, one may exploit an initial procedure to help decide on an appropriate fixed num-
72:2203:143207:15:12:91:519:200:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ber of eigenvectors, or “factors”, in order to maintain a constant dimensionality of the correlation
72:2204:143307:12:9:91:185:188:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:structure across days.
72:2205:143329:9:15:101:519:179:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:57Notice that for any square matrixA, the operationA−diag(A) leaves the off-diagonal entries
72:2206:143421:15:12:91:520:164:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:inAunchanged, while producing zeros along the diagonal.  Hence,I+ [A−diag(A)] yields a matrix
72:2207:143514:12:0:91:419:152:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:with unit entries on the diagonal and off-diagonal entries inherited fromA.
73:2208:143591:0:18:91:191:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as in equation (61).
73:2209:143611:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It remains a matter for future work to systematically characterize the performance
73:2210:143693:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  these  approaches  toRCovtestimation  based  on  the  spectral  decomposition  in
73:2211:143778:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:equation (60) for empirically realistic situations involving different scenarios for the
73:2212:143866:18:18:91:417:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:number of included assets and the trading (quoting) intensities.
73:2213:143930:18:18:109:520:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Rather than extracting principal components day-by-day to obtain a factor struc-
73:2214:144010:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ture  for  the  realized  covariance  matrix,  a  number  of  authors  propose  using  pre-
73:2215:144101:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specified observable factors, or returns on factor mimicking portfolios, as a way to
73:2216:144185:18:18:91:502:541:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:reduce the dimensionality of the problem and the associated estimation errors.58
73:2217:144265:18:18:109:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Recall the basic linear factor structure in equation (51),  where the parameters
73:2218:144345:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are assumed to be constant across days.  Extending the corresponding expression for
73:2219:144428:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the discrete-time returns on the factors in equation (50) to a continuous-time setting,
73:2220:144515:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:maintaining the same diffusion representation for the logarithmic factor price process
73:2221:144601:18:32:91:345:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as for the returns in equation (54), we may write,
73:2222:144651:32:33:233:520:419:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:dPF(t)  =  ΩF(t)1/2dWF(t),(65)
73:2223:144681:33:18:91:520:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where ΩF(t)1/2denotes theNF×NFpositive definite “square-root” of the instan-
73:2224:144757:18:18:91:520:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:taneous  covariance  matrix,  andWF(t)  is  aNF-dimensional  vector  of  independent
73:2225:144841:18:18:91:519:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Brownian motions.  Denoting the resulting daytrealized covariance matrix for the
73:2226:144921:18:18:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:factors byˆΩF,t, an implied day-by-day realized covariance matrix estimator for the
73:2227:145004:18:30:91:404:314:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:N-dimensional vector of returns may then be constructed as,
73:2228:145063:30:35:243:520:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩFt=ˆBˆΩF,tˆB′+ˆDν,(66)
73:2229:145087:35:18:91:520:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereˆBandˆDνrefer to estimates of the factor loadings and the (diagonal) covariance
73:2230:145171:18:18:91:352:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix for the idiosyncratic variances, respectively.
73:2231:145224:18:18:109:520:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:This approach has been successfully implemented by Bannouh et al. (2010) for the
73:2232:145304:18:18:91:519:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimation of large dimensional daily covariance matrices for hundreds of individual
73:2233:145388:18:19:91:519:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stocks.  Bannouh et al. (2010) rely on a set of highly liquid exchange traded funds
73:2234:145471:19:15:101:519:158:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:58Fan et al. (2008) provide a formal theoretical analysis of the impact of dimensionality on the
73:2235:145567:15:0:91:376:143:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:estimation of covariance matrices in the context of factor models.
74:2236:145635:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(ETFs) as factors.  Prices for these contracts are essentially free of microstructure
74:2237:145720:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:noise  at  relatively  high  frequencies,  allowing  for  accurate  estimation  ofˆΩF,t.   In
74:2238:145813:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contrast,  they estimate the factor loadings from daily data to avoid biases due to
74:2239:145896:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:microstructure and Epps type effects.  An even simpler approach would be to rely
74:2240:145976:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on the market model, effectively settingκ= 0 in the earlier equations (57) and (58)
74:2241:146059:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for  the  shrinkage  estimator,  thereby  only  exploiting  the  realized  return  variation
74:2242:146151:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the market index as the single dynamic factor driving the covariance matrix in
74:2243:146232:18:18:91:249:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accordance with equation (66).
74:2244:146262:18:18:109:520:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Of course, as already noted in section 3.1.2, the restriction that the covariance
74:2245:146343:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix  of  the  idiosyncratic  returns  is  diagonal  is  rather  strong.   For  example,  it
74:2246:146437:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:precludes  sector  specific  effects.   In  an  effort  to  relax  this  assumption,  Fan  et  al.
74:2247:146535:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2011)  allow  for  some  correlation  in  the  error  covariance  matrix  by  imposing  the
74:2248:146627:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weaker requirement that the matrix is “sparse.”  Their estimation procedure exploits
74:2249:146711:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:random  matrix  theory  as  they  achieve  the  requisite  parsimony,  or  sparcity,  in  the
74:2250:146804:17:18:91:453:434:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:idiosyncratic covariance matrix via so-called thresholding techniques.59
74:2251:146876:18:18:109:520:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  assumption  that  the  factor  loadings  are  constant  may,  of  course,  also  be
74:2252:146964:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:problematic in some situations.  Just as high-frequency data for the factors may be
74:2253:147047:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:used in accurately estimatingˆΩF,t, high-frequency data for the factorsandthe returns
74:2254:147132:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:could similarly be used in the estimation of day-by-day realized factor loadings, or
74:2255:147216:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“betas.”  This idea for the estimation of daily realized factor loadings from intraday
74:2256:147302:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data  was  first  pursued  empirically  by  Bollerslev  and  Zhang  (2003)  and  Andersen
74:2257:147391:18:18:91:510:308:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:et al. (2006b) for the three Fama-French portfolios and the market, respectively.60
74:2258:147474:18:18:109:520:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:From a practical perspective, however, the estimation of the loadings runs into
74:2259:147553:18:18:91:520:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the exact same market microstructure problems that plague the originalRCovtes-
74:2260:147631:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:timator:  it  is  difficult  to  implement  with  illiquid  assets  and  the  large  dimensions
74:2261:147726:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:typically  required  for  asset  level  risk  analysis.   These  difficulties  may,  of  course,
74:2262:147822:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be partly overcome by resorting to some of the techniques already outlined above.
74:2263:147903:18:17:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This  mainly  involves  suitably  combining  the  different  procedures,  and  we  abstain
74:2264:147993:17:16:101:519:183:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:59Related banding and thresholding procedures for estimating daily realized covariance matrices
74:2265:148088:16:8:91:261:167:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:are discussed in Wang and Zou (2010).
74:2266:148125:8:16:101:519:159:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:60Estimation and forecasting of betas based on high-frequency data have also been explored more
74:2267:148220:16:0:91:417:143:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:recently within the Realized GARCH framework by Hansen et al. (2010b).
75:2268:148292:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from fleshing out the details.  Hence, instead of further discussion of techniques for
75:2269:148378:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measuring the current realized covariance matrix, we now turn to different dynamic
75:2270:148460:18:35:91:353:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models for forecasting realized covariance matrices.
75:2271:148512:35:26:91:438:614:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.2.2  Dynamic Modeling of Realized Covariance Matrices
75:2272:148567:26:18:91:519:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:All of the different procedures discussed in the preceding section for estimating the
75:2273:148652:18:18:91:519:570:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realized covariance matrix may in principle be applied as short term daily forecasts
75:2274:148736:18:17:91:519:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as well, when augmented with a martingale assumption for the realized covariance
75:2275:148816:17:18:91:520:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix, e.g., tomorrow’s expected covariance matrix equals today’s realization.61Of
75:2276:148899:18:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:course, the martingale hypothesis is at best a short term approximation, as both vari-
75:2277:148985:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ances and covariances generally display mean reversion.  Hence, for longer horizons
75:2278:149068:18:18:91:490:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:explicit time series models must be developed as a basis for sensible forecasts.
75:2279:149148:18:18:109:520:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Building on the univariate procedures discussed earlier, this section outlines var-
75:2280:149231:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ious strategies for modeling and forecasting integrated covariance matrices, treating
75:2281:149316:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the realized covariance matrix as directly observable, albeit with some measurement
75:2282:149399:18:18:91:519:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:error.  Since the literature on the estimation of large realized covariance matrices is
75:2283:149486:18:18:91:519:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:recent and remains limited, there are still no authoritative studies of the relative per-
75:2284:149575:18:18:91:520:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:formance of different approaches.62Consequently, our review of existing techniques
75:2285:149657:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is invariably somewhat speculative.  However, we anticipate this to be an area where
75:2286:149741:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:substantial progress will be made over the coming years, and therefore summarize
75:2287:149821:18:17:91:394:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:what we see as some of the more promising new directions.
75:2288:149878:17:18:109:520:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In parallel to the notation for the variance forecasts discussed earlier, we denote
75:2289:149961:18:18:91:519:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:theN×Npoint forecast of the integrated return covariance matrix for periodt+k
75:2290:150038:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:based on information through periodt, byˆΩt+k|t, while the corresponding measures
75:2291:150119:18:18:91:520:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the realized covariance matrix in periodtis generically labeledˆΩt.63Just as many
75:2292:150204:18:16:101:519:230:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:61Both  Hautsch  et  al.  (2011)  and  Lunde  et  al.  (2011)  base  their  exploration  of  one-day-ahead
75:2293:150310:16:8:91:294:214:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:covariance matrix forecasts on this hypothesis.
75:2294:150357:8:16:101:519:206:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:62The set of potential applications is literally unlimited, thus making it hard to settle on a simple
75:2295:150458:16:12:91:519:190:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:metric for assessing the economic value of improved forecasts, even if one focuses on practical risk
75:2296:150558:12:12:91:519:178:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:measurement and management problems.  An early study inspiring this literature is Fleming et al.
75:2297:150654:12:11:91:519:166:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:(2003), who suggest dramatic improvements vis-a-vis the RM and multivariate GARCH frameworks
75:2298:150746:11:9:91:363:155:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:for standard mean-variance efficient asset allocation problems.
75:2299:150809:9:0:101:519:146:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:63Of course, as discussed in the previous section, there are many alternative proposals for esti-
76:2300:150908:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  forecasting  models  for  the  realized  volatilities  discussed  in  section  2.2  were
76:2301:151005:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:directly inspired by existing techniques for forecasting with daily or lower frequency
76:2302:151091:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data, so are many of the procedures for dynamic realized covariance matrix modeling.
76:2303:151175:18:18:109:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In particular, directly emulating the Risk Metrics approach in equation (40), it
76:2304:151255:18:30:91:209:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is natural to postulate,
76:2305:151279:30:36:225:520:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩt+1|t=λˆΩt|t−1+ (1−λ)ˆΩt,(67)
76:2306:151310:36:18:91:520:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where 0< λ <1.  Thus, the integrated covariance matrix forecast is generated as an
76:2307:151392:18:18:91:520:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:exponentially weighted average of past realized covariance matrix measures withλ
76:2308:151472:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:controlling the relative weight ascribed to the more recent realizations.64Intuitively,
76:2309:151559:18:17:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this  allows  for  persistent  time-variation  in  the  realized  covariance  matrices,  while
76:2310:151653:17:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implicitly  acknowledging  that  each  realization  is  measured  with  error.   Of  course,
76:2311:151745:18:18:91:519:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this approach also inherits all of the problems with the conventional RM approach,
76:2312:151827:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:including the lack of mean-reversion, and as such may not be appropriate for longer
76:2313:151910:18:18:91:180:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forecast horizons.
76:2314:151928:18:18:109:520:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Alternatively,  mimicking  the  scalar  diagonal  GARCH  model  in  equation  (43)
76:2315:152010:18:33:91:392:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:suggests the following multivariate regression specification,
76:2316:152071:33:33:185:520:353:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:vech(ˆΩt+1)  =vech(C) +β vech(ˆΩt) +ξt+1,(68)
76:2317:152116:33:18:91:520:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where theN(N+ 1)/2×1 vectorξtdenotes an error term.  This system requires
76:2318:152189:18:14:91:520:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:nothing but OLS to implement, and conditional on the estimated parameters,ˆCand
76:2319:152268:14:36:93:486:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ˆβ,, the forecast for the integrated covariance matrix is readily obtained from,
76:2320:152348:36:24:201:520:252:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:vech(ˆΩt+1|t)  =vech(ˆC) +ˆβ vech(ˆΩt).(69)
76:2321:152391:24:12:91:520:228:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:mating Ωtand associated procedures for forecasting it, soˆΩtandˆΩt+k|tmerely serve as generic
76:2322:152484:12:12:91:519:216:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:indicators for the realized covariance measure and forecast being entertained at a given point in the
76:2323:152585:12:12:91:520:204:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:exposition.  We reserve the more specific notation,RCovt(∆), for the standard realized covariance
76:2324:152682:12:12:91:519:192:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:estimator  based  on  the  cross-product  of  returns  sampled  at  fixed  frequency  ∆.   Also,  as  in  the
76:2325:152791:12:12:91:520:180:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:univariate case, the models will typically stipulate a specific dynamic evolution for Ωt, whereas any
76:2326:152892:12:8:91:380:168:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:empirical analysis will be based on the time series of observedˆΩt.
76:2327:152959:8:16:101:519:160:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:64This particular procedure is among the set of dynamic specifications explored by, e.g., Fleming
76:2328:153056:16:0:91:443:144:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:et al. (2003), Liu (2009), Bannouh et al. (2010) and Varneskov and Voev (2010).
77:2329:153137:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Strict positive definiteness of the covariance matrix forecast in equation (69) is guar-
77:2330:153225:18:18:91:469:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:anteed for any pd matrixˆCand positive values ofˆβ, as long asˆΩtis psd.
77:2331:153297:18:18:109:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Even though the above procedure generalizes the “martingale” hypothesis, cor-
77:2332:153374:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding toC= 0 andβ= 1, it still assumes a common degree of mean rever-
77:2333:153448:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sion across all variances and covariances.  As noted previously, this is likely overly
77:2334:153534:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:restrictive,  especially  when  considering  a  diverse  set  of  assets,  so  it  is  worthwhile
77:2335:153631:18:18:91:290:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contemplating suitable generalizations.
77:2336:153670:18:18:109:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Pushing the above approach one step further,  any of the other procedures dis-
77:2337:153748:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cussed  in  section  3.1  could  be  similarly  adapted  to  modeling  realized  covariances,
77:2338:153841:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:keeping in mind the restrictions required for positive definiteness.  For example, the
77:2339:153927:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DCC-type framework naturally suggests first modeling the realized standard devia-
77:2340:154008:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions asset-by-asset using any of the procedures discussed in section 2.2, and the cor-
77:2341:154095:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding realized correlations in a second step.  Specifically, maintaining a simple
77:2342:154181:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic structure as in equation (68), the correlation dynamics for the standardized
77:2343:154265:17:33:91:239:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns could be modeled as,
77:2344:154293:33:33:193:520:401:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:vech(Qt)  =vech(C) +β vech(Qt−1) +ξt,(70)
77:2345:154334:33:18:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where we have extended the notation for the conventional DCC model in the obvious
77:2346:154415:18:18:91:519:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:way.  Again, simple OLS is all that is required for estimation.  As for the conventional
77:2347:154503:18:18:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DCC model, an additional normalization along the lines of equation (47) is needed
77:2348:154584:18:18:91:519:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to ensure that the resulting correlation matrix is well defined, with ones along the
77:2349:154668:18:18:91:448:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:diagonal and all of the off-diagonal elements falling between -1 and 1.
77:2350:154739:18:18:109:520:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The advantages of these approaches are twofold.  First, high-frequency informa-
77:2351:154818:18:17:91:519:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion is used to obtain more precise estimates of current variances and covariances,
77:2352:154901:17:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in turn resulting in better “initial conditions” for forecast calculations.  Second, by
77:2353:154988:18:18:91:519:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:treating the covariance matrices as directly observable no numerical optimization is
77:2354:155072:18:18:91:298:207:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:needed for the estimation of the models.
77:2355:155112:18:18:109:520:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Even  though  we  have  focussed  on  simple  first-order  models  and  corresponding
77:2356:155197:18:18:91:519:171:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one-day-ahead forecasts, all the procedures discussed above could easily be iterated
77:2357:155281:18:0:91:519:153:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:forward  to  generate  multi-period  forecastsˆΩt+k|t.   More  complicated  long-memory
78:2358:155370:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamics,  regime-switching,  or  asymmetries,  could  also  be  incorporated  into  the
78:2359:155458:18:18:91:499:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models, provided the dimensionality of the estimation problem is kept in check.
78:2360:155537:18:18:109:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A  major  obstacle  for  adopting  more  realistic  and  complex  representations  for
78:2361:155623:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the realized covariance  matrix  dynamics  than offered by,  e.g.,  equation  (68)  is,  as
78:2362:155714:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed at length previously, the requirement for positive definiteness.  A possible
78:2363:155800:18:18:91:520:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:solution consists of first applying a nonlinear transform to theRCovtmatrix with the
78:2364:155884:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:property that the inverse transform will ensure positive definiteness.  One may then
78:2365:155968:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specify and estimate the dynamics of the transformed system without imposing any
78:2366:156048:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constraints.  Once the future expected value of the transformed system is determined,
78:2367:156133:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  inversion  back  into  a  covariance  representation  automatically  produces  a  pd
78:2368:156222:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix forecast.  A popular example of this approach within the univariate setting
78:2369:156304:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  the  specification  of  dynamic  models  for  log  volatility,  as  in  the  EGARCH  and
78:2370:156396:18:18:91:434:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:log-HAR-RV models discussed in sections 2.1 and 2.2, respectively.
78:2371:156462:18:17:109:520:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In this regard, Andersen et al. (2003a) proposed modeling the Cholesky decompo-
78:2372:156541:17:18:91:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sition ofRCovrather than the matrix itself.  The Cholesky decomposition provides
78:2373:156621:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one possible definition of a unique square-root of a positive definite realized covari-
78:2374:156708:18:15:91:207:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance matrix estimator,
78:2375:156730:15:29:274:520:383:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩt=LtL′t,(71)
78:2376:156744:29:18:91:520:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereLtis a unique lower triangular matrix.  The data vector subjected to dynamic
78:2377:156825:18:18:91:520:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling is thenvech(Lt), and one simply substitute the forecast ofvech(Lt+k) back
78:2378:156907:18:18:91:520:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into equation (71) to construct a forecast of Ωt+k,∆.65One drawback to the use of
78:2379:156988:18:18:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Cholesky decompositions, and other non-linear transformations, is that the estimated
78:2380:157072:18:18:91:519:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameters can be difficult to interpret in terms of the marginal impacts of shocks
78:2381:157155:18:18:91:519:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to specific elements in the covariance matrix.  Related to this, the dynamic Cholesky
78:2382:157240:18:18:91:519:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling strategy inevitable involves a bias, arising from modeling and forecasting
78:2383:157323:18:18:91:519:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a nonlinear transformation and then mapping the resulting point forecasts back into
78:2384:157406:18:15:101:519:210:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:65Building on this framework,  Chiriac and Voev (2011) explore various dynamic specifications
78:2385:157499:15:12:91:519:195:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:of  the  realized  covariance  matrix  for  six  liquid  U.S.  stocks,  and  find  that  a  long-memory  vector
78:2386:157610:12:12:91:519:183:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ARFIMA model performs well.  The reliance on approximate maximum likelihood estimation ren-
78:2387:157701:12:12:91:519:171:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ders their approach problematic for large scale systems, but it should be feasible to adopt simpler
78:2388:157800:12:0:91:355:159:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:specifications that would enable estimation whenNis large.
79:2389:157860:0:18:91:213:685:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:the covariance matrix.66
79:2390:157884:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another strategy, proposed by Bauer and Vorkink (2011), is to exploit the matrix
79:2391:157964:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:logarithmic function.67Specifically,  provided thatˆΩtis positive definite,  then the
79:2392:158049:18:18:91:225:631:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:N×Nsymmetric matrix,
79:2393:158069:18:0:257:319:613:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:At=logm
79:2394:158076:0:10:320:327:626:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:(
79:2395:158077:10:0:329:339:616:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:A:ˆΩt
79:2396:158080:0:13:340:347:626:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:)
79:2397:158081:13:26:351:520:613:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:,(72)
79:2398:158086:26:35:91:450:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is implicitly defined by the inverse of the matrix exponential function,
79:2399:158158:35:0:260:287:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:ˆΩt=
79:2400:158162:0:29:301:314:564:8:g_d0_f9:12:g_d0_f10:?:∞∑
79:2401:158164:29:0:297:313:535:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:n=0
79:2402:158167:0:16:321:327:557:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:1
79:2403:158168:16:0:319:329:541:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:n!
79:2404:158170:0:40:332:520:549:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ant.(73)
79:2405:158178:40:18:91:520:509:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:One may then proceed as before by specifying the dynamics ofvech(At), estimating
79:2406:158258:18:17:91:520:491:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  system  and  constructing  the  impliedˆΩt+k|tforecasts.   Of  course,  the  dynamic
79:2407:158347:17:18:91:519:474:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specification forvech(At) must be kept relatively simple to remain tractable in large
79:2408:158432:18:18:91:520:456:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dimensions.68Also, the same general problems arising from the use of a non-linear
79:2409:158513:18:15:91:519:438:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:transformation in the Cholesky decomposition discussed above remain for theAtto
79:2410:158592:15:21:93:186:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ˆΩttransformation.
79:2411:158610:21:18:109:520:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In summary, while the literature on modeling the covariance matrix dynamics is
79:2412:158688:18:18:91:519:384:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:progressing rapidly along many different directions, there is still no consensus on the
79:2413:158775:18:18:91:519:366:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relative merits of the approaches.  It is clear, however, that the use of high-frequency
79:2414:158863:18:18:91:519:348:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:intraday  data  and  realized  covariance  measures  hold  the  promise  of  substantially
79:2415:158953:18:18:91:519:330:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:improving  the  accuracy  of  covariance  matrix  forecasting.   Going  one  step  further,
79:2416:159044:18:18:91:519:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  direct  parallel  to  the  approach  taken  in  the  univariate  setting  of  section  2.2.3,
79:2417:159141:18:18:91:519:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  realized  covariance  forecasts  discussed  above  may  also  be  embedded  within  a
79:2418:159231:18:18:91:519:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multivariate GARCH setting to provide a vehicle for combining the realized covari-
79:2419:159313:18:18:91:519:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance matrices with a multivariate distribution for the return innovations.  We briefly
79:2420:159399:18:17:91:363:240:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discuss some recent ideas for implementing this next.
79:2421:159452:17:16:101:519:223:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:66The aforementioned study by Chiriac and Voev (2011) also provides approximate bias correction
79:2422:159547:16:8:91:519:207:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:terms for this, but deem the extent of the bias to be relatively minor in their empirical application.
79:2423:159649:8:12:101:519:199:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:67A related multivariate matrix Exponential GARCH model was proposed by Kawakatsu (2006).
79:2424:159738:12:16:101:519:187:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:68The actual application in Bauer and Vorkink (2011) is relatively modest in terms of dimension-
79:2425:159834:16:0:91:475:171:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ality, and too highly parameterized to be be practical for high-dimensional applications.
80:2426:159925:0:26:91:314:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.2.3  Combining GARCH and RCov
80:2427:159956:26:18:91:519:659:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As  with  the  univariate  setting,  it  is  tempting  to  combine  the  precision  of  high-
80:2428:160049:18:18:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequency realized volatility based measures with the powerful and flexible economet-
80:2429:160134:18:18:91:519:623:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ric tools provided by (quasi) likelihood estimation of GARCH models in extracting
80:2430:160215:18:18:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the volatility dynamics for multivariate systems.  This can be done in a variety of
80:2431:160298:18:18:91:519:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ways, especially if one breaks the approach down into multiple steps.  Nonetheless,
80:2432:160381:18:18:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the literature dealing with this approach remains nascent and we have little evidence
80:2433:160466:18:18:91:519:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regarding the relative performance of alternative procedures,  so we only briefly il-
80:2434:160551:18:18:91:519:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lustrate how these methods may be combined to construct candidate models with
80:2435:160628:18:17:91:461:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-trivial dynamic covariance structures through a couple of examples.
80:2436:160699:17:18:109:520:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First, it is natural to exploit the various techniques for estimation of the realized
80:2437:160784:18:18:91:519:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correlation matrix, discussed in the initial parts of section 3, with the flexible dynamic
80:2438:160874:18:18:91:519:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling of the individual conditional variances afforded by GARCH style models.
80:2439:160954:18:18:91:519:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Recall  the  decomposition  in  equation  (45),  Ωt=DtΓtDt.   The  diagonal  condi-
80:2440:161037:18:18:91:520:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tional standard deviation matrix,Dt, may be obtained from univariate models, each
80:2441:161118:18:18:91:519:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimated  in  isolation  using  flexible  dynamic  specifications.   When  high-frequency
80:2442:161208:18:18:91:519:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data are available, the candidate univariate volatility models include the GARCH-X
80:2443:161290:18:18:91:519:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and Realized GARCH techniques reviewed in section 2.3.3.  These approaches en-
80:2444:161368:18:18:91:519:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sure volatility dynamics that quickly respond to changes in the underlying realized
80:2445:161451:18:18:91:519:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility measures and provide a great deal of freedom in adapting the estimation to
80:2446:161536:18:18:91:519:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:accommodate critical features of each specific series,  including asymmetric return-
80:2447:161620:18:18:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatility  relations,  long  memory  dynamic  dependencies,  calendar  effects,  and  the
80:2448:161710:18:18:91:337:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:degree of heavy tails in the return distributions.
80:2449:161760:18:17:109:519:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The conditional correlation matrix, Γt, also changes over time, but it is likely to
80:2450:161843:17:18:91:519:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:evolve more slowly than the conditional variances.  As such, one may exploit wider
80:2451:161925:18:18:91:519:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:estimation windows to enhance the precision of estimation. Technically, one may sim-
80:2452:162009:18:18:91:520:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ply stipulate a constant correlation matrix,  Γt= Γ , for a period of one week or one
80:2453:162094:18:18:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:month, say, but allow this constant matrix to be estimated over a rolling window so
80:2454:162177:18:18:91:519:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that it does evolve slowly over time.  The longer time series allows for additional flex-
80:2455:162266:18:0:91:519:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ibility in estimating the realized correlation matrix, even for a very large set of assets,
81:2456:162359:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:using the various techniques discussed in the previous sections.  The candidate proce-
81:2457:162445:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dures for estimating Γ , include the basicRCovtestimator using appropriately sparse
81:2458:162528:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sampling frequencies, the shrinkage estimators, or the various techniques exploiting
81:2459:162612:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:regularization via principal components,  observable factor structures,  thresholding
81:2460:162697:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  blocking.69Clearly,  the  potential  for  developing  alternative  approaches  along
81:2461:162786:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:these lines is vast and we currently have only limited knowledge about the relevant
81:2462:162869:18:18:91:471:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:empirical tradeoffs that will govern the success of the different techniques.
81:2463:162946:18:18:109:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, we briefly discuss a proposal that directly combines realized covariance
81:2464:163026:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:measures with GARCH style dynamics, namely the multivariate HEAVY model of
81:2465:163100:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Noureldin et al. (2011), which extends the univariate specification in equation (37).
81:2466:163185:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In the general form, the model inherits the curse of dimensionality from multivariate
81:2467:163270:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:GARCH representations, so the empirical work focuses on parsimonious, and restric-
81:2468:163352:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tive, representations.  The model is explicitly designed for the low-frequency (daily)
81:2469:163438:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realized return cross-product, but the information set is given by corresponding high-
81:2470:163524:17:18:91:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequency observations.  Denoting the realized daily return cross-product byUt, the
81:2471:163607:18:35:91:260:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model may be defined as follows,
81:2472:163639:35:0:216:274:381:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Ut=RtR

81:2484:163886:18:18:109:519:294:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Forecasting the covariance matrix requires a dynamic model forHt. One tractable
81:2485:163965:18:18:91:519:276:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:option is the scalar HEAVY parametrization, which is well defined subject to regu-
81:2486:164047:18:32:91:495:258:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:larity conditions resembling those from the scalar multivariate GARCH model,
81:2487:164123:32:0:216:290:226:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Ht+1=CHC
81:2488:164131:0:10:292:294:233:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:A:′

81:2490:164148:30:18:91:520:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Here,aHandbHare positive scalars,CHis aN×Nmatrix of constants, which may
81:2491:164220:18:17:91:520:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be fixed by covariance targeting, andVtdenotes a realized covariance measure, such
81:2492:164302:17:16:101:519:158:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:69One  example  of  applying  such  procedures  is  Rosenow  (2008)  although  he  only  applies  the
81:2493:164403:16:0:91:203:142:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:procedures for daily data.
82:2494:164431:0:18:91:438:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as, e.g., the realized covariance matrix based on 5-minute sampling.
82:2495:164499:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Equation  (75)  allows  for  one-step-ahead  forecasting,  but  multi-step  forecasting
82:2496:164586:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:requires  an  explicit  representation  of  the  dynamics  forVtas  well.   LettingMt=

82:2498:164725:33:33:252:520:598:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Vt=M1/2tΨtM1/2t,(76)
