82:2500:164822:18:18:91:520:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:associated dynamic representation forMtis analogous to the scalar GARCH style
82:2501:164899:18:32:91:443:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specification of equation (75), and directly generalizes equation (37),
82:2502:164970:32:0:211:288:497:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f5:A:Mt+1=CMC
82:2503:164978:0:10:291:293:504:6:g_d0_f13:6:g_d0_f13:A:′
82:2504:164979:10:30:289:520:494:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:M+bMMt+aMVt.(77)
82:2505:164995:30:18:91:519:464:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:With covariance matrix targeting, the scalar HEAVY system may be estimated by
82:2506:165072:18:18:91:519:446:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:standard  likelihood  techniques  once  we  provide  a  conditional  distribution  for  the
82:2507:165163:18:18:91:519:428:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stochastic  shocks  to  the  system.   In  particular,  if  the  return  innovations  are  i.i.d.
82:2508:165260:18:18:91:520:410:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Gaussian, the innovation matrix, Ξt, in equation (74) will be Wishart distributed.
82:2509:165342:18:18:91:466:392:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Likewise, one may assume Ψtin equation (76) to be Wishart distributed.
82:2510:165412:18:18:109:520:374:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In parallel to the univariate literature, Noureldin et al. (2011) find the inclusion of
82:2511:165499:18:18:91:519:356:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the high-frequency return information to provide significant improvements over cor-
82:2512:165582:18:18:91:519:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:responding GARCH models utilizing only daily return observations.  The upshot is
82:2513:165662:18:18:91:519:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that generalizations of multivariate GARCH models into settings that accommodate
82:2514:165742:18:17:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the inclusion of high-frequency data appear to provide a similar boost to the pre-
82:2515:165824:17:18:91:519:285:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dictive performance that was observed in the univariate case.  Obviously, the models
82:2516:165908:18:18:91:519:267:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:still impose quite unsatisfactory constraints on the dynamic evolution of the system
82:2517:165992:18:18:91:519:249:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as well as the conditional return innovations, rendering further tractable extensions
82:2518:166077:18:18:91:373:231:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to the framework important objectives for future work.
82:2519:166131:18:18:109:520:213:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In  summary,  the  opportunities  for  combining  factor  structures,  multiple  com-
82:2520:166216:18:18:91:519:195:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ponents, GARCH modeling approaches and realized covariance measures in distinct
82:2521:166295:18:18:91:519:177:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ways are nearly unlimited. The literature is progressing in different directions, but we
82:2522:166383:18:0:91:519:159:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lack consensus on how to assess and rank the performance of alternative procedures.
83:2523:166468:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Moreover,  it  is  evident  that  the  focus  on  the  covariance  matrix  fails  to  explicitly
83:2524:166564:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:incorporate features of the return distribution beyond the second moments,  which
83:2525:166645:18:39:91:499:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are potentially critical for active risk management.  We now turn to such issues.
83:2526:166726:39:26:91:440:610:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.3  Modeling Multivariate Return Distributions
83:2527:166773:26:18:91:519:584:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Just as a fully specified and realistic univariate distribution is needed for risk mea-
83:2528:166860:18:18:91:519:566:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:surement,  so  too  is  a  fully  specified  and  realistic  multivariate  (non-Gaussian)  dis-
83:2529:166955:18:18:91:519:548:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tribution needed for risk management.  For example,  a fully specified multivariate
83:2530:167038:18:18:91:519:530:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution  allows  for  the  computation  of  VaR  sensitivities  and  VaR  minimizing
83:2531:167127:18:18:91:180:512:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:portfolio weights.
83:2532:167145:18:18:109:520:494:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The results of Andersen et al. (2000a) suggest that, at least in the FX market, the
83:2533:167228:18:17:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multivariate distribution of returns standardized by the realized covariance matrix
83:2534:167311:17:18:91:519:459:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is  again  closely  approximated  by  a  normal  distribution.   As  long  as  the  realized
83:2535:167403:18:18:91:519:441:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatilities  are  available,  a  multivariate  version  of  the  log-normal  mixture  model
83:2536:167495:18:18:91:373:423:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed in section 2.3.2 could therefore be developed.
83:2537:167551:18:18:109:520:405:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As discussed at length above, however, construction and use of realized covariance
83:2538:167633:18:18:91:519:387:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrices may be problematic in situations when liquidity is not high.  In that situa-
83:2539:167718:18:18:91:519:369:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion one of the more traditional parametric GARCH type models discussed in section
83:2540:167800:18:18:91:519:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:3.1 may be used for modeling the temporal dependencies in the conditional covari-
83:2541:167881:18:18:91:519:333:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance matrix and then combined with an explicit (and by assumption time-invariant)
83:2542:167962:18:18:91:367:315:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multivariate distribution for the standardized returns.
83:2543:168017:18:18:109:520:297:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Specifically,  assuming the mean to be zero,  orMt= 0,  we have from equation
83:2544:168094:18:18:91:115:279:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(41),
83:2545:168099:18:26:142:520:261:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:Zt=  Ω−1/2tRt,Zt∼i.i.d.,Et−1(Zt) = 0V art−1(Zt) =I,(78)
83:2546:168154:26:18:91:519:235:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Alternatively,  recalling  the  decomposition  in  equation  (45),  it  is  sometimes  more
83:2547:168245:18:32:91:487:217:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:convenient to consider the vector of standardized, but correlated asset shocks
83:2548:168323:32:33:174:520:185:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:et=D−1tRt,Et−1(et)  =  0,  V art−1(et)  =  Γt,(79)
83:2549:168373:33:0:91:519:152:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereDtdenotes  the  diagonal  matrix  of  conditional  standard  deviations  for  each
84:2550:168462:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  the  assets,  and  Γtrefers  to  the  potentially  time-varying  conditional  correlation
84:2551:168555:18:18:91:128:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix.
84:2552:168562:18:18:109:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For concreteness, we focus on the DCC type decomposition in equation (79) and
84:2553:168639:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:express the return distributions below in terms ofet.  As discussed in section 3.1.1,
84:2554:168724:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:this is often more convenient in large dimensions, but the same general ideas apply
84:2555:168807:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for the basic decomposition in equation (78) and distributions expressed in terms of
84:2556:168891:18:35:91:106:577:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:Zt.
84:2557:168894:35:25:91:356:542:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3.1  Multivariate Parametric Distributions
84:2558:168938:25:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  normal  distribution  is  convenient  and  tempting  (but  dangerous)  to  use.   It
84:2559:169027:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implies that aggregate portfolio returns are also conditionally normally distributed.
84:2560:169112:18:33:91:362:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The multivariate normal density has the simple form
84:2561:169163:33:0:214:316:448:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:f(et)  =C(Γt) exp
84:2562:169180:0:10:318:323:458:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:(
84:2563:169181:10:0:326:383:448:12:g_d0_f8:8:g_d0_f6:A:−12e′tΓ−1tet
84:2564:169193:0:10:386:391:458:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:)
84:2565:169194:10:33:393:520:448:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:,(80)
84:2566:169199:33:18:91:520:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where  theC(Γt)  normalization  factor  ensures  that  the  density  integrates  to  one.
84:2567:169288:18:18:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The multivariate normal distribution, however, typically does not provide an accu-
84:2568:169370:18:18:91:519:379:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate  picture  of  tail  risk.   In  parallel  to  our  earlier  discussion  of  univariate  return
84:2569:169469:18:17:91:519:361:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distributions, several multivariate distributions have been proposed to remedy this
84:2570:169552:17:18:91:143:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deficiency.
84:2571:169563:18:18:109:520:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Especially prominent among these is the multivariate Student’st-distribution first
84:2572:169645:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:employed in this context by Harvey et al. (1992); see also the more recent work by
84:2573:169727:18:18:91:520:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Glasserman  et  al.  (2002).   The  multivariate  standardized  symmetrict-distribution
84:2574:169814:18:39:91:356:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with correlation matrix Γthas the following density
84:2575:169865:39:0:196:287:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:f(et)  =C(d,Γt)
84:2576:169880:0:17:291:300:250:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:(
84:2577:169881:17:0:300:318:233:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:1 +
84:2578:169884:0:17:321:357:241:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:A:e′tΓ−1tet
84:2579:169893:17:0:321:357:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:(d−2)
84:2580:169898:0:17:361:409:250:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f7:?:)−(d+N)/2
84:2581:169907:17:36:412:520:233:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:,(81)
84:2582:169912:36:18:91:520:197:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:whereC(d,Γt) again ensures that the density integrates to one.  Thed >2 scalar
84:2583:169990:18:18:91:520:179:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parameter determines the degree of leptokurtosis in the distribution.  Whendgoes
84:2584:170070:18:18:91:520:161:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to infinity the power-form of thet-distribution converges to an exponential function
84:2585:170154:18:0:91:519:143:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and  the  multivariate  normal  distribution  emerges  in  the  limit.   Unlike  the  normal
85:2586:170248:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution, the multivariatet-distribution allows for nonlinear tail dependence be-
85:2587:170333:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tween assets.  It does so in a symmetric fashion, however.  It cannot accommodate
85:2588:170414:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two assets having a higher probability of a large joint down move than a joint up
85:2589:170495:18:17:91:241:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:move of the same magnitude.

85:2639:171044:13:18:164:520:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:is another normalization factor.  The definitions of   ̇μand ̇Γ ensure that
85:2640:171119:18:18:91:520:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the vector of standardized return shocks,et, has mean zero and correlation matrix
85:2641:171200:18:15:91:519:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Γt.  Note that forξ= 0 and the absence of any asymmetries,  we have   ̇μ= 0 and
85:2642:171279:15:21:95:520:338:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B: ̇Γt= Γt.  The asymmetrict-distribution therefore nests the symmetrict-distribution
85:2643:171362:21:18:91:177:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:as a special case.
85:2644:171380:18:18:109:520:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:While  the  asymmetrict-distribution  is  more  flexible  than  the  symmetrict,  it
85:2645:171464:18:18:91:520:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:requires that theNasymmetry parameters inξbe estimated simultaneously with the
85:2646:171542:18:18:91:519:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other parameters of the model.  This becomes quite challenging in large dimensions.
85:2647:171625:18:18:91:519:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Instead copula methods sometimes provide a more flexible approach by allowing the
85:2648:171706:18:18:91:519:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:univariate  and  distinctly  multivariate  distributional  aspects  to  be  specified  in  two
85:2649:171800:18:0:91:166:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:separate steps.
86:2650:171817:0:26:91:230:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3.2  Copula Methods
86:2651:171838:26:18:91:519:659:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Much attention in risk management has focused on the construction of multivariate
86:2652:171919:18:18:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:densities from the marginal densities via copulas, as in, for example, Li (2000), Jon-
86:2653:172005:18:18:91:519:623:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deau and Rockinger (2006), Patton (2006), Rosenberg and Schuermann (2006), Creal
86:2654:172085:18:18:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2011),  and Hafner and Manner (2011).  We will not attempt an exhaustive
86:2655:172165:18:18:91:519:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:review of this extensive literature here, referring instead to the in-depth treatment
86:2656:172250:18:18:91:211:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in McNeil et al. (2005).
86:2657:172274:18:18:109:520:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  central  result  in  copula  theory  is  Sklar’s  theorem.    The  theorem  states
86:2658:172361:18:18:91:520:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that for a very general class of multivariate distribution functions,  sayF(e),  with
86:2659:172446:18:17:91:520:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal distribtionsF1(e1),...,FN(eN),there exists a unique copulaG(·) linking
86:2660:172525:17:33:91:286:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the marginals to the joint distribution
86:2661:172564:33:32:152:520:465:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:F(e)  =G(F1(e1),...,FN(eN) )≡G(u1,...,uN)≡G(u),(83)
86:2662:172615:32:17:91:520:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where theN×1uvector is defined via theNmarginals.  In turn, this implies that
86:2663:172692:17:37:91:321:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the multivariate density may be expressed as
86:2664:172736:37:0:177:211:379:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f15:A:f(e)  =
86:2665:172743:0:15:216:333:387:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f15:A:∂NG(F1(e1),...,FN(eN))
86:2666:172765:15:0:252:296:372:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f6:A:∂e1...∂eN
86:2667:172774:0:0:339:385:379:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f8:?:=g(u)×
86:2668:172780:0:27:391:402:393:8:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f10:A:N∏
86:2669:172782:27:0:388:402:366:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:i=1
86:2670:172785:0:37:404:519:379:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f15:F:fi(ei).(84)
86:2671:172796:37:18:97:519:342:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The  resulting  log  likelihood  function  for  a  sample  of  sizeTtherefore  naturally
86:2672:172884:18:40:91:272:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:decomposes into two separate sums
86:2673:172917:40:0:189:230:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:logL=
86:2674:172922:0:28:245:256:299:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:A:T∑
86:2675:172924:28:0:241:255:271:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:t=1
86:2676:172927:0:0:260:318:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:logg(ut)  +
86:2677:172938:0:28:333:344:299:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:T∑
86:2678:172940:28:0:329:343:271:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:A:t=1
86:2679:172943:0:28:353:365:299:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:N∑
86:2680:172945:28:0:350:364:271:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f7:?:i=1
86:2681:172948:0:39:370:520:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:logfi(ei,t).(85)
86:2682:172964:39:18:91:519:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:This offers a potentially powerful framework for risk model builders by allowing the
86:2683:173048:18:18:91:519:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:modeling of the marginal densities, corresponding to the second double summation,
86:2684:173129:18:18:91:519:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to  be  separated  from  the  modeling  of  the  copula  function  appearing  in  the  first
86:2685:173221:18:15:91:159:191:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:summation.70
86:2686:173233:15:16:101:520:176:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:70Note, this implicitly assumes that the copula functiong(·) is constant through time.  Although
86:2687:173329:16:12:91:519:160:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:fundamentally different, this parallels the assumption of a time-invariant multivariate distribution
86:2688:173429:12:0:91:418:148:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f15:F:f(·) for the standardized returns underlying the discussion in section 3.3.1.
87:2689:173508:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Of course, in order to actually implement this approach, we need to specify the
87:2690:173587:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:copula functiong(·).  The most commonly employed copula is constructed from the
87:2691:173666:18:36:91:436:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multivariate normal distribution.  It may be succinctly expressed as
87:2692:173734:36:0:161:245:613:12:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f9:?:g(ut; Γ∗t) =|Γ∗t|−
87:2693:173752:0:9:246:250:622:6:g_d0_f12:6:g_d0_f12:A:12
87:2694:173754:9:0:253:271:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:exp
87:2695:173757:0:17:273:282:630:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:{
87:2696:173758:17:0:282:291:613:12:g_d0_f8:12:g_d0_f8:?:−
87:2697:173759:0:16:293:299:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:1
87:2698:173760:16:0:293:299:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:2
87:2699:173761:0:0:300:434:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:?:Φ−1(ut)′(Γ∗−1t−I)Φ−1(ut)
87:2700:173785:0:17:434:443:630:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:C:}
87:2701:173786:17:37:446:520:613:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:,(86)
87:2702:173791:37:17:91:519:576:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where Φ−1(ut) refers to theN×1 vector of standard inverse univariate normals, and
87:2703:173872:17:33:91:496:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the correlation matrix Γ∗tpertains to theN×1 vectore∗twith typical element,
87:2704:173947:33:33:218:520:526:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:e∗i,t=  Φ−1(ui,t)  =  Φ−1(Fi(ei,t)).(87)
87:2705:173987:33:18:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The normal copula has the advantage that it is relatively easy to work with. However,
87:2706:174072:18:18:91:519:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:even though it is more flexible than the standard multivariate normal distribution, for
87:2707:174159:18:18:91:519:457:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:many financial risk applications it does not allow for sufficient dependence between
87:2708:174243:18:18:91:147:439:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tail events.
87:2709:174255:18:18:109:520:421:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To  remedy  this  an  alternative  copula  model  can  be  built  from  the  multivari-
87:2710:174342:18:18:91:519:403:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:atet-distribution.   The  resultingt-copula  allows  for  tail  dependence  between  the
87:2711:174430:18:17:91:520:385:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:marginal  probabilitiesui,tbut  only  in  a  symmetric  fashion.   Going  one  step  fur-
87:2712:174519:17:18:91:520:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ther, an asymmetrict-copula may also be developed from the asymmetric multivari-
87:2713:174599:18:18:91:520:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:atet-distribution discussed above.  From a practical modeling perspective,t-copula
87:2714:174681:18:18:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:models have the potential to break the curse of dimensionality, which is otherwise
87:2715:174763:18:18:91:519:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unavoidable  in  multivariatet-distributions  whenNis  large.   In  particular,  while
87:2716:174849:18:18:91:520:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the asymmetrictdistribution in (82) requires the simultaneous estimation ofξand
87:2717:174928:18:18:91:520:278:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:d, amounting to a total ofN+ 1 parameters, when using the asymmetrict-copula
87:2718:175004:18:18:91:519:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:instead,  it  is  possible  to  separately  estimate  each  of  theNmarginal  distributions
87:2719:175095:18:18:91:519:242:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:allowing for asset specific distributional features.71The marginal distributions may
87:2720:175179:18:18:91:519:224:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:then be “tied” together using an asymmetrict-copula with only two parameters:  a
87:2721:175259:18:18:91:520:206:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:scalar copuladGand a scalar copula asymmetry parameterξG.  This approach has
87:2722:175335:18:18:91:413:188:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:successfully been implemented by Christoffersen et al. (2011a).
87:2723:175398:18:16:101:520:170:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:71Of course, the need to estimate theN×Ncorrelation matrix Γtfurther confound the estimation
87:2724:175490:16:0:91:129:154:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:problem.
88:2725:175500:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Many  other  classes  of  copula  functions  exist  as  well.   Most  of  these,  however,
88:2726:175590:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:including the popular Gumbel and Clayton classes, are not yet operational in high
88:2727:175671:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dimensions.  An intriguing approach to overcoming this general dimensionality prob-
88:2728:175754:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lem has recently been suggested by Oh and Patton (2011), who recommend relying
88:2729:175832:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:on  a  latent  factor  structure  for  the  copula.   Fully  efficient  estimation  of  this  new
88:2730:175929:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:class of models is complicated by the lack of closed-form expression for the likelihood
88:2731:176016:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:function but it is relatively easy to do via simulation-based procedures that match
88:2732:176099:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:appropriate rank statistics.  Oh and Patton (2011) find that this new approach works
88:2733:176183:18:18:91:520:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:well in an application involving one hundred individual stocks.72It is too early to
88:2734:176266:18:34:91:382:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tell how widely applicable this copula-factor structure is.
88:2735:176325:34:26:91:314:489:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3.3  Combining GARCH and RCov
88:2736:176356:26:18:91:519:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Another  approach  for  obtaining  full-fledged  multivariate  conditional  return  distri-
88:2737:176447:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:butions is to combine the realized covariance measures and GARCH style dynamic
88:2738:176525:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:specifications  with  specific  distributional  assumptions,  along  the  lines  of  the  pro-
88:2739:176619:18:18:91:519:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cedures discussed in section 3.2.3 where the innovation distributions were specified
88:2740:176703:18:18:91:519:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mostly to ensure tractable (quasi-likelihood) estimation of the underlying dynamic
88:2741:176785:18:18:91:186:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model parameters.
88:2742:176802:18:18:109:520:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For example, if the distributions adopted for each of the univariate return innova-
88:2743:176885:18:18:91:520:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion series in the GARCH specifications for the individual components ofDtin the
88:2744:176965:18:17:91:519:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DCC-style decomposition in equation (45) are taken as exact representations of the
88:2745:177047:17:18:91:519:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data generating process, this in principle defines a conditional one-step-ahead return
88:2746:177133:18:18:91:519:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution given the estimated (and assumed to be constant) realized correlation
88:2747:177215:18:18:91:519:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:matrix.  However, this is only tractable if simple, and restrictive, distributional as-
88:2748:177302:18:18:91:519:248:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sumptions are imposed.  Typically,  this implies resorting to a multivariate normal
88:2749:177385:18:18:91:519:230:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or studentt-distribution for the return innovation vector.  This severely limits the
88:2750:177469:18:18:91:519:212:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:complexity and realism in modeling the individual return innovations and volatili-
88:2751:177551:18:18:91:519:194:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ties.  Short-term multi-horizon forecasts may be similarly obtained, if one stipulates
88:2752:177637:18:15:101:519:176:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:72Their actual estimation results also suggest significant tail dependencies for most of the indi-
88:2753:177735:15:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:vidual stocks in their sample,  with the degree of tail dependence being stronger in crashes than
88:2754:177832:12:0:91:122:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:booms.
89:2755:177840:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the correlation matrix remains constant.  For longer horizons, however, the dy-
89:2756:177924:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:namics of the realized correlation matrix would need to be modeled separately.  In
89:2757:178006:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that situation the system quickly becomes analytically untractable, and simulation
89:2758:178088:18:18:91:464:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:techniques are required for obtaining the multi-horizon density forecasts.
89:2759:178162:18:18:109:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Another possible route involves the HEAVY model introduced in equations (74)-
89:2760:178239:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(77).   Assuming  both  multivariate  innovation  distributions  are  truly  Wishart,  as
89:2761:178328:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussed in section 3.2.3, the model naturally delivers a complete characterization
89:2762:178412:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the one-step-ahead joint return distribution.  The multi-horizon density forecasts
89:2763:178497:18:18:91:317:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:must again rely on Monte Carlo procedures.
89:2764:178539:18:18:109:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As an alternative to these GARCH representations, there has recently been an
89:2765:178615:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:upsurge in work on related multivariate stochastic volatility models.  These specifi-
89:2766:178700:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cations generalize GARCH models in the sense that the dynamics of the volatility
89:2767:178780:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:process is governed by independent random shocks rather than a deterministic func-
89:2768:178862:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion of the return innovations.  The models tend to be heavily parametric but they
89:2769:178944:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may, under appropriate simplifying assumptions, be combined with realized covari-
89:2770:179025:18:18:91:520:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ance matrix measures.73These models typically exploit Gaussian assumptions for
89:2771:179103:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the return and volatility (square-root covariance matrix) innovations as they produce
89:2772:179188:18:18:91:463:380:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:“squares” that are Wishart distributed and thus known in closed form.74
89:2773:179259:18:18:109:520:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The additive component Wishart-RCOV-A(K) model in Jin and Maheu (2010)
89:2774:179329:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provides an interesting example of combining such stochastic volatility representa-
89:2775:179412:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tions with realized measures, by exploiting features akin to a multivariate HAR-RV
89:2776:179494:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:model for the individual components of the realized covariance matrix.  Although the
89:2777:179578:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:empirical results appear promising, the parametric assumptions remain somewhat re-
89:2778:179660:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:strictive and estimation must be performed via Bayesian techniques using Markov
89:2779:179739:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) procedures that are tractable only for moderately sized
89:2780:179819:18:16:101:519:236:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:73Among the initial contributions in this area are Philipov and Glickman (2006), who specify a
89:2781:179913:16:12:91:519:220:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:standard Wishart transition density for the inverse covariance matrix of daily returns, as well as
89:2782:180011:12:12:91:519:208:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Gourieroux et al. (2009) who introduce the Wishart autoregressive model for daily data.  Extensions
89:2783:180110:12:12:91:519:196:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:of these models that involve realized covariance measures have been developed by, e.g., Bonato et al.
89:2784:180211:12:8:91:333:184:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:(2009), Golosnoy et al. (2010), and Asai and So (2010).
89:2785:180266:8:16:101:519:176:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:74The Wishart distribution provides the matrix generalization of a “squared” normal distribution,
89:2786:180363:16:12:91:520:160:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:i.e., just as the sum of squaredi.i.d.normal variates areχ2distributed, the sampling distribution
89:2787:180460:12:0:91:510:148:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:of the sample covariance matrix for draws from the multivariate normal distribution is Wishart.
90:2788:180557:0:18:91:134:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:systems.
90:2789:180565:18:18:109:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To summarize, the work on incorporating time-varying realized covariance mea-
90:2790:180642:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sures within the multivariate GARCH and related stochastic volatility model setting
90:2791:180725:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is in its infancy.  Given the need for tractability, the existing procedures invoke overly
90:2792:180815:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simplistic distributional assumptions, rendering the multi-horizon density forecasts
90:2793:180899:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:unable to fully account for critical features such as pronounced return-volatility asym-
90:2794:180987:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:metries, the possibility of jumps, long memory style volatility dynamics, and extreme
90:2795:181072:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correlations in down markets.  For the time being, such features are more readily por-
90:2796:181158:18:35:91:407:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trayed through the design of appropriate simulation methods.
90:2797:181218:35:25:91:328:506:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3.4  Multivariate Simulation Methods
90:2798:181256:25:18:91:519:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The multivariate normal distribution implies normally distributed portfolio returns
90:2799:181339:18:18:91:520:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:so that theV aR,ESand most other risk measures are easily computed analytically.
90:2800:181419:18:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:When using non-normal distributions, or any kind of copula, portfolioV aRandES
90:2801:181497:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:must instead be computed via Monte Carlo simulation, rendering purely simulation-
90:2802:181578:18:18:91:304:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:based methods relatively more attractive.
90:2803:181619:18:18:109:520:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In the general multivariate case, we can in principle use the Filtered Historical
90:2804:181700:18:18:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Simulation (FHS) approach discussed in section 2.3.4, but a multivariate standard-
90:2805:181782:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ization is needed.  Using for example the Cholesky or the spectral decomposition we
90:2806:181865:18:29:91:434:337:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:first create vectors of standardized returns as in equation (78); i.e.,
90:2807:181936:29:36:217:396:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:A:ˆZt=ˆΩ−1/2tRt,  t= 1,2, ... ,T ,
90:2808:181968:36:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:whereˆΩ−1/2tdenotes the relevant decomposition of the estimated covariance matrix.75
90:2809:182052:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Now, resampling with replacement vector-wise from the standardized returns will en-
90:2810:182135:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sure that the marginal distributions, as well as particular features of the multivariate
90:2811:182223:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution, as for example, the contemporaneous cross-sectional dependencies sug-
90:2812:182306:18:18:91:483:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gested by Longin and Solnik (2001), will be preserved in the simulated data.
90:2813:182382:18:18:109:520:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The dimensionality of the system may render the general multivariate standard-
90:2814:182460:18:15:101:519:164:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:75Patton  and  Sheppard  (2009)  recommend  the  spectral  decomposition  because  unlike  the
90:2815:182554:15:0:91:335:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:Cholesky, it is invariant to a reordering of the variables.
91:2816:182615:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ization above practically infeasible.  However, the same FHS approach can be applied
91:2817:182699:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the base asset setup discussed in section 3.1.2, resampling from the factor in-
91:2818:182783:18:15:91:142:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:novations,
91:2819:182793:15:7:203:271:634:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:A:ˆZF,t=ˆΩ−1/2
91:2820:182805:7:22:252:410:627:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:A:F,tRF,t,  t= 1,2, ......, T ,
91:2821:182834:22:18:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:where  we  again  rely  on  the  spectral  or  Cholesky  decomposition  to  build  up  the
91:2822:182924:18:18:91:519:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of the factor returns.  Given the specification in section 3.1.2, the corre-
91:2823:183013:18:33:91:458:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sponding idiosyncratic asset innovations may then be constructed from,
91:2824:183083:33:33:201:411:536:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:?:ˆνt=Rt−ˆB RF,t,  t= 1,2, ......, T .
91:2825:183119:33:18:91:520:503:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Thus, by resampling sequentially fromˆZtand ˆνt, we can easily build up the required
91:2826:183203:18:17:91:519:485:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:distribution of the individual asset returns.  This, of course, assumes that the base
91:2827:183288:17:18:91:430:468:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:asset model provides a good description of the joint dependencies.
91:2828:183354:18:18:109:520:450:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Alternatively,  if  one  is  willing  to  assume  constant  conditional  correlations,  as
91:2829:183444:18:18:91:520:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in equation (45) with Γt= Γ,  then the standardization can simply be done on an
91:2830:183523:18:18:91:519:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:individual asset-by-asset basis using the univariate GARCH or RV-based predictive
91:2831:183604:18:18:91:519:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatilities.   Resampling  vector-wise  from  the  standardized  returns  will  naturally
91:2832:183694:18:35:91:415:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:preserve the cross-sectional dependencies in the historical data.
91:2833:183759:35:25:91:344:343:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.3.5  Multivariate Extreme Value Theory
91:2834:183799:25:18:91:519:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The simulation procedures discussed above work well for numerically describing cor-
91:2835:183882:18:18:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relations and related “central” features of the joint return distributions.  Multivariate
91:2836:183971:18:18:91:519:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Extreme Value Theory (EVT) offers a tool for exploring cross-asset dependencies in
91:2837:184053:18:18:91:519:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the “tails” of distributions, which are not well-captured by standard parametric dis-
91:2838:184138:18:18:91:267:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tributions or correlation measures.
91:2839:184173:18:18:109:520:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:For example, Longin and Solnik (2001) define and compute extreme correlations
91:2840:184250:18:18:91:519:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between monthly U.S. index returns and a number of foreign country indexes.  In
91:2841:184329:18:18:91:519:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the case of the bivariate normal distribution, correlations between extremes taper off
91:2842:184415:18:18:91:519:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to zero as the thresholds defining the extremes get larger in absolute value.  Actual
91:2843:184500:18:0:91:519:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial  returns,  however,  behave  quite  differently.   In  particular,  the  correlation
92:2844:184596:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:between  the  large  (in  an  absolute  sense)  negative  returns  reported  in  Longin  and
92:2845:184688:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Solnik  (2001)  tend  to  be  much  larger  than  the  normal  distribution  would  suggest
92:2846:184779:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(while  interestingly,  the  correlations  of  large  positive  returns  appear  to  approach
92:2847:184872:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:zero in accordance with the normal distribution).76Such strong correlation between
92:2848:184954:18:18:91:408:613:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:negative extremes is clearly a key risk management concern.77
92:2849:185015:18:18:109:520:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:To  illustrate  the  important  deviations  from  multivariate  normality  commonly
92:2850:185098:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:found  in  financial  markets,  consider  the  threshold  plots  in  Figure  12.   The  solid
92:2851:185191:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lines in Figure 12 show the empirical equity index threshold correlations averaged
92:2852:185273:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across the 120 possible pairs of correlations based on the same 16 developed market
92:2853:185356:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns used in the estimation of the DECO model in Figure 11.  For comparison, the
92:2854:185439:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dashed lines indicate the threshold correlations implied by a multivariate standard
92:2855:185522:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:normal distribution with constant correlation, while the lines with square markers are
92:2856:185608:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the threshold correlations computed via simulations from the previously estimated
92:2857:185689:18:17:91:164:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DECO model.
92:2858:185700:17:18:109:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:As  the  figure  clearly  shows,  the  down-market  threshold  correlations  are  much
92:2859:185786:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stronger than the up-market correlations.  The multivariate normal distribution with
92:2860:185870:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:constant correlation captures quite closely the up-market correlations but it cannot
92:2861:185954:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simultaneously account for the much larger, and increasing with the threshold, down-
92:2862:186038:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market correlations.  The dynamic normal distribution driven by the basic Gaussian
92:2863:186120:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:DECO  model  generates  larger  threshold  correlations  overall,  but  the  model  does
92:2864:186208:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not explain the strong multivariate asymmetry that actually exists in the returns.
92:2865:186290:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The specification of dynamic multivariate models and distributions to satisfactorily
92:2866:186374:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:account for these important non-linear asymmetric extreme dependencies is challeng-
92:2867:186457:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ing.  It remains the focus of much ongoing work, much of which rely on the use of
92:2868:186538:18:18:91:309:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:copulas and/or EVT type approximations.
92:2869:186577:18:18:109:520:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A full treatment of this literature,  and the extensive literature on multivariate
92:2870:186659:18:15:101:519:218:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:76See also Ang and Bekaert (2002), Ang and Chen (2002) and Ang et al. (2006), among many
92:2871:186747:15:8:91:495:203:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:others, for additional empirical evidence on similar nonlinear dependencies in equity returns.
92:2872:186841:8:16:101:519:195:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:77It is generally unclear where these increased dependencies in the “tails” are coming from.  Poon
92:2873:186939:16:12:91:519:179:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:et al. (2004), for instance, report that “devolatilizing” the daily returns for a set of international
92:2874:187041:12:12:91:519:167:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:stock markets significantly reduces the joint tail dependence, while Bae et al. (2003) find that time-
92:2875:187143:12:12:91:519:155:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:varying volatility and GARCH effects can not fully explain the counts of coincident “extreme” daily
92:2876:187242:12:0:91:342:143:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:price moves observed across international equity markets.
93:2877:187301:0:0:219:198:506:2:g_d0_f1:2:g_d0_f1:A:−1−0.500.510
93:2878:187313:0:0:193:198:545:2:g_d0_f1:2:g_d0_f1:A:0.1

93:2880:187319:0:0:193:198:616:2:g_d0_f1:2:g_d0_f1:A:0.3

93:2886:187398:20:13:374:389:665:2:g_d0_f1:2:g_d0_f1:?:EmpiricalGaussian
93:2887:187415:13:175:374:385:652:2:g_d0_f1:2:g_d0_f1:?:DECO
93:2888:187419:175:12:91:519:477:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Figure 12:  Average Threshold Correlations for Sixteen Developed Equity Markets.
93:2889:187499:12:12:91:519:465:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:The solid line shows the average empirical threshold correlation for GARCH residuals across sixteen
93:2890:187598:12:12:91:519:453:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:developed equity markets.  The dashed line shows the threshold correlations implied by a multivari-
93:2891:187697:12:12:91:519:441:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:ate standard normal distribution with constant correlation.  The line with square markers shows
93:2892:187792:12:12:91:519:429:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the threshold correlations from a DECO model estimated on the GARCH residuals from the 16
93:2893:187881:12:47:91:411:417:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:equity markets.  The figure is based on weekly returns from 1973 to 2009.
93:2894:187954:47:17:91:519:370:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:EVT more generally,  is well beyond the scope of the present chapter.  Instead we
93:2895:188035:17:18:91:519:353:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:refer to the books by Embrechts et al. (2002) and McNeil et al. (2005), along with
93:2896:188117:18:18:91:519:335:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the recent discussion in Embrechts (2009).  Unfortunately, it is not yet clear whether
93:2897:188203:18:18:91:519:317:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:multivariate EVT distributions will be operational in large-dimensional systems.  Is-
93:2898:188288:18:18:91:519:299:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sues of scalability, as well as cross-sectional and temporal aggregation problems in
93:2899:188372:18:18:91:519:281:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parametric  approaches,  all  present  formidable  challenges.   Meanwhile,  just  as  the
93:2900:188462:18:18:91:519:263:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:newly available high-frequency data may be used in the construction of more accu-
93:2901:188543:18:18:91:519:245:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:rate  realized  volatility  measurements,  and  in  turn  covariance  matrix  forecasts,  we
93:2902:188635:18:18:91:519:227:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conjecture that the intraday data may be constructively used in a similar manner for
93:2903:188719:18:18:91:519:209:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:better measuring the “tails” of the return distributions, and in turn the joint extreme
93:2904:188806:18:18:91:519:191:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dependencies.  The recent theoretical results in Bollerslev and Todorov (2011a) and
93:2905:188889:18:0:91:439:173:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:related empirical findings in Bollerslev et al. (2011b) are suggestive.
94:2906:188962:0:26:91:359:685:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:3.4  Systemic Risk and Measurement
94:2907:188996:26:18:91:519:659:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We have emphasized using the univariate portfolio-level and multivariate asset-level
94:2908:189080:18:18:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk models discussed in sections 2 and 3, respectively, to construct real-time portfolio
94:2909:189169:18:18:91:519:623:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk  measures,  such  asV aRandES,  conditional  on  the  history  of  returns.   It  is
94:2910:189258:18:18:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sometimes  informative  also  to  consider  risk  measures  that  condition  not  only  on
94:2911:189348:18:18:91:520:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:historical  returns,  but  also  on  assumedscenariosfor  particular  risk  factors.   We
94:2912:189437:18:18:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:might, for example, be interested in the firm-specific effects of a market-wide shock,
94:2913:189523:18:18:91:348:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or the market-wide effects of a firm-specific shock.
94:2914:189575:18:18:109:520:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Such  scenario-based  conditional  risk  measures  are  intrinsically  related  to  mea-
94:2915:189663:18:17:91:520:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:surement  ofsystemicrisk.   There  is  no  single  definition  of  systemic  risk,  and  we
94:2916:189754:17:18:91:519:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:will  shortly  introduce  several,  but  the  defining  characteristic  is  that  systemic  risk
94:2917:189850:18:18:91:519:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:– one way or another – involves market-wide movements.  Systemic risk measures
94:2918:189928:18:18:91:519:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can help firms to develop richer and more informative risk reports internally.  They
94:2919:190012:18:18:91:519:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:can also be used by supervisory authorities to measure and monitor the firm-specific
94:2920:190096:18:18:91:519:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effects  of  market-wide  shocks,  the  market-wide  effects  of  firm-specific  shocks,  and
94:2921:190189:18:18:91:519:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the corresponding totals across all firms.  Those measurements may then impact pol-
94:2922:190272:18:18:91:519:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:icy decisions, such as which banks to support during crises, which bank mergers to
94:2923:190354:18:35:91:191:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:approve, and so on.
94:2924:190373:35:25:91:487:337:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.4.1  Marginal Expected Shortfall and Expected Capital Shortfall
94:2925:190438:25:33:91:339:312:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Marginal expected shortfall (MES) for firmjis
94:2926:190483:33:33:210:520:279:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:MESj|mktT+1|T=ET[rj,T+1|C(rmkt,T+1)],(88)
94:2927:190524:33:18:91:520:246:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wherermkt,T+1denotes the overall market return, andC(rmkt,T+1) denotes a systemic
94:2928:190605:18:18:91:520:228:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:event, such as the market return falling below some thresholdC.MESj|mkttracks
94:2929:190682:18:18:91:520:210:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the sensitivity of firmj’s return to a market-wide extreme event, thereby providing
94:2930:190765:18:18:91:353:192:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a simple market-based measure of firmj’s fragility.
94:2931:190816:18:17:109:520:174:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ultimately, however, we are interested in assessing the likelihood of firm distress,
94:2932:190900:17:0:91:519:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the fact that a firm’s expected return is sensitive to market-wide extreme events
95:2933:190987:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:– that is, the fact that itsMESis large – does not necessarily mean that market-
95:2934:191067:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wide extreme events are likely to place it in financial distress.  Instead, the distress
95:2935:191155:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:likelihood should depend not only onMES, but also on how much capital the firm
95:2936:191233:18:18:91:390:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:has on hand to buffer the effects of adverse market moves.
95:2937:191291:18:18:109:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:These distress considerations raise the idea of expected capital shortfall (ECS),
95:2938:191372:18:18:91:520:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:B:which is closely related to, but distinct from,MES.ECSis the expectedadditional
95:2939:191451:18:18:91:520:577:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:B:capitalneeded by firmjin case of a systemic market event.  ClearlyECSshould be
95:2940:191529:18:18:91:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:related toMES, and Acharya et al. (2010) indeed show that in a simple model the
95:2941:191608:18:33:91:213:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:two are linearly related,
95:2942:191633:33:32:221:520:508:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:A:ECSj|mktT+1|T=a0j+a1jMESj|mktT+1|T,(89)
95:2943:191672:32:18:91:519:476:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wherea0jdepends on firmj’s “prudential ratio” of asset value to equity as well as
95:2944:191753:18:18:91:520:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:its debt composition, anda1jdepends on firmj’s prudential ratio and initial capital.
95:2945:191837:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Note that the conditioning inECSis closely related to the idea ofstress testspopular
95:2946:191921:18:18:91:519:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  both  best-practice  private-sector  and  regulatory  risk  management.   Indeed  the
95:2947:192010:18:18:91:520:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:thought experiment embodied inECSisa stress test, with a very important and
95:2948:192085:18:18:91:351:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:natural stress (a large market event ) being tested.
95:2949:192137:18:18:109:520:368:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Building  on  the  theory  of  Acharya  et  al.  (2010),  Brownlees  and  Engle  (2011)
95:2950:192224:18:18:91:520:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:propose  and  empirically  implementECSj|mktT+1|Tas  a  measure  of  firmj’s  systemic
95:2951:192310:18:9:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk  exposure  to  the  market  at  timeT,  with  overall  systemic  risk  then  given  by
95:2952:192401:9:12:91:111:323:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:C:∑N
95:2953:192403:12:0:104:147:311:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:j=1ECS
95:2954:192409:0:10:148:169:320:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:j|mkt
95:2955:192414:10:14:147:519:310:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:T+1|T.  Implementation ofMES(and henceECS) requires specification
95:2956:192479:14:18:91:519:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of the systemic market eventC(rmkt,T+1), or more simply a market return threshold
95:2957:192560:18:18:91:520:278:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:C.   Values  ofC=  2%  andC=  40%  have,  for  example,  been  suggested  for  one-
95:2958:192643:18:17:91:519:260:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:day  and  six-month  returns,  respectively.   In  addition,  and  of  crucial  importance,
95:2959:192734:17:18:91:519:243:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implementation ofMESalso requires a multivariate volatility model.  That is, the
95:2960:192814:18:9:91:520:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditioning onC(rj,T+1) in all of the measures above, fromMESj|mktT+1|Tthrough to
95:2961:192896:9:13:91:111:216:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:C:∑N
95:2962:192898:13:0:104:147:203:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:j=1ECS
95:2963:192904:0:10:148:169:213:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:j|mkt
95:2964:192909:10:14:147:520:203:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:T+1|T,  requires at least a bivariate volatility model for firm and market
95:2965:192983:14:18:91:519:189:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns, and more generally a high-dimensional volatility model for all firms’ returns.
95:2966:193070:18:18:91:405:171:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:The models introduced in sections 3.1-3.3 satisfy that need.78
95:2967:193132:18:0:101:519:153:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:78Brownlees  and  Engle  (2011),  for  example,  use  the  daily  GARCH-DCC  modeling  approach
96:2968:193229:0:26:91:257:685:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.4.2  CoVaR and∆CoVaR
96:2969:193251:26:18:91:520:659:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In  the  previous  section  we  introducedMESandECS,  which  measure  firm  sys-

96:2973:193546:18:18:109:520:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In equation (1) we defined firmj’s 1-step-aheadV aRat levelpas the value of

96:2991:194180:18:18:91:520:343:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:As such,CoV aRis well-suited to measure tail-event linkages between financial in-
96:2992:194261:18:17:91:143:325:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stitutions.

96:2999:194740:25:12:91:520:163:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:described in section 3.1.1.  Interestingly, they find that aggregateMESincreased sharply starting
96:3000:194837:12:0:91:500:151:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:in mid-2007, and that even by mid-2010 it was still much higher than in the pre-crisis period.
97:3001:194933:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A direct extension lets us progress to the more interesting case of firmi’s overall
97:3002:195016:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:systemic  risk  contribution,  as  opposed  to  just  firmi’s  contribution  to  firmj.   We
97:3003:195108:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simply  setj=mkt,  so  that  ∆CoV aRmkt|iT+1|Tthen  measures  the  difference  between
97:3004:195194:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:marketV aRconditional on firmiexperiencing an extreme return, and marketV aR
97:3005:195270:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional on firmiexperiencing a normal return.79Hence ∆CoV aRmkt|iT+1|Tmeasures
97:3006:195352:18:0:91:345:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the contribution of firmito overall systemic risk,
97:3007:195402:0:13:349:368:604:12:g_d0_f10:8:g_d0_f6:?:∑N
97:3008:195404:13:0:361:426:591:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:i=1∆CoV aR
97:3009:195414:0:10:427:447:601:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:mkt|i
97:3010:195419:10:0:427:456:591:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:?:T+1|T.
97:3011:195425:0:22:456:464:599:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f7:?:80
97:3012:195427:22:18:109:537:577:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:A:The conditioning onC(ri,T+1) in all of theCoV aRmeasures above, fromCoV aRj|iT+1|T
97:3013:195509:18:0:91:145:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:through to

97:3018:195597:14:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns on firmsiandj, oriandmkt, and more generally a high-dimensional volatil-
97:3019:195677:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ity model for all firms’ returns.  The models introduced in sections 3.1-3.3 are again
97:3020:195763:18:34:91:143:505:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:relevant.81
97:3021:195774:34:26:91:260:471:12:g_d0_f2:12:g_d0_f2:C:3.4.3  Network Perspectives
97:3022:195801:26:18:91:519:445:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Interestingly, modern network theory provides a powerful unifying framework for sys-
97:3023:195885:18:18:91:519:427:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:temic risk measures, including measures likeECSandCoV aRintroduced above.82
97:3024:195960:18:18:91:520:409:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The simplest network is composed ofNnodes, where any given pair of nodes may or
97:3025:196039:18:18:91:520:391:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may not be linked.  We represent the network algebraically by anN×Nsymmetric
97:3026:196115:18:18:91:519:373:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:adjacency  matrixAof  zeros  and  ones,A=  [aij],  whereaij=  1  if  nodesiandj
97:3027:196194:18:18:91:519:355:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:are linked, andaij= 0 otherwise.  Because all network properties are embedded in
97:3028:196274:18:18:91:519:337:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:A, any sensible connectedness measure must be based onA.  The most important
97:3029:196350:18:17:91:519:319:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and popular, by far, are based on the idea of a node’sdegree, given by the number
97:3030:196431:17:0:91:257:302:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of  its  links  to  other  nodesδi=
97:3031:196466:0:12:263:276:310:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:∑
97:3032:196467:12:14:275:520:298:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:jaij,  as  well  as  aspects  of  the  degree  distribu-
97:3033:196523:14:18:91:519:284:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion across nodes.  The total degree Σiδi(or mean degree1NΣiδi) is the key network
97:3034:196605:18:16:91:212:266:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:connectedness measure.
97:3035:196627:16:15:101:520:250:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:79Alternatively we might setj=sys, wheresysdenotes the financial system, as measured by
97:3036:196714:15:9:91:334:235:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:the return on a portfolio of major financial institutions.
97:3037:196772:9:15:101:519:226:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:80The concept ofCoV aRalso has interesting parallels to the conditioning ofV aRin Garcia et al.
97:3038:196867:15:12:91:520:211:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:(2007), who show that proper conditioning inV aRcan eliminate the subadditivity problems raised
97:3039:196962:12:9:91:198:199:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:by Artzner et al. (1999).
97:3040:196987:9:15:101:519:190:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:81Multivariate quantile models, such as those recently developed by White et al. (2010), could
97:3041:197081:15:9:91:213:175:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:also be used in this context.
97:3042:197110:9:15:101:519:166:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:82Here we provide a brief overview of key ideas. Extended discussion, references, and systemic risk
97:3043:197209:15:0:91:519:151:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:measures based directly on network topology are contained in Diebold and Yilmaz (2009, 2011a,b).
98:3044:197307:0:18:109:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:The network structure sketched above is, however, rather too simple to describe
98:3045:197386:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the network connections of relevance in financial risk management.  Generalization
98:3046:197468:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in two key directions is necessary.  First, links may be of varying strength, not just
98:3047:197554:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:0-1.   Second,  links  may  be  of  different  strength  in  different  directions  (e.g.,  firmi
98:3048:197651:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:may impact firmjmore than firmjimpacts firmi).  Note,  for example,  that the
98:3049:197728:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:systemic risk measures introduced above are weighted and directional.  For example,
98:3050:197811:18:18:91:519:577:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:CoV aRj|iT+1|Ttracks effects fromitoj, whereasCoV aRi|jT+1|Ttracks effects fromjto
98:3051:197893:18:18:91:328:559:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:i, and in generalCoV aRj|iT+1|T6=CoV aRi|jT+1|T.
98:3052:197941:18:18:109:520:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:It is a simple matter, however, to characterize directed, weighted networks in a
98:3053:198021:18:18:91:520:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:parallel fashion.  To allow for directionality, we allow the adjacency matrixAto be
98:3054:198104:18:18:91:520:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:non-symmetric, and to allow for different relationship strengths we allowAto contain
98:3055:198188:18:18:91:520:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:weightsaij∈[0,1] rather than simply 0-1 entries.  Node degrees are now obtained
98:3056:198267:18:18:91:520:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by summing weights in [0,1] rather than simply zeros and ones.  In addition,  and
98:3057:198348:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:importantly, there are now “to-degrees” and “from-degrees,” corresponding to row
98:3058:198428:17:18:91:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sums and column sums, which generally differ sinceAis generally non-symmetric.
98:3059:198506:18:0:91:286:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The from-degree of nodeiisδfromi=
98:3060:198539:0:13:290:303:425:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:∑
98:3061:198540:13:0:303:498:412:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:jaij, and the to-degree of nodejisδ
98:3062:198575:0:7:498:505:420:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:to
98:3063:198577:7:19:498:104:413:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f10:?:j=∑
98:3064:198580:19:0:104:268:394:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:iaij.The total degree isδ= Σiδ
98:3065:198610:0:8:269:290:403:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:from
98:3066:198614:8:0:268:324:395:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:i= Σjδ
98:3067:198620:0:7:324:331:402:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:to
98:3068:198622:7:15:324:335:395:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:j.
98:3069:198624:15:18:109:520:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Crucially,  the  from-  and  to-degrees  (and  of  course  the  total  degree)  measure
98:3070:198711:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aspects of systemic risk. The from- and to-degrees measure systemic risk with respect
98:3071:198796:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to particular firms.  From-degrees measure exposures of individual firms to systemic
98:3072:198880:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:shocksfromthe network, in a fashion analogous toECSj|mktT+1|T.  To-degrees measure
98:3073:198962:18:18:91:520:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:contributions of individual firmstosystemic network events, in a fashion analogous to
98:3074:199047:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:∆CoV aRmkt|iT+1|T.  The total degree aggregates firm-specific systemic risk across firms,
98:3075:199136:18:18:91:375:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:providing a measure of total system-wide systemic risk.
98:3076:199191:18:18:109:520:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A key insight is that many approaches to systemic risk measurement fit naturally
98:3077:199271:18:18:91:520:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:into the network framework.  Consider,  for example,  ∆CoV aRmeasure.  One can
98:3078:199349:18:0:91:189:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f5:B:view the ∆CoV aR
98:3079:199365:0:10:189:198:225:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:j|i
98:3080:199368:10:15:189:518:215:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:F:T+1|T,i,j= 1,...,N(suitably scaled) as elements of anN×N
98:3081:199424:15:17:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:adjacency matrix for a weighted directed network of firms.  Then, for example, the
98:3082:199506:17:18:91:520:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:systemic  risk  of  firmi,  ∆CoV aRsys|iT+1|T,  is  the  network  to-degree  of  firmi,δtoi=
98:3083:199598:18:0:91:382:165:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Σj∆CoV aRj|iT+1|T.   And  finally,  the  total  systemic  risk,
98:3084:199661:0:13:388:401:174:12:g_d0_f10:12:g_d0_f10:A:∑
98:3085:199662:13:0:400:455:161:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f5:?:i∆CoV aR
98:3086:199670:0:10:455:473:171:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:?:sys|i
98:3087:199675:10:14:455:520:161:8:g_d0_f6:12:g_d0_f3:A:T+1|T,  is  the
98:3088:199690:14:0:91:209:147:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:network total degreeδ.
99:3089:199714:0:30:91:519:685:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:F:4  Conditioning on Macroeconomic Fundamentals
99:3090:199759:30:18:91:519:655:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The  risk  models  that  we  have  discussed  thus  far  are  inherently  “reduced  form,”
99:3091:199849:18:18:91:519:637:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  nature.   They  explain  risk  in  an  autoregressive  fashion,  as  exemplified  by  the
99:3092:199942:18:18:91:519:619:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:canonical  GARCH  family.   Fortunately,  even  if  the  models  fail  to  provide  a  deep
99:3093:200033:18:18:91:519:601:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:structural understanding of volatility movements, they are nevertheless powerful and
99:3094:200117:18:18:91:519:583:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:useful in a variety of contexts.  We have obviously emphasized risk measurement and
99:3095:200200:18:18:91:519:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:management, but other successful areas of application include portfolio allocation,
99:3096:200283:18:18:91:455:547:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:spot and derivative asset pricing, active trading, and dynamic hedging.
99:3097:200354:18:18:109:520:529:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Ultimately, however, we aspire to a deeper structural understanding.  That is, we
99:3098:200435:18:18:91:519:511:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:aspire to understand the connections between returns (especially, for our purposes,
99:3099:200518:18:18:91:519:493:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:return volatilities) and macroeconomic fundamentals, sayr↔f.  Asset prices are
99:3100:200596:18:17:91:519:475:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk-adjusted discounted claims on fundamental streams, so prices and their proper-
99:3101:200679:17:18:91:519:458:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ties should ultimately depend on expected fundamentals and associated fundamental
99:3102:200760:18:18:91:519:440:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risks.  Here we sketch emerging empirical aspects of those connections, through the
99:3103:200843:18:18:91:519:422:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:lens of return and fundamental first and second moments, denotedμr,σr,μf, andσf,
99:3104:200923:18:18:91:520:404:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:respectively.83Figure 13 provides a simple schematic diagram for all of the possible
99:3105:201007:18:18:91:520:386:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:connections amongσr,μr,σf, andμf.  Each of the six connections represents a po-
99:3106:201086:18:18:91:519:368:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:tentially important link, and a correspondingly important line of research inquiry.84
99:3107:201171:18:18:109:520:350:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Historically,  however,  it  is  well-known  thatσr,μr,σf,  andμfhave  often  ap-
99:3108:201252:18:18:91:519:332:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:peared only weakly connected, or even disconnected.  This observation is memorably
99:3109:201334:18:18:91:519:314:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enshrined  in  equity  markets  in  the  “excess  volatility”  puzzle  of  Shiller  (1981),  in
99:3110:201429:18:18:91:519:296:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:foreign exchange markets in the “exchange rate disconnect” puzzle of Obstfeld and
99:3111:201510:18:18:91:519:278:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rogoff  (2000),  in  bond  markets  in  Alan  Greenspan’s  long-maturity  yield  “conun-
99:3112:201598:18:17:91:192:260:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:drum,” and so on.85
99:3113:201617:17:16:101:519:243:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:83In parallel to the models for returns emphasized so far in this chapter, we will content ourselves
99:3114:201717:16:8:91:477:227:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:with means and variances, but one could, of course, also consider higher-order moments.
99:3115:201804:8:16:101:519:219:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:84Note that the links in Figure 13 are “undirected,” or “non-causal,” and as such more about
99:3116:201896:16:12:91:519:203:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:correlation than causation.  One could go even farther and consider directed, or causal, links, but
99:3117:201995:12:12:91:520:191:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:that would require replacing each bi-directional arrow in Figure 13 with apairof uni-directional
99:3118:202091:12:8:91:348:179:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:arrows, thus doubling the number of links to be addressed.
99:3119:202149:8:16:101:519:171:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:85On the conundrum:  “ ...  the broadly unanticipated behavior of world bond markets remains
99:3120:202241:16:12:91:519:155:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:a conundrum.  Bond price movements may be a short-term aberration,  but it will be some time
99:3121:202333:12:0:91:519:143:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:before we are able to better judge the forces underlying recent experience” [Alan Greenspan, U.S.
100:3122:202432:0:20:254:358:680:12:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f22:A:μr--σr

100:3130:202452:124:12:91:519:542:12:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f15:B:Figure 13: Return and Fundamental Mean and Volatility Linkages.Each link represents

100:3138:203055:18:39:91:246:388:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We now address them in turn.
100:3139:203083:39:25:91:425:349:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.1  The Macroeconomy and Return Volatility
100:3140:203126:25:18:91:519:324:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To begin, consider the link between macroeconomic fundamentals and return volatil-
100:3141:203208:18:18:91:520:306:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ity,μf↔σr.  Officer (1973) was among the first to document and emphasize the
100:3142:203284:18:18:91:519:288:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:very high stock market volatility during the very severe recession of the 1930s.  The
100:3143:203369:18:18:91:519:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:U.S.  stock  market  crash  of  1987  spurred  additional  research  into  the  fundamental
100:3144:203460:18:18:91:519:252:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:determinants of volatility.  In a well-known and exhaustive study in the wake of the
100:3145:203544:18:18:91:519:234:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:1987 crash, for example, Schwert (1989) went farther, showing that, surprisingly, the
100:3146:203629:18:18:91:519:216:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:oft-suspected  fundamentals  (leverage,  corporate  profitability,  etc.)   have  negligible
100:3147:203721:18:18:91:520:198:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:impact on market volatility,  while recessionsdo.  In particular,  return volatility is
100:3148:203808:18:23:91:519:180:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:significantly higher in recessions, so that high volatility during bad times is not just
100:3149:203896:23:0:91:440:157:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:congressional testimony, February 16, 2005]; see also Backus and Wright (2007).
101:3150:203977:0:14:257:462:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Mean RecessionStandardSample

101:3156:204295:12:12:91:519:569:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:is the cross-sectional inter-quartile range of quarterly returns.  Source:  Adapted from Bloom et al.
101:3157:204396:12:34:91:121:557:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:(2009).
101:3158:204403:34:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a  one-off  Great  Depression  phenomenon,  but  rather  a  regularly-recurring  business
101:3159:204492:18:18:91:188:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cycle phenomenon.
101:3160:204509:18:18:109:520:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:These findings regarding the link between financial market volatility and the busi-
101:3161:204592:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ness cycle have since been echoed repeatedly.  Hamilton and Lin (1996), for example,
101:3162:204676:18:18:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:provide strong and sophisticated confirmation using regime-switching models of real
101:3163:204759:18:18:91:519:433:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:growth and equity returns,  allowing for both high and low real growth states and
101:3164:204840:18:18:91:519:415:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high and low equity return volatility states.  Their estimated regime transition prob-
101:3165:204926:18:17:91:519:397:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:abilities indicate high positive steady-state coherence between low (high) real growth
101:3166:205012:17:18:91:289:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and high (low) equity return volatility.
101:3167:205052:18:18:109:520:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:More recent work, in particular Bloom et al. (2009) as summarized in Table 1,
101:3168:205129:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also  confirms  and  significantly  amplifies  Schwert’s  earlier  result,  showing,  among
101:3169:205220:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:other  things,  that  it  holds  not  only  for  stock  returns  at  the  aggregate  level,  but
101:3170:205316:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:also for the cross section of returns at the firm level.  Table 1 makes clear not only
101:3171:205402:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the statistical significance of the “recession effect” on volatility, but also its sizable
101:3172:205492:18:18:91:203:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:economic importance.
101:3173:205512:18:18:109:520:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although  we  have  emphasized  the  links  between  macroeconomic  fundamentals
101:3174:205592:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and equity market risk, one would expect related links in other market risk contexts.
101:3175:205677:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:To  take  one  example,  consider  foreign  exchange.   The  expected  real  streams  that
101:3176:205767:18:18:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:underlie exchange rate determination are similar to those that underlie broad equity-
101:3177:205852:18:18:91:519:182:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:market price determination,  except that for exchange rates there are two streams,
101:3178:205934:18:18:91:180:164:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for two countries.
101:3179:205952:18:0:109:520:146:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:A second example is credit risk.  In defaultable bond markets, for example, the
102:3180:206033:0:14:256:461:682:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Mean RecessionStandardSample
