102:3186:206354:12:34:91:501:569:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:inter-quartile range of quarterly real sales growth.  Source:  Adapted from Bloom et al. (2009).
102:3187:206450:34:18:91:519:535:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:celebrated Merton (1974) model directly links credit spreads to equity volatility, pre-
102:3188:206537:18:18:91:519:517:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dicting that higher equity volatility should widen spreads, as emphasized empirically
102:3189:206622:18:18:91:519:499:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:by Campbell and Tacksler (2003).  Hence the business cycle effects in equity volatility
102:3190:206709:18:39:91:482:481:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:imply parallel business cycle effects in credit spreads, via the Merton model.
102:3191:206787:39:25:91:466:442:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.2  The Macroeconomy and Fundamental Volatility
102:3192:206835:25:18:91:520:417:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The next link that we consider pertains toμf↔σf;  that is,  real activity and its
102:3193:206916:18:18:91:519:399:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:relationship  toreal(fundamental)  volatility.   It  transpires  that  real  fundamentals
102:3194:207005:18:18:91:519:381:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:affect real volatility not only at business-cycle frequencies, but also at lower growth
102:3195:207092:18:18:91:263:363:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequencies.  Hence we treat both.
102:3196:207126:18:18:109:519:345:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First  consider  fundamental  volatilityσfat  business-cycle  frequencies.   Bloom
102:3197:207208:18:18:91:520:327:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et  al.  (2009)  show  thatσfis  much  higher  in  recessions  (just  as  withσr),  at  both
102:3198:207300:18:18:91:519:309:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the aggregate level and at the cross-sectional firm level.  We summarize their results
102:3199:207386:18:18:91:519:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in Table 2.  Just as with the recession effect in stock return volatility, the recession
102:3200:207474:18:18:91:519:273:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:effect in real growth volatility is notable not only for its statistical significance, but
102:3201:207564:18:18:91:306:255:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:also for its sizable economic importance.86
102:3202:207607:18:18:109:519:237:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Observed  links  at  business-cycle  frequencies  between  real  growthμfand  real
102:3203:207689:18:18:91:520:219:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volatilityσfare also well-grounded in theory.  Recent research, for example, explores
102:3204:207774:18:18:91:519:201:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic stochastic general equilibrium models with heteroskedastic shocks (technol-
102:3205:207857:18:18:91:519:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ogy, preferences, policy, ...), as in Bloom (2009), Fern ́andez-Villaverde et al. (2011)
102:3206:207945:18:16:101:519:165:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:86Note that if stock return volatility and real growth volatility both increase during recessions,
102:3207:208043:16:0:91:505:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:then they themselves must, of course, be positively related.  We will return to this point below.
103:3208:208142:0:18:91:256:685:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:and Basu and Bundick (2011).87
103:3209:208172:18:18:109:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Now consider fundamental volatilityσfat growth frequencies.  Many have com-
103:3210:208247:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:mented  on  the  large  reduction  (roughly  fifty  percent)  in  U.S.  real  GDP  volatility
103:3211:208340:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:beginning  around  1985.   Dubbed  the  “Great  Moderation”  by  Stock  and  Watson
103:3212:208423:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2002), it was originally documented by Kim and Nelson (1999) and McConnell and
103:3213:208502:18:18:91:196:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Perez-Quiros (2000).
103:3214:208522:18:18:109:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Perhaps the “Great Moderation” was just a long string of good luck, or perhaps
103:3215:208600:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:it was a structural shift due to improved policy.  In any event it seems likely that it
103:3216:208687:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is over, as the recession of 2007-2009 was very long and very deep.  That is, even if
103:3217:208772:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a structural shift toward lower real volatility occurred in the mid-1980s, so too did
103:3218:208857:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:a shiftbackaround 2008.  Hence it may be useful to think of the Great Moderation
103:3219:208937:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:not  as  a  one-off  structural  shift,  but  rather  as  a  manifestation  of  a  low-frequency
103:3220:209033:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real  volatility  dynamic  driven  by  macroeconomic  factors  potentially  very  different
103:3221:209124:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from those that drive the earlier-discussed real volatility dynamics at business-cycle
103:3222:209210:17:18:91:150:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:frequencies.
103:3223:209222:18:18:109:520:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In intriguing recent work, Carvalho and Gabaix (2010) do precisely that, arguing
103:3224:209302:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that the Great Moderation was neither good policy nor good luck,  but rather the
103:3225:209382:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:natural  outcome  of  the  evolution  of  sectoral  shares,  which  during  the  post-1984
103:3226:209472:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:period produced a better-diversified (and hence less volatile) GDP. In related work
103:3227:209555:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from  an  explicit  network  perspective,  Acemoglu  et  al.  (2010)  make  clear  that  the
103:3228:209647:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:dynamic workings of “better diversification” are subtle and nuanced, depending not
103:3229:209729:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only on first-order connections among sectors, but also crucially on higher-ordered
103:3230:209812:18:39:91:153:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:connections.
103:3231:209824:39:26:91:447:251:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.3  Fundamental Volatility and Return Volatility
103:3232:209873:26:17:91:519:225:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Now consider the links between fundamental volatility and return volatility,σf↔σr.
103:3233:209955:17:18:91:518:208:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f6:B:Even  with  no  additional  work,  our  earlier  discussion  ofμf↔σrandμf↔σf
103:3234:210031:18:18:91:520:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:immediately implies thatσrandσfmust be positively related.  This is so because
103:3235:210109:18:19:91:520:172:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:σrandσfboth covary negatively with the business cycle (μf), and hence they must
103:3236:210188:19:0:101:464:153:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:87See also the insightful survey of Fern ́andez-Villaverde and Rubio-Ram ́ırez (2011).
104:3237:210276:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:covary positively with each other.  Hence the case is closed as soon as it is opened;
104:3238:210361:18:18:91:434:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:return volatility and real fundamental volatility are clearly related.
104:3239:210431:18:18:109:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:But  one  might  want  to  go  farther.   First,  one  might  want  to  complement  our
104:3240:210518:18:18:91:520:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:deduction of aσf↔σrlink with a direct exploration.  Engle et al. (2006) do just
104:3241:210597:18:18:91:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that,  directly  documenting  the  links  betweenσfandσrafter  effectively  removing
104:3242:210681:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:high-frequency variation in returns and fundamentals using a persistent/transitory
104:3243:210763:18:18:91:185:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:component model.
104:3244:210779:18:18:109:520:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second,  one  might  want  to  explore  cross-section  and  panel  aspects.   That  can
104:3245:210866:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:be useful because the precision with which relationships can be inferred depends on
104:3246:210949:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the amount of variation in the data, and there may be more variation over a broad
104:3247:211030:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cross section of countries than for a single country over time.  Diebold and Yilmaz
104:3248:211113:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2010) do this, showing that countries with higher fundamental volatility tend to have
104:3249:211199:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:higher broad stock market volatility, even controlling for initial development level.  In
104:3250:211288:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the most thorough study to date, Engle and Rangel (2008) explore time-series, cross-
104:3251:211372:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sections and panels, clearly finding that the “long-term volatilities of macroeconomic
104:3252:211458:18:18:91:459:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fundamentals ...  are primary causes of low-frequency market volatility.”
104:3253:211531:18:18:109:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:In closing this section we note that we have largely interpreted “market risk and
104:3254:211612:18:18:91:520:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:macro fundamentals” as “marketvolatilityand macro fundamentals.” As we have
104:3255:211687:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:emphasized  earlier  in  our  discussion  of  portfolio-level  risk  measurement,  however,
104:3256:211778:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:one may naturally approach market volatility from a top-down (portfolio-level) or
104:3257:211859:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bottom-up (asset-level) perspective.  In a bottom-up approach, not only conditional
104:3258:211942:18:18:91:520:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:variances but also conditionalcorrelationsamong individual returns are of central
104:3259:212023:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:importance  as  they  obviously  impact  portfolio  (i.e.,  market)  volatility.   Hence  the
104:3260:212116:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fundamental  determinants  of  conditional  correlations  have  also  recently  begun  to
104:3261:212205:18:39:91:341:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:receive attention, as in Engle and Rangel (2011).
104:3262:212254:39:25:91:212:215:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.4  Other Links
104:3263:212270:25:18:91:519:190:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:The links between volatility and fundamentals that we have discussed thus far do not
104:3264:212354:18:18:91:519:172:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:involveμr.  There are two main reasons.  First, the horizons emphasized throughout
104:3265:212436:18:0:91:519:154:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:most of the chapter tend to be fairly short – typically less than a month – and at such
105:3266:212526:0:18:91:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:short horizonsμris small and arguably almost constant.88Second, at longer horizons
105:3267:212608:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for whichμris larger and likely time-varying in interesting ways, we can interpret
105:3268:212690:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:μras an excess return (“the equity premium”), which, of course, is the subject of an
105:3269:212774:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:enormous and distinguished literature that is treated extensively elsewhere in this
105:3270:212857:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:volume.  Hence we provide here only brief glimpses of aspects of the linksμr↔σr,
105:3271:212937:18:18:91:474:595:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:μr↔μfandμr↔σfas they relate most directly to our present concerns.
105:3272:213003:18:18:109:519:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:First, consider the equity premium and return-volatility relationship,μr↔σr.
105:3273:213079:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Stimulated by the pioneering work of Markowitz (1959), an enormous amount of asset
105:3274:213161:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:pricing research has focused on quantifying various aspects of this financial market
105:3275:213245:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“risk-return tradeoff.” Financial econometric research has followed suit, as exempli-
105:3276:213330:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fied by the GARCH-M model of Engle et al. (1987), defined by equations (7) and (8)
105:3277:213412:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:above withμt=x′tβ+δσt.  In this model the conditional standard deviation enters
105:3278:213491:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:directly as an explanatory variable for the conditional mean – together with other
105:3279:213573:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:possible explanatory variablesxt– thus providing an econometric approximation to
105:3280:213653:17:18:91:249:434:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:a time-varying risk premium.89
105:3281:213683:18:18:109:520:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although intuitively appealing, a number of subtleties have emerged in both the-
105:3282:213763:18:18:91:519:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ory and empirics.  Modern general equilibrium theory reveals that, in principle, pos-
105:3283:213848:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:itive contemporaneous risk-return correlation is not guaranteed, as subtle dynamic
105:3284:213930:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:interactions may be operative;  see,  e.g.,  Abel (1988),  Backus and Gregory (1993),
105:3285:214015:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Whitelaw (2000), and Bollerslev et al. (2011a) among others.  In parallel, a wealth
105:3286:214098:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of recent empirical work reveals that, in practice, the contemporaneous risk-return
105:3287:214181:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:correlation is often found to benegative; see, e.g., Bollerslev et al. (2006), Lettau and
105:3288:214270:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Ludvigson (2010) and Brandt and Wang (2010).  Hence,  rather ironically,  we now
105:3289:214350:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:realize  that  we  know  less  than  we  thought  about  the  most-researched  connection,
105:3290:214440:18:18:91:136:254:12:g_d0_f5:12:g_d0_f3:B:μr↔σr.
105:3291:214446:18:18:109:520:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Second, consider the relationship between the equity premium and the business
105:3292:214523:18:18:91:520:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:cycle,μr↔μf.  Fama and French (1989) and Fama (1990) emphasize expected busi-
105:3293:214600:18:17:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ness conditions as a likely key driver of expected excess returns, with expected excess
105:3294:214687:17:12:101:398:183:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:88Indeed that is why we typically fixμrat zero in previous sections.
105:3295:214755:12:16:101:520:171:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:89The  conditional  standard  deviation  is  sometimes  replaced  by  the  conditional  variance,μt=
105:3296:214855:16:0:91:511:155:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f15:F:x′tβ+δσ2t, or other monotone transformations ofσt, in the estimation of the GARCH-M model.
106:3297:214948:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:returns negative near business cycle peaks and positive near troughs.  However, they,
106:3298:215033:18:18:91:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and the huge ensuing literature, use mostlyproxiesfor expected business conditions,
106:3299:215116:18:18:91:519:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:typically the dividend yield, the term premium, and the default premium; see, e.g.,
106:3300:215199:18:18:91:431:631:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:Campbell and Thompson (2008) and the literature cited therein.90
106:3301:215263:18:18:109:520:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Lettau and Ludvigson (2001) began a movement toward explicit incorporation of
106:3302:215340:18:18:91:519:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expected business condition variables with their celebrated generalized consumption-
106:3303:215424:18:18:91:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wealth ratiocay, or more precisely, the cointegrating residual between log consump-
106:3304:215507:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tion  and  log  wealth.   Campbell  and  Diebold  (2009),  and  subsequently  Goetzman
106:3305:215593:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:et al. (2009), extended the movement with direct inclusion of expected real growth,
106:3306:215676:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:or more precisely, Livingston survey expectations of real growth.91The results sug-
106:3307:215759:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:gest that expected growth is indeed a central determinant of expected excess returns,
106:3308:215844:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the Livingston expectations generally the most stable and significant predictor
106:3309:215928:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:across numerous competing specifications, including ones involving the “standard”
106:3310:216009:18:17:91:236:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:financial predictor variables.
106:3311:216039:17:18:109:520:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Having discussed a number of links involving fundamental volatility, we are now
106:3312:216118:18:18:91:519:416:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in a position to consider the final link,  which also involves fundamental volatility,
106:3313:216204:18:18:91:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:namelyμr↔σf.   Modern  asset-pricing  theory  emphasizes  not  only  fundamental
106:3314:216284:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:expectations,  but  also  fundamental  volatilities  in  the  determination  of  the  equity
106:3315:216376:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:premium.  An obvious example is the “long-run risk” model by Bansal and Yaron
106:3316:216453:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2004), and its extension explicitly incorporating time-varying economic uncertainty
106:3317:216537:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:in  Bollerslev  et  al.  (2009b).   In  this  new  class  of  models,  which  features  Epstein
106:3318:216632:18:18:91:520:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:B:and Zin (1989) preferences, variation in both consumption’s conditional meanand
106:3319:216711:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:conditional variance contribute importantly to variation in the equity premium.  Sup-
106:3320:216796:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:porting empirical evidence is provided in Bansal et al. (2005) and Bollerslev et al.
106:3321:216880:18:18:91:209:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:(2011a), among others.
106:3322:216902:18:12:101:424:236:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:90Note that, ironically, the standard proxies are financial rather than real.
106:3323:216979:12:0:101:366:224:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:91For details on the Livingston survey, see Croushore (1997).
107:3324:217043:0:26:91:302:685:14:g_d0_f2:14:g_d0_f2:C:4.5  Factors as Fundamentals
107:3325:217071:26:18:91:519:659:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:In our discussion of the the links between market risk and macro fundamentals we
107:3326:217151:18:18:91:519:641:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have sometimes been casual in distinguishing returns from excess returns, realized
107:3327:217233:18:18:91:519:623:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:from expected returns, realized from expected volatility, and related, in our treatment
107:3328:217320:18:18:91:519:605:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of timing.  This is to some extent unavoidable, reflecting different conventions both
107:3329:217405:18:18:91:519:587:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:within and among different and evolving literatures, as well as our desire to convey
107:3330:217489:18:18:91:519:569:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:wide-ranging  ideas  in  this  broad  survey.   Nevertheless,  a  clearly-emergent  theme
107:3331:217578:18:18:91:520:551:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is that financial markets, as summarized byμrandσr, are very much linked to the
107:3332:217657:18:18:91:520:533:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:business cycle, as summarized byμfandσf.  Indeed it is not an exaggeration to claim
107:3333:217740:18:17:91:520:515:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f4:B:that business cycle risk may be the key driver of expected excess equity returnsand
107:3334:217823:17:18:91:353:498:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:return volatilities.  Here we expand on that insight.
107:3335:217876:18:18:109:520:480:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Although the business cycle may be a key risk factor, a long tradition, dating at
107:3336:217957:18:18:91:519:462:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:least to Burns and Mitchell (1946) and actively extending to the present, recognizes
107:3337:218041:18:18:91:519:444:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that no single observed variable is “the business cycle” or “real activity.” Instead, we
107:3338:218129:18:18:91:519:426:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:observe literally dozens of indicators (employment, industrial production, GDP, per-
107:3339:218213:18:18:91:519:408:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:sonal income, etc.), all of which contain information about the business cycle, which
107:3340:218298:18:18:91:519:390:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:is not directly observable.  Hence the key business cycle real activity fundamental
107:3341:218381:18:18:91:519:372:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:underlying risk may be appropriately and productively viewed as a common factor
107:3342:218460:18:18:91:406:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:to be extracted from many individual real activity indicators.
107:3343:218522:18:18:109:520:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Expanding on this “factors as fundamentals” perspective, another likely-relevant
107:3344:218602:18:18:91:519:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:additional factor candidate is price/wage pressure, which may of course interact with
107:3345:218687:18:18:91:519:300:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real activity, as emphasized in Aruoba and Diebold (2010).  In any event, the point is
107:3346:218773:18:18:91:519:282:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:simply that, although we see hundreds of macroeconomic fundamentals, a drastically
107:3347:218855:18:17:91:519:264:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:smaller set of underlying macroeconomic factors is likely relevant for tracking market
107:3348:218941:17:18:91:519:247:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:risk.  This is useful not only for best-practice firm-level risk management, but also
107:3349:219026:18:18:91:519:229:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:for regulators.  In particular, the factors-as-fundamentals perspective has important
107:3350:219111:18:18:91:519:211:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:implications for the design of stress tests that simulate financial market responses to
107:3351:219198:18:18:91:519:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:fundamental shocks, suggesting that only a few key fundamentals (factors) need be
107:3352:219279:18:18:91:134:175:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:stressed.
107:3353:219288:18:0:109:520:157:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Not surprisingly,  then,  we advocate that risk managers pay closer attention to
108:3354:219371:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:macroeconomic factors, as they are the ultimate drivers of market risk.  We hasten to
108:3355:219456:18:18:91:519:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:add, however, that due to the frequent “disconnect” problems mentioned earlier, we
108:3356:219538:18:18:91:520:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:would never advocate conditioning risk assessmentsonlyon macroeconomic factors.
108:3357:219617:18:18:91:519:631:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Rather,  macroeconomic factors complement,  rather than substitute,  for the meth-
108:3358:219699:18:18:91:519:613:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:ods discussed in earlier sections, by broadening the conditioning information set to
108:3359:219783:18:18:91:343:595:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:include fundamentals in addition to past returns.
108:3360:219832:18:18:109:520:577:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:One might reasonably question the usefulness of conditioning on macroeconomic
108:3361:219909:18:18:91:519:559:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:data for daily risk assessment, because macroeconomic data are typically available
108:3362:219991:18:18:91:519:541:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:only quarterly (e.g., GDP and its components), or sometimes monthly (e.g., indus-
108:3363:220072:18:18:91:519:523:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:trial production and the CPI). Recent developments that exploit state space methods
108:3364:220155:18:18:91:519:505:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and optimal filtering, however, facilitate high-frequency (e.g., daily) monitoring of la-
108:3365:220244:18:18:91:519:487:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:tent macroeconomic fundamental factors.  In particular, based on the high-frequency
108:3366:220327:18:18:91:519:469:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:real activity monitoring approach of Aruoba et al. (2009), the Federal Reserve Bank
108:3367:220410:18:17:91:519:451:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of Philadelphia produces the “ADS index” of real activity, updated and written to
108:3368:220491:17:18:91:519:434:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the  web  in  real  time  as  new  indicator  data,  released  at  different  frequencies,  are
108:3369:220586:18:18:91:197:416:12:g_d0_f3:8:g_d0_f7:B:released or revised.92
108:3370:220608:18:18:109:520:398:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:We have emphasized macroeconomic fundamentals for equity market risk, but the
108:3371:220685:18:18:91:519:380:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:bond market is also closely linked to macroeconomic fundamentals.  In particular,
108:3372:220766:18:18:91:519:362:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:government bond yield curves are driven by just a few factors (level, slope, curvature),
108:3373:220854:18:18:91:519:344:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:with the level factor closely linked to price/wage activity and the slope factor closely
108:3374:220942:18:18:91:519:326:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:linked to real activity.93The same is true for yield curves of defaultable bonds, except
108:3375:221030:18:18:91:519:308:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:that there is the additional complication of default risk, but that too is linked to the
108:3376:221118:18:18:91:519:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:business cycle.  Hence despite data on dozens of government bond yields, and dozens
108:3377:221201:18:18:91:519:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:of macroeconomic indicators, the interesting reality is their much lower-dimensional
108:3378:221285:18:18:91:519:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:“state vectors” – the level and slope factors beneath the yield curve,  and the real
108:3379:221369:18:18:91:519:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and price/wage activity factors beneath the macroeconomy.  One can easily imagine
108:3380:221450:18:18:91:519:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:the usefulness for daily market and credit risk management (say) of systems linking
108:3381:221533:18:18:91:519:200:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:yield curve factors (level, slope, curvature, ...), equity factors (market, HML, SMB,
108:3382:221618:18:16:101:519:182:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f24:F:92The index and a variety of related materials are available athttp://www.philadelphiafed.
108:3383:221708:16:8:91:432:166:10:g_d0_f24:10:g_d0_f15:F:org/research-and-data/real-time-center/business-conditions-index.
108:3384:221773:8:0:101:402:158:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:?:93For background and references, see Diebold and Rudebusch (2012).
109:3385:221842:0:18:91:519:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:momentum, liquidity, ...), and macroeconomic factors (real, price/wage, ...).  All of
109:3386:221927:18:46:91:385:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:those factors are now readily available at daily frequency.
109:3387:221986:46:29:91:297:621:17:g_d0_f2:17:g_d0_f2:C:5  Concluding Remarks
109:3388:222007:29:18:91:519:592:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:We  have  attempted  to  demonstrate  the  power  and  potential  of  dynamic  financial
109:3389:222095:18:18:91:519:574:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:econometric methods for practical financial risk measurement and management.  We
109:3390:222175:18:18:91:519:556:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:have surveyed the large literature on high-frequency volatility modeling, interpreting
109:3391:222261:18:18:91:520:538:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:and unifying the most important and intriguing results of practical relevance.94Our
109:3392:222344:18:18:91:519:520:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:discussion has many implications for practical financial risk management; some point
109:3393:222428:18:18:91:519:502:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:toward desirable extensions of existing approaches, and some suggest new directions.
109:3394:222512:18:31:91:190:484:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B:Key points include:
109:3395:222531:31:18:106:520:453:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:1.  Standard  “model-free”  methods,  such  as  historical  simulation,  rely  on  false
109:3396:222619:18:18:121:520:435:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:assumptions  of  independent  returns.   Reliable  risk  measurement  requires  a
109:3397:222700:18:28:121:451:417:12:g_d0_f4:12:g_d0_f3:A:conditionaldensity model that allows for time-varying volatility.
109:3398:222765:28:18:106:520:389:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:2.  Successful  risk  measurement  may  be  achieved  through  the  use  of  univariate
109:3399:222852:18:17:121:520:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:density models directly for portfolio returns.  GARCH volatility models offer a
109:3400:222931:17:18:121:520:354:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:convenient and parsimonious framework for modeling key dynamic features of
109:3401:223005:18:18:121:520:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:such portfolio returns, including volatility mean-reversion, long-memory, and
109:3402:223082:18:28:121:188:318:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:asymmetries.
109:3403:223094:28:18:106:520:290:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:3.  Successful risk management, in contrast, requires a fully-specified multivariate
109:3404:223178:18:18:121:520:272:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:density model.  In that regard,  standard multivariate models are too heavily
109:3405:223255:18:18:121:520:254:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:parameterized to be useful in realistic medium- and large-scale financial market
109:3406:223335:18:18:121:520:236:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:contexts.  In medium-scale financial contexts, recently-developed multivariate
109:3407:223413:18:18:121:520:218:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:GARCH models are likely to be useful.  In very large-scale financial contexts,
109:3408:223491:18:15:101:519:200:7:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f15:F:94We hasten to add that this chapter is a complement, not a substitute, for the more general and
109:3409:223587:15:12:91:519:185:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:technical survey of volatility and covariance forecasting of Andersen et al. (2006a).  In addition,
109:3410:223686:12:12:91:519:173:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:space  constraints  and  other  considerations  have  invariably  limited  our  choice  of  included  topics.
109:3411:223795:12:12:91:519:161:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:For instance, we have largely neglected stochastic volatility and other parameter-driven approaches
109:3412:223894:12:0:91:343:149:10:g_d0_f15:10:g_d0_f15:F:to volatility modeling, as well as option-implied volatility.
110:3413:223958:0:18:121:520:685:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:more structure must be imposed, such as decoupling variance and correlation
110:3414:224033:18:18:121:520:667:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:dynamics.  In all cases, resampling methods applied to standardized returns is
110:3415:224111:18:28:121:510:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:an attractive strategy for accommodating conditionally non-normal returns.
110:3416:224185:28:18:106:520:621:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:4.  Volatility measures based on high-frequency return data hold great promise for
110:3417:224267:18:18:121:520:603:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:practical risk management, as realized volatility and correlation measures pro-
110:3418:224346:18:18:121:520:585:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:duce more accurate risk assessments and forecasts than their conventional com-
110:3419:224424:18:18:121:520:567:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:petitors.  Because high-frequency information is only available for highly liquid
110:3420:224505:18:18:121:520:549:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:assets, a base-asset factor approach may sometimes be useful.  In addition, the
110:3421:224584:18:18:121:520:531:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:near  log-normality  of  realized  volatility,  together  with  the  near-normality  of
110:3422:224671:18:18:121:520:513:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:returns standardized by realized volatility, holds promise for relatively simple-
110:3423:224752:18:28:121:520:495:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:to-implement log-normal/normal mixture models in financial risk management.
110:3424:224827:28:18:106:520:467:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:5.  The business cycle emerges as a key macroeconomic fundamental driving risk in
110:3425:224908:18:17:121:520:449:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:a variety of markets, including equities and bond yields.  Among other things,
110:3426:224986:17:18:121:520:432:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:this  means  that  our  emphasis  on  conditioning  applies  not  only  at  the  short
110:3427:225072:18:18:121:520:414:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:horizons (typically daily) stressed in sections 2 and 3, but also at much longer
110:3428:225152:18:18:121:520:396:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:horizons, once the information set is appropriately broadened to include macro
110:3429:225230:18:0:121:356:378:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:fundamentals as opposed to just past returns.
